If the ridge-beam collapses, if the wise man withers,
Where shall I find refuge?”
The Master, it seems, was gravely ill—
After seven days of sickness, he passed away.

*(The above* Dragging Staff Song *was not composed for sightseeing, yet in it we see how our Master likened himself to Mount Tai—thus it is included here.)*

**Han Dynasty**
**Zhang Heng – One of the "Four Sorrows" Poems**

What I long for lies on Mount Tai,
Yet Liangfu’s path is steep and harsh.
Turning east, I gaze—tears stain my brush.
A beauty gifts me a golden inlaid blade.
How to repay her? With finest jade.
The road is distant, I cannot send it—
Leaning in idle ease, why does sorrow weigh on my heart?

**Wei Dynasty**
**Cao Zhi – "Soaring Dragon" Ode**

At dawn I roamed Mount Tai, where buds swathed in mist stood veiled and fair.
Suddenly I met two youths—fresh were their faces, bright their hues—
Riding white deer, their hands shading stalks of sacred lingzhi.
I knew them as Perfected Ones; kneeling long, I sought the Dao.
Westward they led me to the Jade Hall, where golden towers linked by sky-bridges stood.
They bestowed upon me elixirs, wrought by the Divine Sovereign,
And taught me how to consume them, to refine essence and replenish the brain.
Thus would my years match gold and stone, forever ageless through the ages.

**Driving the Chariot**
Driving my chariot, urging on my swift steeds,
Eastward I came to the city of Fenggao.
Wondrous is that Mount Tai, whose name alone commands the Five Peaks.
Lofty and towering, it pierces the clouds, its craggy heights soaring into the Great Purity.
I circled its twelve watchtowers, inquiring at each pavilion along the way.
Above gushes the Sweet Wine Spring, where jade and stone gleam with radiant bloom.
To the northeast I gazed upon the vast wilds; to the west, I beheld the sun’s essence.
Here the soul and spirit are bound, and the departed feel its omen.
Kings ascend to heaven here, their primal merit fulfilled,
A rite observed by every dynasty, its protocol set in the *Book of Rites*.
Yet the span of years may be long or short—only virtue ensures blessings and integrity.
Seventy emperors have performed the Feng sacrifice, yet the Mystic Lord’s spirit stands supreme.
Feasting on auroral mist, rinsing with celestial dew,
Feathers cloak my form.
I rise, treading the void’s expanse, ascending through courts and gates to the distant dark.
May I share the years of Father East, achieving boundless, eternal life.

**The Immortals**
The Immortals grasp the six throws, casting lots at Mount Tai’s corner.
Xiang’e plucks the zither, Qin’s maidens play the sheng and yu.
Jade cups brim with osmanthus wine; the River Lord offers divine fish.
How confined the Four Seas seem! Where in the Nine Provinces can one go?
Han Zhong and Wang Qiao beckon me to the celestial crossroads.
A thousand miles are but a single step; lightly I rise, soaring through the Great Void.
I mount the radiant clouds, borne aloft by lofty winds,
And turn my chariot to gaze upon the Purple Tenuity.
There I join the Emperor, our spirits in accord.
I hear the towering gates stand majestic, their twin watchtowers soaring ten thousand yards.
Jade trees line the path, while White Tigers guard the gate’s pivot.
Riding the wind, I roam the Four Seas, eastward passing the Queen Mother’s abode.
Looking down upon the Five Peaks, I see how human life is but a fleeting sojourn.
I nurture my inner light, cultivate my wings,
Advancing slowly, step by step.
I do not see the Yellow Emperor, who rode a dragon from Mount Geng.
I wander the Nine Heavens, awaiting you for eternity.

**Jin Dynasty**
**Lu Ji – "Chant of Mount Tai"**
How high soars Mount Tai!
Far and distant, it reaches the celestial court.
Its towering heights stretch boundless, layered clouds shrouding its depths.
Liangfu has its lodge, Haoli its pavilion.
In its secluded peaks dwell myriad ghosts; divine powers gather from all spirits.
Long I chant by Mount Tai’s side, my voice ringing with fervent, sorrowful tones.

**Wife of Wang Ningzhi, née Xie – "Chant of Mount Tai"**
The lofty spirit of the Eastern Peak soars,
Its beauty piercing the azure heavens.
Within its cliffs lies a hollow chamber, silent and profound, shrouded in mystery.
No craftsman, no artisan—its cloud-wrought form arises naturally.
What manner of vessel or image is this, that compels me to wander ceaselessly?
I shall dwell in this rocky abode, where I may live out my allotted years.

**Song Dynasty**
**Xie Lingyun – "Chant of Mount Tai"**
Mount Tai, foremost among the sacred peaks, stands jagged against the sky.
Its cliffs jut sharply, their edges tangled in trailing clouds.
Ascending to perform the Feng rite upon its lofty altar,
Descending to enact the Shan sacrifice in solemn reverence.
Yet what obscurity veils its stony depths? What secrets lie in the Hall of Light’s arcane texts?

**Tang Dynasty**
**Li Bai – "Chant of Mount Tai"**
In the fourth month I climbed Mount Tai, where the stone path lay smooth for the imperial carriage.
Six dragons crossed ten thousand ravines, the valleys winding in their wake.
Hoofprints, once distant on emerald peaks, now overgrown with moss.
Flying cascades spray sheer cliffs, the rushing waters mingling with the pines’ mournful sighs.
Northward I gazed upon startling crags, their precipices tilting eastward.
The cavern’s gate, sealed by stone doors, rumbles with subterranean thunder.
Ascending high, I beheld Penglai and Yingzhou, imagining their golden and silver terraces.
At Heaven’s Gate I let forth a long whistle—ten thousand miles of pure wind answered.
Four or five jade maidens descended from the Nine Heavens,
Smiling as they extended their fair hands, offering me a cup of flowing rosy clouds.
I bowed my head in reverence, ashamed of my unworthy talents.
How vast the world seems, yet how fleeting life—why cling to it?
At dawn I rode a white deer, ascending straight to Heaven’s Gate Mountain.
There I met a feathered being, his square pupils and fine features radiant.
I grasped the vines, eager to speak, but he retreated behind the gates of azure clouds.
He left me a book of crow-tracks, drifting down to the rocky crags.
Its script was ancient, its meaning beyond my grasp.
I sighed thrice, resolved to follow a master—yet still I have not returned.

At first light I climbed Sunrise View, lifting my gaze to part the clouds.
My spirit soared in all directions, as if freed from heaven and earth.
The Yellow River flowed from the west, winding into distant mountains.
Leaning against the cliff, I gazed to the eight horizons, my eyes lost in the boundless sky.
Suddenly I met a green-haired youth, his twin topknots like clouds.
I lamented my late pursuit of immortality, my crimson face now withered.
Hesitating, I looked again—he was gone, vanished into the vast expanse, impossible to pursue.

For three thousand days I purified myself, tearing silk to transcribe the sacred scriptures.
Through chanting and recitation, I gained insight, and the gods guarded my form.
Riding the long winds, swift as if wings had sprouted,
I scaled the cliffs to Sunrise View, peering over the eastern darkness.
The sea’s hues stirred distant mountains; the celestial rooster had already crowed.
Silver terraces emerged from inverted reflections; white waves churned like leviathans.
How can I obtain the elixir of immortality, to soar high toward Penglai and Yingzhou?

At Sunrise View, the northeast slope tilts, two cliffs embracing twin stones.
The sea’s waters lie before my eyes; the sky’s light shimmers in empty azure.
A thousand peaks vie to pierce the heavens; ten thousand ravines stand sheer and precipitous.
Far off, the crane-riding immortals leave no trace in the clouds.
Towering pines reach into the Milky Way, their distant forms no larger than a foot.
Mountain flowers bloom in strange realms; in the fifth month, snow remains white.
One day I shall meet Anqi Sheng, here to refine the jade nectar.

At dawn I drank from the Queen Mother’s Pool; at dusk I lodged at Heaven’s Gate.
Alone I cradled my green jade zither, wandering by moonlight through the green mountains.
The mountains gleamed, the moon’s dew silvered the night; the wind in the pines stilled.
Immortals roamed the emerald peaks, their flutes and songs echoing everywhere.
I listened in quiet joy to the pure radiance, as Wang Zhen merged with the verdant ridges.
I imagined phoenixes dancing, their robes fluttering like dragon scales.
I reached to pluck gourds from the heavens, lost in reverie, forgetting to return.
I raised my hand to play in the clear shallows, mistakenly grasping the Weaving Maid’s loom.
At dawn I sat, only to find them gone—nothing remained but five-colored clouds.

**Seeing Master Fan of the Mountains Off on His Return to Mount Tai**

A man of Lu cradles a white crane,
bidding me farewell as he departs for Mount Tai.
At first, his journey seems but a wisp of cloud,
vanishing amid the blue cliffs.
Lofty, he ascends to Heaven’s Gate;
the Sun Terrace lies near, almost within grasp.
The cloud-wreathed peaks stretch beyond sight—
when will he return from this journey?

---

**Du Fu – Gazing at Mount Tai**

O Peak of Peaks, what can one say?
Qi and Lu’s verdure knows no end.
Creation gathers here its divine splendor;
yin and yang cleave dawn from dusk.
My breast swells with layered clouds;
I watch the crows return at dusk.
One day I shall scale the summit’s height—
and all mountains shrink to naught.

---

**Liu Yuxi – Seeing Daoist Refiner Zhang of the Eastern Peak Off**

Daoist Refiner Zhang of the Eastern Peak,
his lofty spirit and refined grace rare in this world.
Fit to inscribe the deeds of chaste women in green bamboo,
long has he served the Primordial Sovereign in the Purple Tenuity.
From the golden-threaded loom he casts brocade words;
on the Jade Clarity Altar he dons robes of rainbow hues.
No need for flute-playing companions on the cloudways—
he means to ride a simurgh home alone.

---

**Li Yifu – Passing Mount Tai on the Way to Offer Sacrifice at Junzhou**

Heaven’s Pillar marks this mighty bastion;
the Sun Terrace opens its sacred shrine.
Joyous, we recall Yao’s visit to Bohai’s shores;
hidden reefs guard the rivers Yi and Si.
To establish the Peak was truly a lasting deed;
to ascend in merit surely lies herein.
The Emperor’s way accords with vast destiny;
profound words unfold his literary thought.
His fame resounds through all the earth’s veins;
his transforming power sustains the cosmic frame.
Auspicious omens summon the treasured phoenix;
propitious charts present the sacred tortoise.
The Eastern Monarch now makes his fourfold visitation;
the Western Capital marshals its sixfold host.
The Celestial Chariot shifts the Starry Park;
the drought-dispelling carriage commands the Wind Bureau.
Drums thunder across the level plains;
imperial progress stills the thoroughfares.
At Wenyang, moon-feathered banners fly;
at Mengyin, lightning-guarded chariots gleam.
Rock flowers drift past the dawn imperial carriage;
peak leaves flutter the springtime standards.
Amid the jade-studded stones, patterned guards encircle;
the golden altar glows beneath the sturgeon-hung curtains.
The Three Beginnings bestow distant blessings;
the myriad years receive renewed grace.
Not by substance alone is favor bestowed—
I hasten to the steps of the vermilion court.
Entangled in the net, I sink to dark exile;
bound by limits, I miss the radiant age.
Long ago, the *Zhou Nan* lamented this—
how much more do I grieve now in the west!

---

**Xiao Chu – Offering a Poem in Harmony with the Sacrificial Rites at Mount Tai**

Across the Han, starry banners turn;
through the clouds, sun-feathered flags gleam.
To follow the traces of the sacred mound’s rites,
inscribe anew the Mount Tai inscription.
Forest spears choke the Ji’s banks;
beast drums shake the river’s court.
Leaf-arrows pierce the cold with grace;
the crow startles at dawn’s gaze.
Already descended to compose the Fen’s waters,
still deeper the welcome for the Wei’s sentiments.

---

**Xue Ke’gou – Offering a Poem in Harmony with the Sacrificial Rites at Mount Tai**

The Dragon Chart crowns the Six Directions;
the Phoenix Chariot points to Cloud Pavilion.
Auspicious mists drift over Ji’s shores;
green characters emerge on the river’s isles.
Morning robes answer the moon’s call;
patterned halberds part the dawn stars.
Four fields observe the bowing rites;
the Three Hunts align with scriptural truth.
Joyful to serve the ten thousand years,
I secretly grasp at a thousand ages.

---

**Lu Zhaolin – Song of the Great Sacrifice at Mount Tai**

At Sunrise Terrace, immortal clouds follow the phoenix carriage;
at Heaven’s Gate, azure snow illumines the dragon robes.
All night, lush strings and brocade mats resound;
exquisite dances and pure songs—joy knows no end.

---

**Lü Dongbin – Inscribed at the Queen Mother’s Pool**

Once I wandered here before—
now ninety springs have passed.
How many travelers tread the red dust?
Who among them knows me?

**Inscribed Again at the Queen Mother’s Pool**

Years ago, I left words to mark my visit;
my deeds now fill the world, spanning the nine realms.
Those meddlesome boys know my name—
so I leave these traces behind, lest they fade away.

---

These poems are engraved on steles within the Huizhen Palace of this prefecture. The stele is square, its characters in ancient seal script, elegant and worthy of contemplation. The latter inscriptions are said to be in Lü Dongbin’s own hand—upon reflection, they seem genuine.

**Fan Zhichong’s "Lü Gong’s Grotto"**

At dawn I roam the Northern Sea, by dusk—Yingzhou;
when did the immortal’s jade pendants journey here?
If only I could follow and ask the elixir’s secret,
we’d share spring wine, drunk together at Yueyang Tower.

**Bamboo Grove Temple**

Deep in the bamboo grove stands a monastery,
its meditation gate sealed—few travelers pass.
Beneath the eaves, plum blossoms bloom as spring wanes;
cold chimes and chants mingle where white clouds hang low.

**Sun-Viewing Peak**

The first sight east of Mount Tai’s southern ridge,
where azure skies soar high o’er emerald peaks.
Were one to stand atop this summit’s flight,
the sun’s bath in the sea would still gleam wet.

**Zha Dao’s Ascent of Mount Tai**

Soaring past layered crags, beyond mortal dust,
the Azure Lord sits high, his crimson banners unfurled.
Does he lift the sea and sky to bring the sun near?
Or summon Peng Isle’s rosy clouds to draw them close?

Stone gates flicker where sunlight spills,
the Fengshan Altar glows with Wang Jian’s radiance.
Since the Xiangfu era’s rites concluded,
the Peaceful Summit stands most towering still.

*(Zha Dao served the Song as Academician of the Dragon Diagram; his filial piety is recorded in* Filial Piety’s True Accounts*.)*

**Mei Shengyu’s "Ascending Mount Tai’s Sun-Viewing Peak"**

At dawn I climb Sun-Viewing Peak—
the sea melts into molten gold.
The sun emerges, chariot-wheel bright,
trailing heaven’s path, leaving no trace.

It pierces my eyes like a sword’s point,
its light gathering sharp as a drill.
It kindles the flourishing of all things,
grinds away the ominous and fell.

Grass and trees, though soulless,
must hear the stone gate’s pines sigh.
Once I sheltered there from rain—
how could I earn the title of "Great Officer"?
If man meets no fateful chance,
he clutches his scrolls, chanting the Six Dragons’ names.

**Wang Qinruo’s Ascent of Mount Tai**

Gazing round—no clouds, the path lies clear;
yellow banners welcome the Six Dragons’ approach.
The rites for the Three Spirits shine through the ages,
ten thousand banners’ cheers shake the nine realms.

Dark birds seem to grasp the Kun board’s signs,
true pines hide beams fit for a palace’s frame.
Now I know this life is no common affair—
twelve times I’ve reached Heaven’s Gate.

**Yuan Dynasty – Wang Yi’s "Matching Yuan Yishan’s Poem, Presented to Mount Tai’s Tianni, and Layman Zhang"**

**The True Man**

A scholar of the eastern lands, his hair grown white in vain,
only with a blossomed staff did he first wander this mountain.
Hand brushing the red sun, he ascends the Three Observances,
sleeve sweeping the yellow dust, he surveys the Nine Provinces.

**Mount Tai**

The imperial chariot of Qi and Lu parts Heaven’s Gate,
left and right, the lesser constellations array in two ranks.
The grand court unfolds, all in harmonious accord—
east of the Yellow River, few roam these peaks.

**The Feng and Shan Altar at Maoling**

The sacred altar of the Xiangfu Emperor’s bright hall,
where Qin and Han once carved steles, now lies in overgrown grass.
Though the world has changed, the altar still stands—
rubbing its stones, old tears wet the slanting sun.

**The Han Chancellor**

Bark peeled, heart withered through the depths of years,
yet his descendant’s branch now utters the dragon’s cry.
A fierce wind stirs its lone and lofty melody,
still sounding the *Liangfu* hymn atop the peak.

**The Shrine of Shi Shoudao and Sun Mingfu**

Master and disciple claimed the fame of two mountains,
who dares say their Dao and righteousness were slight?
On stormy nights in the forest of the Sacred Peak’s court,
the clamor of their reading still rings clear.

**Du Renjie’s Inscription at the Lead Gate of Heaven**

Mount Tai’s Heavenly Gate had no halls of old—
until Master Zhang of Bu Mountain labored for years to build them,
truly a feat that split the sky’s fabric.
The Qi man Du Renjie thus inscribed it:

The primal *qi* split, the Two Modes took form,
the Five Peaks stood firm, their true shapes revealed.
Only the Great Peak, poised like a dustpan,
soars ever higher, a pillar of Heaven.
Through a thousand kalpas, it stands empty,
who carved it? Who conceived such a thought?
Not by axe or adze, but by prayer and curse.
One family opened it, reaching the very depths.
Eighteen bends, each a thousand steps,
where shepherd’s purse sprouts and trees clasp the earth.
The sun’s chariot turns back, its radiance dimmed,
the Six Dragons falter.
Vast and dark, the path winds onward—
countless worthies, from Wu Huai’s time below,
seventy rulers laid down their weapons.
Yet when the imperial reins were seized,
the sagely Dao faded.
Rites and teachings decayed, abdication ceased,
usurpations recurred, all suddenly closed.
Blocked were the roads, the stars loomed,
salvation and protection summoned the hundred spirits.
Through this gate, golden splendor gleams.
Crimson portals, nine tigers crouch—
ten thousand men tremble, yet I long to knock,
but who dares open it? When will it part?
As of old, it stands serene, the imperial seals flow.
Grievances are quelled, illusions dispelled,
dust and mist cleared, governance’s flaws scraped away,
the people’s pests excised, the high receive truth,
the low find peace in their toil.
The emperor’s brow glistens with blood, his wisdom awakens,
the cliff remains unweathered, the green wall stands firm.
I carve this inscription, hoping it endures,
handed down through ten thousand ages to rectify the royal measure.

**Yuan Haowen’s Ascent of the Peak**

Mount Tai stands between heaven and earth,
towering like a dense, misty terrace.
At its inception, the hand of creation
split it—how mighty the act!
The Heavenly Gate, how lofty,
its perilous heights like steps to the sky.
Layered moss and piled stones
clearly reveal the Nine Realms.
Even the *Zhuangzi*’s nine-thousand-mile ascent
cannot gainsay this truth.
The First Emperor amplified its numinous power,
Emperor Wu of Han too was a man of heroic talent.
Yet their jade banners never returned,
the stone altar now thick with green moss.
Past and present—one glance, one sigh—
the emotion overwhelms, leaving one enfeebled.
The marvels explored make the climb forgotten,
contentment lingers, delaying the descent.
That night, lodging at the Jade Maiden’s Shrine,
the crashing torrents surge like thunderclouds.
At dawn, ascending the Sun-Watching Terrace,
the four directions clear of haze.
The Six Dragons emerge from Fusang,
stirring the mounds of blue mist.
Though I’ve wandered Hua and Song in my life,
this mountain remains unforgotten.
For ten years I gazed toward Qi and Lu,
a lone cloud brushing the layered cliffs.
The green walls stand stark, clouds parting between—
before my eyes, words fail to capture it,
only the vastness within my breast.
From the summit of Zulai, I call to Li Bai—
from here, I would gaze toward Penglai.

**Duan Fu’s Inscription on Li Bai’s *Sunrise at Mount Tai***

The Great Peak, majestic, lord of all beneath heaven,
the banished immortal, peerless dragon among men.
Mountain and man thus conjoined,
their *qi* overawed even the gods, vexing Feng Long.
The Jade Court, left to the clouds’ embrace,
he soared with a long whistle past the Qin Emperor’s pines.
At night, he summoned the sun from the eastern sea,
once more parting the primordial chaos for this world.
The Celestial Lord of the Ninefold Depths,
drunken, danced and shattered the blue lotus.
The Heavenly Granddaughter and Jade Maiden composed themselves,
gazing back, the Five Peaks no larger than autumn hairs.
The great whale departed, never to return,
while the cosmos, ten thousand miles wide, resounds with autumn insects.
The traces of his breath and spittle linger on the peaks,
to this day, trees and stones exhale fragrant winds.
I long to follow him, but he is lost in the void—
unexpectedly, I encounter him here,
where the moon still hangs empty above the rafters.

**Zhang Yanghao’s Ascent of the Peak**

With a single bound of wind and cloud, I reach Heaven’s Gate,
a sight to gladden a lifetime.
For ages, the nine points of Qi have smoked,
at dawn, the sun rises three poles high over the eastern sea.
Only now do I know how cramped my well-dwelling was,
hereafter, even a nest feels spacious.
Laughing, I clap Hong Ya and chant new verses,
as phoenixes and cranes fill the frigid sky.

**Xu Shilong’s Record of a Dream**

I dreamed of Master Tianni,
together we ascended Sun-Watching Peak.
His bones were as sturdy as a crane’s,
his steps as steady as an old dragon’s.
Beyond the world’s bounds, no courts or offices,
yet within his hall stood the Great Peak.
I heard this was a true blessed land—
with staff and sandals, I would follow.

**Seeing Master Tianni Off to Mount Tai**

At ninety, his hair still dark,
the Daoist’s bearing steeped in mist and rosy clouds.
Three thousand miles of grotto-heavens and blessed lands,
his abode the foremost of divine courts and immortal realms.
The *niuqi* herbs are potent, the wine rich,
the rabbit-hair cups vie for fragrant buds.
He loves his reclusion like Tao Hongjing—
let him not boast of being the "Mountain Prime Minister."

**Yuan Haowen’s Farewell to Master Tianni Returning to Bu Mountain**

Li Bai’s poetic brush graces Bu Mountain’s heights,
yet in cloth saddle and green shoes, you’ve yet to wander there.
I’d thought to seek the lofty one’s elixir mirror,
but feared your bones might rival Danqiu’s.
Between the clouds, the thatched hut, the chickens and dogs still,
beyond the world, mist and rosy clouds in autumn’s wind and dew.
One day, when you climb Heaven’s Gate again,
pray linger at the Immortal-Shedding Cliff.

Tianni is Zhang Zhipu; Bu Mountain is Bujin Mountain, southwest of Mount Tai.
Du Renjie’s inscription for the Heavenly Gate also calls it Bu Mountain, perhaps where Master Zhang once dwelled in truth.

**Wang Dan’s Ode to the Han Wutong Trees**

No city walls encircle the Han tombs at Cangwu,
yet the ancestral halls’ surviving trees stand tall and rugged.
They do not grow from the foundations of the Bright Hall—
creation’s currents link them to the peak’s numen.

Amid ten thousand ravines, mist and haze seal the towering trunks;
Midair winds and rains shake autumn’s voice.
On the day of the eastern feng rites, white-haired, we shall meet again—
lush hues mirroring the phoenix banner, all in verdant green.

**Zhang Zhi’s Inscription at Peach Blossom Vale**
From the heavens flows the water of the cave;
a single pulse links the human realm.
Peach Blossom Spring cannot be far—
floating forth, fallen blossoms red.

**Delight in Rain on Mount Tai**
The sacred peak, fairest under heaven,
its timely rains soak the mortal world.
Beyond the heights, where now is he?
This eastern mountain resembles that one.

*All eleven poems are carved on the rocks of Dayu Creek.*

**Li Jian’s Ascent of the Sacred Peak**
Three peaks thrust skyward, level with the heavens;
before reaching Heaven’s Gate, toil and climb.
Layer upon layer, stone steps emerge from treetops,
a winding, hundred-fold ladder of azure clouds.
On a sculpted boulder I rest, gazing afar;
wind howls through ravines, roaring in ten thousand hollows.
Water’s voice plays atop the treetops—
I wonder if a celestial tiger roars beyond the sky.
At dawn I reach Sunrise Peak,
parting clouds and mist to open the primal vastness.
The fiery wheel nears, dyeing the eastern waves crimson;
golden radiance stirs the Azure Dragon’s palace.
The Yellow River, a single thread stretching thousands of li,
Wu and Yue’s mountains and rivers lie truly beneath the earth.
Counting the nine green dots of the Central Plain,
I lean over the railing to peer into the eastern gloom.
Li Bai failed to meet Master Anqi—
how might one grow wings to soar to Penglai’s isles?

**The Court of Homage**
Here the court of homage was built in years past,
banners and pennants clustering the immortal ranks.
Now only the green mountains remain;
at dusk, solitary clouds drift to and fro.

**Dengdu Vale**
A stone cave, desolate and cold, a lone tree’s shadow;
locals say this is Dengdu.
Ancient steles still speak of Han Qinhu—
I ask: does he remain today?

**Wang Xu’s Visit to Bamboo Grove Temple**
A stone path descends into cloud-filled ravines;
a bamboo grove opens a secluded realm.
The temple is ancient, its monks few;
the mountain deep, its mists crystalline.
Before my excursion ends, my interest unspent,
the red sun suddenly inverts its light.
I drag my staff through twilight’s haze,
singing as I descend the ridge ahead.

**West Creek**
I love West Creek’s beauty,
often parting clouds to come and go.
A prefecture’s misty scenes converge;
three sides unfold like painted screens.
The shallow world lacks recluses like Shang,
yet in this clear age, men of leisure abound.
Near the cliffs lie many vacant plots—
more pines and bamboos must be planted.

**Jia Lu’s Ascent of Mount Tai**
How towering and majestic is the Sacred Peak!
No mountain compares.
Long have I dwelt in the dusty clamor;
at the sight, joy overflows.
With no ladder to scale the summit,
I offer these words in humble admonition.
Why does but one hall remain,
while a thousand chambers lie exposed in ruin?
They say it fell to flames in war,
amid the chaos of the Jin’s collapse.
Moved by its desolation of past years,
grieved that it remains unrestored,
I submit a memorial to the vermilion court—
its reconstruction must be near.
Yet alas! Qi and Lu suffer famine,
their people reduced to chaff and husks.
O Spirit, if you would manifest your power,
let abundant sacrifices bring joy.
Soon the former palace shall be restored,
its gold and azure dazzling the eye.

**Gazetteer of Mount Tai, Volume Sixteen: Records of Ascents and Visits**
From the founding of the august Ming to the *jiayin* year of the Jiajing era, all poems by renowned officials and scholars are recorded here. The old gazetteer preserved their original titles; where known, these have now been slightly corrected.

**Song Lian, Academician of Jinhua, Ascends Mount Tai**
Rejoicing in Yao’s pillar of the azure vault,
ten thousand ravines and a thousand crags linked by a single path.
The celestial bodies descend to the Green Emperor’s temple;
divine radiance eternally encircles the Azure Clouds Palace.
At dawn, cloud curtains whiten the horizon;
at midnight, the clear sky sways the sun over the sea.
Jade dew and golden stems must be close—
raising my head to the celestial river, my thoughts turn bold.

**Fang Xiaoru, Academician of Zhejiang, Ascends Mount Tai in Summer**
Shaking my robes at a thousand fathoms, my thoughts drift far;
today’s ascent of the Sacred Peak fulfills a long-held desire.
The ancient feng rites of Qin and Han hang in the azure void;
the cosmos’ grandest structures dot the floating realm.
At Sunrise Peak, the sea’s sun rises at the third watch;
wind stirs Heaven’s Gate through all nine summers and autumns.
Climbing higher to the clouds’ edge, I gaze again—
the Purple Tenuity’s lightning flashes like the hook of heaven.

**Zeng Cai, Zhuangyuan of Jiangxi, Gazes at the Sacred Peak at Dawn from Pingzhou**
I long to ascend Mount Tai,
to stand on high and survey the eight poles.
Twelve years of wandering,
in vain have I let time slip by.
This morning, from horseback, I suddenly see it—
standing in the southeast, half in the azure sky.
I imagine when chaos first stirred,
the two qi coiled and intertwined,
the great clod playing with yellow earth,
unable to discern its origin.
The round spirit descended in awe;
the earth’s queen conceived peaks and ridges.
When heaven and earth split open,
all was seen to pierce the heavens, ten thousand fathoms high.
Then I knew the divine workings of creation,
placing this to anchor the earth’s axis.
The Giant Spirit rests upon its summit;
six turtles bear its base.
Even Yu Gong could not move it;
even Fang Ping could not shrink it.
Heaven’s craftsmanship, the ghosts’ axes—
carving out a thousand peaks, a hundred green.
Since ancient times, the Jade Pillar has stood,
unleveled by the southern wind.
Sun and moon emerge in radiant splendor;
stars and constellations gleam.
Cold cliffs accumulate ice and snow;
shady ravines race with wind and thunder.
Clouds and mist dazzle in shifting light;
plants and trees flourish with vital essence.
Above, golden and silver qi float;
below, demons and monsters lurk in hiding.
Majestic, it is Lu’s gaze,
the anchor of a hundred spirits’ court.
Kunlun is its father;
the Four Sacred Peaks its elder brothers.
Mount Lu and Mount Emei are its sons—
all others are but its echoes.
“Qi and Lu’s green is endless”—
how can such words suffice?
Above, the heavens for ten thousand li
borrow this mountain’s verdure.
Qin Shihuang and Han Wudi traversed it all,
sealing their jade tablets and golden caskets in grand feng rites.
Wind and rain, moss and lichen cover the steles of old;
mist and pines, the halls of their time.
Since ancient times, the Five Peaks have ranked with the Three Dukes—
how much more this great anchor, the mountain’s ancestor?
Its concentrated spirit and nurtured beauty are fathomless;
its vastness commands the earth’s might.
Our August Emperor, born with sagely virtue,
his power vast, his benevolence manifest, his transformation far-reaching.
With one campaign, he pacified the south;
with another, he cleansed the northern deserts.
His imperial carriage often passes Mount Tai,
where he offers sacrifices, building altars and presenting jade and silk.
As a humble servant, I am fortunate to attend this northern journey—
at one glimpse of this mountain, I love its hues.
Though I lack even a drop to aid river or mountain,
my breast swells with poetic fervor.
One day, bearing my brush, I shall sing of his divine merit,
inscribing it upon every stone of Mount Tai.

**Wang Guangyang, Prime Minister of Gaoyou, Returns to Mount Tai and Writes Impromptu**

The seventy-two divine provinces,
awash with floating purple qi.
The sky lowers, all mountains shrink—
one autumn peak gathers the stars’ embrace.

Mists coil into dragons and tigers,
mountain haze veils the Dipper and Ox.
The Supreme Peak and Mount Heng,
lead the gaze eastward.

**Li Shimian, Libationer, at the Towering Pavilion Sends Off Minister Chen Returning to Shandong**
The Supreme Peak’s grandeur defies comparison,
its emerald hues stretch autumn’s thousand li.
Sheer cliffs cling to the sky’s edge,
a lone pavilion stands firm at the mountain’s foot.

Before you, fragrant grasses obscure the path,
ancient steps frost over, moss spreads unchecked.
Delicate blossoms brush the rail, untouched by hands,
only a lone crow cries, heard by few.

Morning dew bathes the sun—ten peaks turn purple,
a single cup reveals the distant, twilit sea.
Climbing high, the dawn bell echoes within the view,
before the Peak’s shrine, white clouds rise.

Who does not follow the sagely Dao?
Heaven and earth open and close in ceaseless flow.
The Supreme Peak’s majesty eludes description—
who left this famed pavilion here alone?

When you return to the ministry’s leisure days,
visit its traces wherever you roam.
I imagine you leaning on the railing, gazing afar,
composing verses on antiquity—what boundless inspiration!

**Wang Ju Ascends the Peak**
The famed mountains of Qi and Lu revere the Supreme Peak,
steep and fair, a jade hibiscus of ten thousand fathoms.
Moonlit seas stretch wide, linking three isles,
clouds part to reveal peaks piercing the sky.

White stones bear the seals of renowned scholars,
why need the pines the title of "Great Officer"?
My ascent leaves longing unfulfilled—
I climb yet higher to the first crimson crag.

**Wu Jie, Libationer of Ancheng, Miscellaneous Poems on Mount Tai**

*Stone Tablet*
Golden statutes, jade seals buried deep,
phoenix carriages and rainbow banners scatter purple mist.
Where have the seventy-two rulers gone?
Only this lone monument crowns the peak.

*Li Si’s Seal Script Stele*
All books in the land were burned to ash,
only steadfast stone records merit and achievement.
Where now the Yellow Dog of the Eastern Gate?
Yet carved worms still practice seal script.

*Cliffside Stele*
Ten-zhang cliffs carved with azure green,
front inscribed with virtue, back with verse.
Even the Bridge Creek’s "Ode to Revival"
cannot match the Eastern Tour’s praise of Tang’s glory.

*Cloud-Water Pool*
At the summit, a square pool like an empty mirror,
floating clouds here trace the divine.
How many times has a hand’s-breadth of rain departed,
bestowing harvests upon the people?

*Great Officer Pine*
Once favored by the First Emperor’s grace,
rooted high, its branches pierce the clouds.
Pitiful the Second Emperor, now mere dust—
the cold pine outlives him, its descendants enduring.

*Imperial Tent Flat*
Several times celestial decrees descended from purple clarity,
the Song emperor once halted his dragon banner here.
Wildflowers, crying birds change with the years,
yet the tale of the imperial tent lingers still.

**Xu Youzhen, Earl of Wugong, Ascends Mount Tai**
Unwearied by crimson cliffs step by step,
the sacred scene before my eyes shifts with sun and shade.
The horse halts beside pines of ten thousand fathoms,
I walk where nine heavens seem within reach.

At dawn, white clouds rise from the mountainside,
at night, the red sun is born east of the sea.
Knowing my heart yearns for the palace, unbound by distance,
due north, the imperial capital stands clear.

**Nian Fu, Minister from Fengyang, Prays for Snow**
Revered among the Five Peaks, guardian of the east,
its sacred duty is to nurture and transform.
One incense burner’s sincere prayer seeks response—
may three white blessings bring eternal abundance.

**Li Yu, Surveillance Commissioner, Ascends Mount Tai**
Having traversed all mountains as dusk hastens,
I seem to return from the purple empyrean.
Han and Qin’s feng and shan rites stretch boundless,
Tang and Song’s steles half-covered in moss.

Purple qi once congealed above the imperial tent,
mountain haze through the night calls to the immortal terrace.
Is the peak’s spirit only for timely rains?
It also bestows rare talents upon the celestial court.

**Zhou Hao, Assistant Magistrate, Ascends Mount Tai**
Layered peaks soar, scraping the sky,
below, all mountains appear distinct.
On Taihua’s summit, green shoots endure,
on the Immortal’s Palm, a jade hibiscus blooms.

Scaling the summit, I know heaven is near,
through five nights, the sea’s edge reveals the red sun.
Radiant the Peak Lord, revered by all—
unceasing, offerings of livestock and silk come and go.

**Zhang Sheng, Minister, First Ascends Mount Tai**
Gazing up at the Supreme Peak, towering and majestic,
ten thousand ravines and cliffs teem with grandeur.
After rain, spring’s glow spreads emerald hues,
mist veils dawn’s light, revealing blue snail-shell peaks.

The Qin king’s feng stele still stands,
Han Wu’s prayers for spirits remain indelible.
Today, as I ascend and gaze,
heaven is so close I could touch it.

**Zhang Wen, Minister, on the Great Officer Pine**
Before the wind-and-rain cliff, six dragons pause,
the green pine earns the title "Great Officer."
Though Fusu’s plan could have saved Qin,
it was no match for half a day’s merit then.

**Xu Yuan, Magistrate, Ascends the Supreme Peak**
Ascending the summit of the Supreme Peak,
the winding Wen River embraces Mount Zulai.
I pass through Heaven’s Gate like an arrow’s flight,
my horse parts from the sedan at Xian Ridge.

The feng altar stands high, capped with white stone,
the cliffside script is ancient, eroded by moss.
Who now repeats the golden carriage and jade chariot?
Only the Qin king’s lone mound remains.

**Qiao Jin, Magistrate, Ascends Mount Tai**
The Eastern Peak looms—each step is hard,
a bamboo sedan carries me to the clouds’ edge.
Peaks align at Sunrise View, three thousand fathoms tall,
the path winds through Heaven’s Gate, eighteen bends.

High enough to brush the Dipper and Ox,
from here, Qi and Lu spread wide in view.
With fragrant petals, I pay respects at the Primordial Lady’s shrine,
praying the imperial realm endures for ten thousand myriad years.

**Sima Yao, Censor, Ascends Mount Tai**
This journey is extraordinary indeed—
ravine mists and forest haze part at a glance.
A ten-thousand-fathom emerald screen stands in the sky,
a single red sun rises before my eyes.

Ni Hill’s old mound gathers the mountain’s spirit,
Qin and Han’s grand steles are lost to ancient moss.
Yet I recall my lord and kin in the northwest,
where five-colored clouds run deep, I turn my head.

**Bi Yu, Vice Commissioner from Guixi**
*Mourning the Hall of Light*
The "Millet is Scattered" poem laments the Eastern Zhou,
few now visit this place of fading green.
No more envoys bearing silk for court visits,
only alliances of feudal lords remain.

Sages’ words and deeds illuminate the ages,
the rise and fall of kings and hegemons rest in one mound.
Do not seek old traces on the high terrace—
broken steles and scattered rubble stir endless sorrow.

*Sacrificial Cliff*
The Eastern Peak, spirit of life, abhors killing,
this cliff was never Qin’s pit of doom.

**The Foolish Son**
A foolish son alone obscures his fate,
daily bearing the shame of unfilial name.

**The Inscriptionless Stele**
It stands atop the peak like a tyrant lone,
what scheme did the First Emperor here intend?
The *wang-qi* of the southeast still abides—
who says the Qin fell not to the Hu?

**Censor Zhao Ying of Lanzhou, Following Sima’s Rhymes on Ascending Mount Tai**
At the summit’s height, my eyes grow dim,
my voice too loud—I fear the heavens hear.
Eastward, the vast sea fills my robe,
northward, the jade capital bears five-hued clouds.
Rites of Qin and Han fade into tales,
while Stone Grandson’s fame upholds this culture’s weight.
Our sovereign never sought *feng* and *shan*—
through ten thousand ages, men praise the Radiant Lord.

**Vice Commissioner Xia Yin of Huating, on Mount Tai**
The East’s Mount Tai, parent of all peaks,
all hearts beneath heaven turn to it as one.
After seventy-two lords sealed their rites,
millennia’s affairs dissolve in mist.
Wandering the northern sea, clouds stretch black,
parrots test the midnight sky—dawn glows red.
Where lie Weak Waters and Penglai’s isles?
The immortals first parted from the Grand Luminous Palace.

**Academician Bo Zhen Ascending Mount Tai**
Great wings trail clouds, nine myriad leagues,
today’s celestial roaming—I nearly forget to return.
Who in a thousand years has gazed upon the sea?
My old feet now reach Mount Tai at last.
Rain passes, spring cliffs—dragons sport,
pines of ancient times—cranes idle still.
My poem cannot exhaust this lone, lofty mood—
I stand on the central peak to survey the mortal world.

**The Immortal on Crane-Back**
Transcendent, riding a crane’s back,
at dawn I mount Mount Tai, soaring through purple haze.
The mountain presses the eastern sea, coiling the earth,
the path crosses the Northern Dipper, reaching blue heaven.
Who shares the sun and moon in my hands?
Beyond form, I first grasp the wind’s light.
A laugh at the world’s empty millennia—
in the Great Purity, I lean on boundless joy.

**Vice Minister Bi Ascending Mount Tai**
Below coils the sea, above soars the blue sky,
who in ancient times first scaled this peak?
Ten thousand ridges hang their heads in cloud and mist,
the nine provinces’ borders lie before my door.
The Dao’s height—Confucius saw it when he climbed,
Qin’s merit paled—his stele carved after the rites.
I envy only Li Taibai of old,
who sat by the Red Mouth, watching clouds and mist.

**Secretary Shao Zhuang Ascending Mount Tai**
A fair wind lifts me to the layered clouds,
four vistas stretch boundless, rich with scene.
Jade tablets preserve old tales,
ancient steles, wordless, mark past dynasties.
The sun rises east of the sea—seen at midnight’s height,
clouds rise mid-mountain—distant from the world below.
From here I know the earth is small—
I long to follow the Sage’s soaring thought.

**Minister Huang Jing’s Temple to the Lord of Mount Tai (Unfulfilled Ascent)**
How many noble lords, how many rites?
Even piercing clouds, I but glimpse the peak.
Absurd records fill histories,
yet rites shine bright, revered by our ancestors.
If heaven has a gate, men may reach it,
but immortals leave no trace—guests never meet.
The cosmos naturally returns to its true lord—
I imagine the mountain spirit laughing at the First Emperor.

**Warehouse Manager Wang Jing Ascending Mount Tai**
Since heaven and earth were split, this mountain stands,
how fortunate to climb it in this life!
Ascending, I feel the stars draw near,
here I grasp the cosmos’ vast expanse.
A solitary peak thrusts up, cradling sun and moon,
stretching ten thousand miles, forests and ridges rise.
I recall the five years of eastern tours—
three generations of lord and minister shared hardship.

**Vice Minister Zhang Xiu Ascending Mount Tai**
Parrots cry at sea’s dawn, striking the divine shrine,
a stone path winds upward to the azure void.
Before the Horse-Turning Ridge, jade trees stand old,
by the Water Curtain Cave, wildflowers bloom red.
Pines uphold the imperial tent beneath the melting moon,
doves flee the Heavenly Gate in the howling wind.
All day I climb vines to the summit—
this body seems suspended in five-colored clouds.

**Censor Pan Kai of Chengyang Ascending the Sacred Peak**
The Heavenly Gate stands far beyond,
benevolent gaze reduces all mountains to dust.
Sheer cliffs plunge from empty space,
hazy clouds swirl around my seat.
The path leads near the isles of immortals,
my heart parts from the world’s dust.
Yet lingering joy remains—
I sing heartily, riding home.

**Censor Liu Bing Ascending Mount Tai**
Why do I linger alone in midair?
I long to compose verse but lack Song Yu’s talent.
My return path seems to descend from heaven,
my eyes strain to open in the mist.
Carved cliffs bear words men can no longer read,
the imperial tent’s terrace stands empty, waters mourn.
I whistle through wind and frost, ever wandering—
may the mountain spirit permit my return?

**Minister Wang Shouren of Yuyao Ascending the Sacred Peak**
At dawn I climb Mount Tai’s path,
step by step into the misty haze.
Sunlight scatters through ravines,
autumn’s visage glows faintly bright.
Cloud ladders hang on green cliffs,
I look up—spider silk glimmers fine.
A long wind blows the sea’s hue,
rustling, it sends the heavens’ robe.
At the peak, reed pipes play,
two azure lads lean close.
I shake my robes, about to follow,
suddenly soaring high on clouds.
I wave my hand as if they wait,
cinnabar clouds flash their last glow.
This mortal frame lacks sturdy wings—
I gaze longingly, unable to return.

The Heavenly Gate looms sheer,
below, blue clouds drift.
Seething, far from the human world,
the high sky’s autumn stretches vast.
Dusk rises from the earth,
I lodge in a tower above the heavens.
At midnight, the celestial rooster crows,
the sun rises from the eastern sea.
Dimly, Penglai’s trees appear,
faintly, Fusang’s shores emerge.
My resounding song falls into the azure void,
its echoes enter the blue-green flow.
Tang and Yu gave way to Chu and Han,
vanished like dust in the wind.
How remote the Crane Mountain immortal—
could Qin’s emperor ever attain him?
Gold and cinnabar consume days and months,
yet wrinkled faces cannot be preserved.
My intent lies with Pengzu of old,
lightly I ride the freezing gale.
I pledge to meet Guangchengzi,
to roam the Great Void together.
Dry stalks lean toward ravines,
yellow millet is no match.
The vaulted cliffs know no end,
I stride upon the misty rainbow.
Perilous springs cascade down stone paths,
empty shadows hang from cloud-pines.
A thousand peaks jostle like clustered bamboo,
shading and revealing green lotuses.
High terraces lean on jagged cliffs,
tilting over perilous chasms.
A misstep follows the misty haze,
shattered bones lie in the cliff’s heart.
Fools never understand—
they rush to ruin in droves.
I sit at Sunrise Viewing Peak,
parting clouds to howl at the sky’s wind.
I ask the Red Water’s Lord Xuanyuan,
I call to the double-pupiled Chonghua.
Faintly, heaven’s words fall,
idly, the intricate opens.
Go, go—speak no more,
the turbid world knows no end.

The dusty net brings bitter entanglement,
wealth and rank are but dewdrops on grass.
Better to ride a white deer,
eastward to roam the Isles of Penglai.

At dawn I ascend Mount Tai to gaze afar,
mighty waves part the misty vastness.
The sun’s radiance emerges from sea-clouds,
ushering dawn at Heaven’s Gate.
From afar I glimpse the Azure Radiance Lord,
soaring and wheeling in graceful flight.
Jade maidens play purple phoenix flutes,
their twin melodies drifting into the clear sky.
I crane my neck but cannot reach,
bowing low as the wind roars past.
They cast me the Jade Void Scroll—
its words remain unfathomed still.
Beside me stands the Long-Browed Boatman,
pointing out the Way step by step.
From this moment I refine golden cinnabar,
sweeping my traces clean from the mortal world.

Mount Tai’s height—
Ou Sheng, that honest Chu man,
knew only the height of Mount Lu.
Yet Mount Lu’s height
can still be measured in spans.
But Mount Tai—
gazing upward, it blurs into the void,
I know not whether it still stands beneath the blue sky,
or if its hues rise *above* the blue sky.
I long to capture it in words,
but fear my humble vision,
unable to fathom its grandeur,
will fail to render it in ink.

The primal qi surges and swells,
its towering bulk half-veiling the eastern sky.
South lies Mount Heng, north the other Heng, west Mount Hua—
who dares claim supremacy in their midst?
The mortal realm flickers in and out of sight,
as thunderstorms part the primordial chaos.
Embroidered cliffs and cinnabar stairs,
mist and haze dissolve into clarity,
the sea’s sun rises in a burst,
bathing the verdant peaks in light.

The foothills embrace the distant bay,
Sunrise Peak faces Fusang’s dawn.
Listening to the cascading roar below,
I know the hundred rivers converge in the east.
The Stone Gates of Heaven
yawn open at their center.
Hidden crags and secluded valleys
lie buried in obscurity.
Yet within them flow worldly currents—
tortoises lurk, phoenixes nest,
feeding on mist and absorbing essence,
brimming with strange and transcendent talents.

Above, a hundred-zhang cataract
plummets through empty air, threading stone,
piercing clouds in its descent—
its source seems to flow from the blue heavens.
At the cliff’s edge, wisps of mist rise,
in an instant, torrents drench the nine realms.
Since ancient times, seventy-two emperors
have come to perform the Feng sacrifice,
later rulers following in droves,
their rites as numerous as rain.
Jade seals and golden caskets—
all have been made,
yet where are they now?
Only white clouds still rise from the sealed mounds,
broken steles bear no words,
the wind beyond the sky daily grinds them,
flying dust passes in a blink,
vanishing in an instant.

How could they leave a trace?
The emperor’s banners are long gone,
the setting sun bids farewell to a thousand peaks.
In Lu’s fields, the qilin was captured,
at Qiyang, the phoenix gathered.
The Hall of Light lies in ruins—
who now sings its praises?
Confucius, staff in hand,
strolled away and never returned.
The hidden springs sob with sorrow,
the peaks bow in farewell.
Looking up and down at the cosmos,
across a thousand years we gaze.
Even lesser mountains and hills
are bathed in its light.
Its towering majesty matches heaven—
none dare defy its might.

Alas, I stand outside its gates,
how could I glimpse its inner halls?
Yet I come to cling to its traces,
to tread its lingering paths.
Among the three thousand,
I know not if I may bow once more at the end of the line.

Ah! Mount Tai’s height—
its summit knows no end.
Suddenly turning my head,
I find myself beside the Eastern Dipper.

**Zhang Xuan, Censor-in-Chief, of Wusong in Jinzhou:**
Midway up Mount Tai, I laugh at the First Emperor—
an emperor with no third generation to accept his surrender.
A trifling favor was all it took to reverse fate,
bestowed not on his brother’s grandson, but on a pine.

**Lu Qiong, Censor, of Fuliang:**
Beneath the Grand Minister’s tree, no legacy remains,
only the sobbing springs echo their eternal lament.
A foot of earth was not granted to father and son,
yet undeserving men received the emperor’s grace.

*(The Sobbing Springs lie in Guide Prefecture, where Qin Fusu met his end.)*

**Chen Lin, Vice Minister, of Putian:**
Matching rhymes with my fellow censor on our second ascent of Mount Tai—
Atop the ten-thousand-ren ridge, the imperial tent unfurls,
Qin pines and Han ministers—how strange their fate!
I grieve to follow in the footsteps of ancient worthies,
but does the mountain’s spirit permit our return?
At the summit, the wind is biting even in the sixth month,
gnarled pines and jagged rocks coil like dragons.
How many times have we ridden past Heaven’s Gate?
Back then, the imperial carriage bore its jade-green canopy.
Amid the moss-sealed mounds, we seek the Han abdication,
in the depths of the Five Clouds, we scrutinize the Qin observatory.
O East Mountain, do not idly wield your brush—
the people await a statesman’s timely rain like Xie An.

**Zha Huan, Provincial Administration Commissioner of Shandong, of Haining in Zhejiang:**
On the day after the Mid-Autumn full moon, ascending Mount Tai with colleagues—
Mount Tai looms high, gazing across ten thousand li,
the autumn hues of the Three Qi stretch endlessly.
I shake my robes in Dragon Vale, where the blue clouds cling,
lean on my sword at Heaven’s Gate, where the white sun chills.
To the east, the Yellow River meets the sea,
to the north, the purple qi coils around Chang’an.
I pity my towering ambitions—
in a daze, I seem to ride the wind astride a purple simurgh.

**Qin Jin, Minister, of Xishan:**
Stone steps coil through the Eighteen Turns,
the scenery before my eyes vast and boundless.
To the east, Sunrise Peak nears Penglai’s isles,
to the south, Heaven’s Gate opens to the cosmos.
A long whistle awakens me from the mortal dream,
my heroic spirit momentarily cleanses the pedant’s bitterness.
Jade scrolls and golden seals lie scattered nearby—
do not idly gaze upon the steles of Qin and Han.

**Chai Qi, Vice Minister, of Kunshan:**
At dawn I depart from the Gate of the Feng Sacrifice,
brushing the dust from my robes.
In a sedan chair I traverse the winding paths,
the crisp frost of this morning still lingers.
My gaze stretches to Sunrise Peak in the east,
the sea’s waters vast and boundless.
The Qin’s affairs are now distant,
the altars and shrines overgrown with brambles.
I sigh as I survey the scene,
the mountains themselves seem to echo.

**Bian Gong, Minister, of Licheng:**
Mount Tai, the sacred peak, gathers a hundred spirits,
its cliffs stand tall in the misty skies for ten thousand ages.
The earth’s axis turns with the transformations of its hidden depths,
the true qi of the Upper Clarity meets Heaven’s Gate.
Sunrise Peak is crowned with emerald pines,
the Dragon Pool’s waters warm with spring’s touch.
At dusk I shake my robes atop the summit’s stone,
gazing east toward Penglai as the sea-clouds darken.

Northward to Heaven’s Gate, the sun not yet slanted,
the fierce wind carries me past in astonishment.
The Immortal’s Cave still holds its ancient alchemical tripod,
the Jade Maiden’s shrine stands high, guarding the Azure Radiance.
Deep ravines hold snow even after a thousand years,
shaded cliffs see peach blossoms only in the fourth month.

**Of Qin’s Seals and Han’s Sacrifices:**
Qin’s seals and Han’s rites lie long abandoned,
yet tracing the towering stele stirs the passage of years.
By the Jade Emperor’s shrine, I lean upon the balustrade,
where atop the summit, even summer’s wind carries a chill.

Northward, dust and sand stretch toward the Gobi,
westward, heaven and earth converge at Chang’an.
Green clouds part to reveal three thousand realms,
while the sun levels the Eighteen Bends.
As if immortals glide through hidden ravines,
phoenix flutes trill, jade pendants chiming.
Steep cliffs rise, shrouded in mist,
Mount Tai’s numinous beauty praised through the ages.

How could such grandeur exist elsewhere?
Thirty-eight years pass before I ascend once more.
In the conch-shell hall, spring welcomes guests,
while on pine-clad cliffs, the setting sun sees woodcutters descend.
Evening’s clear chime rings through the mid-heavens—
I wonder, on which tier of mist-wreathed peaks does it linger?

---

**Imperial Tent Plateau**
The sun nears Heaven’s Gate,
while the imperial tent’s green hills stand empty.
Pavilions invite endless gazing,
ancient trees bear the marks of past ascents.
Beyond the layers of crows, the void ascends,
the Wailing Spring echoes through ten thousand ravines.
Spring’s emerald leaves never return—
how melancholy, the traces of those who came before.

---

**Turning Horse Ridge**
Before Turning Horse Ridge, the sun slants westward,
gorge flowers and cliff grasses flourish in lush profusion.
The tolling of the upper temple’s bell fades into nowhere,
only white clouds nestle by the rocks.

---

**Minister Qiao Yu of Taiyuan Ascends the Peak**
Which of the Five Peaks vies for supremacy?
The Eastern Monarch claims all things first.
In darkness and light, it divides sun and moon,
in breath and sigh, it shifts clouds and mist.
Its deep veins coil at earth’s core,
its divine work matches heaven’s height.
At Cloud Pavilion, I ask of the ancient sacrifices—
through the ages, their purpose remains obscure.
Where the hundred spirits gather in homage,
the void resounds with their proud, ringing voices.
The land anchors the Central Plain’s splendor,
the sky looms over the lower realm’s grandeur.
My old eyes survey twin peaks,
my gaze spans rivers and seas like a single autumn hair.
To visit Penglai’s isles, I would ask—
from whom might I borrow six giant turtles?

---

**Minister Xu Kui Ascends Mount Tai**
Once I climb the azure heights, how many layers must I traverse?
Steep crags and perilous ravines jostle in disarray.
Pacifying Qi and Lu, it stands as a true stronghold,
its towering peaks dwarfing Penglai’s isles.

---

**Minister Wang Tingxiang of Yifeng Ascends the Peak**
The Five Peaks are all divine and majestic,
yet Mount Tai’s cliffs blaze with unmatched fire.
Halfway up, even swift horses turn back,
from the summit, clouds and mist lie beneath my gaze.
One glance shrinks the world to a trifle,
at midnight, I witness the sun’s slow tread.
Penglai seems but a hand’s breadth away—
I fear it might hinder the flight of immortals.

---

**Educator Zhao He of Yangzhou Ascends the Peak**
Clearly, its verdant grandeur pierces the clouds,
who could fathom its primordial chaos?
Stars press down from below,
while sea and sky revolve to the east.
In its time, the imperial hunt unfolded with stately grace,
through the ages, Song Peak has shaped creation’s materials.
Now, hearing the imperial edict of reverent sacrifice,
I grasp how the divine and wise established the Three Powers.

*Author’s note: Abolishing the extravagant titles of previous dynasties.*

At first ascent, distant peaks rise ten thousand fathoms green,
the sky’s wind seems to brush my robes.
Orioles call again and again as they watch the eastern sun,
voices drift upward from below.
Misty clouds veil the temple’s bells, echoing through seaside trees,
spring’s floral breath drifts into the mountain hall.
My passion for climbing knows no season—
yet the cliff’s birds seem to chide me for my haste.

---

**Censor Cha Yue of Haining Ascends Mount Tai in Autumn’s Dusk**
Dragon Gorge’s perilous peaks loom near,
Heaven’s Gate’s ancient hall stands open.
Moonlight sharpens autumn’s crisp air,
from Sunrise Peak, the sea’s tide returns.
The land stretches far from the imperial capital,
the mountain greets Qufu’s winding path.
What boundless thoughts arise from this ascent?
My gaze extends to Phoenix Terrace.

---

**Passing the Imperial Tent Plateau**
On the day the Song emperor held court here,
this place saw many a royal excursion.
Beneath the blossoms, his twin carriages paused,
amid the pines, a hundred officials paid homage.
Clouds lingered by the jeweled throne,
the moon alone illuminated the jade altar.
Now, the Immortal’s Bridge lies desolate—
only ancient trees remain to witness.

---

**Vice Minister Xu Chengming of Dongchang Ascends the Peak**
At dawn, I tread the twin peaks, a thousand miles bright,
misty light and cloud vapors scatter in the high clear sky.
Far off, the Eastern Sea merges with the azure void,
looking down, I marvel that the mountains lie level with the earth.
The wind stirs petals like jade pendants,
the bridge retains spring grasses where dusty tassels once rested.
On Qin’s royal stone, one could stand and roar—
through the ages, it stirs deep emotion.

---

**Grand Secretary Li Dongyang of Changsha Gazes Upon the Peak**
By chance, I ascend Kuiwen Pavilion,
to behold Mount Tai’s towering summit.
Halfway up, jade waves surge through the void,
across the plains, a green dragon winds.
Purple mists cling, damp with mountain haze,
emerald peaks rise, their dark brows dense.
Vast plains stretch endlessly,
towering trees blur into verdant confusion.
Banners and staffs welcome and bid farewell,
halberds and spears clash in ceaseless motion.
Mists and clouds shift between light and dark,
rain and haze foretell fortune or calamity.
When chaos first split the primal heavens,
this land concentrated the earth’s spirit.
The *Yu Gong* divided its borders,
the sage-king Yao marked its sacred bounds.
Embracing shallows, it faces the surging sea,
from the void, it bows to Hua and Song.
Its stature commands reverence,
its name demands it be called "First."
Outwardly, its numinous power knows no bounds,
within, its virtue holds all things.
The temple’s solemnity befits a king’s image,
the ancient pines stand as ministers of old.
To the north, my body seems to strike the palace gates,
to the east, I briefly enter the imperial realm.
Climbing the cliffs, I dread the Sunrise Peak,
in the valleys, I imagine the wind’s roar.
The sagely ruler’s devotion runs deep,
while his scholar-officials grow weary of their duties.
The sacrificial feast is but a brief repast,
the palanquin bearers pity the overworked officials.
In times of drought, one must worry for the state,
when the people toil, one fears for the farmers.
I, a mere mortal, stand alone—
who will share my twin staffs of office?
Days and months slip by so easily,
mountains and rivers impose their heavy barriers.
To soar like a bird, I lack the wings,
adrift like duckweed, I follow the currents.
Scorched by heat, I long to bathe my hair in the breeze,
facing autumn, I recall the joy of baring my chest.
When the wine runs dry, the crisp air lingers,
as evening deepens, the pines grow more alert.

---

**Minister Zhang Zhen of Jinhua Ascends the Peak and Reflects**
The Bright Hall of ages past now evokes only sorrow,
today, the encircling paths lie smooth and level.
The Five Chariots of Han Wu are lost in obscurity,
while Qin’s emperor’s wordless stele invites only mockery.
The rites of ascent at Sunrise Peak were never enduring,
what purpose did the Heavenly Script’s deceit serve?
The overseers exhaust their gold and silver offerings,
the vulgar throng to the Jade Maiden’s shrine.

---

**The Cliff of Self-Sacrifice**
This land has always cherished life—
why then does the Cliff of Self-Sacrifice exist?
A single death is lighter than an autumn leaf—
who first inspired such fanaticism?

---

**Educator Li Mengyang of Henan Questions Zheng on Ascending Mount Tai**
*You ascended the Eastern Peak yesterday—*
which peak is the loftiest?
Is there a Hermit’s Stone?
How many Minister Pines remain?
The sea’s sun dips below the waves, crows darken the sky,
thunder rumbles from the dragon’s cavern.
Who says the world is small?
Even beyond civilization, it bears the king’s seal.

**Gazing Down from the Summit**
Bowing my head, no Qi or Lu in sight—
eastward, the sea shrinks to a cup.
Suddenly atop this single peak,
I cannot believe the ten thousand mountains lie open.

The sun cradles Fusang in its leap,
heaven bears Jieshi on its flank.
Behold, after the First Emperor’s reign,
still stands the Terrace of the Han King.

---

**Ode to the Five Peaks, I**
What I revere is Mount Tai—
turning east, I strain past Qi’s barriers.
Southward loom Guimeng and the solemn Su,
where immortals bestow upon me jade-green elixir.

They summon me to journey east, to question Fusang,
yet the path is steep and fraught.
At the eastern mouth, the Yellow and Ji Rivers weep in torrents.

---

**Vice Minister Ma Rujiao of Shaanxi Presents a Hua Mountain Stone to Xiongfeng**
**Eastern Sacrifice**
The year’s three micro-seasons unfold its chronicle,
a hundred rites harmonize with the times.
On the day the emperor unfurls the dark talisman,
heaven bestows the jade-green standard of the season.

The envoy’s star trembles over the palace walls,
the minister’s moon illumines the Celestial Ford.
The path passes through Qi’s ancient fiefs,
the decree seeks Lu’s new halls.

Ni Qiu fades into mist,
Mount Tai stands resplendent in its radiance.
These steles are not Qin’s vain inscriptions,
these brushwood altars replace Shun’s circuits.

Golden mud mingles with five hues,
the royal seal endures a thousand springs.
The ridge and plain coil with azure dragons,
the spring kneels before white cranes.

Gaze across the sea—islands divide like scattered beads,
watch the sun—now veiled in haze and dust.
Virtue has already forged a pact with the numinous,
form must seek kinship in dreams.

Longing for home, I chant the *Greater Odes*,
entrusting my hopes to those who aid the great fisherman.
I would compose a hymn to Song Gao,
but my brush falters, lacking divine inspiration.

---

**Zhou Xiang’s Avocation: A Man of Songling Ascends the Peak**
Yan’s garrison flaunts its divine marvels,
eastward it overawes the Lord of Peaks.
The Star of the Year shines to the eight limits,
the Dark Maiden descends to the Three Palaces.

Clouds congeal into twin gates,
fiery essence births a crimson rainbow.
For a thousand years, Han ministers stand in solemn ranks,
the ancient path is dense with Qin pines.

Golden baskets proclaim the sacred rites,
mushroom chambers glow amid emerald thickets.
Tang steles record the old calendars,
Han inscriptions mark the few who scaled the summit.

Entering the ridge, the Gate of Heaven dawns,
halting the carriage, the imperial tent stands empty.
Cinnabar clouds welcome the purple canopy,
a lone toad carves the hibiscus.

Alone, I survey the three thousand realms,
then ascend to the first tier.
Mirage towers rise at Sunrise Peak,
the Sacred Spring nurtures Lotus Summit.

Spring altars coil with incense smoke,
village shrines receive the work of transformation.
Seizing the moment, I brandish my jade scepter,
surveying all, I exhaust the dragon’s freedom.

---

**Educator Ye Fen of Ziyuan Ascends Mount Tai**
Mount Tai towers above the clustered peaks,
a colossal bastion marking the eastern pillar.
At dawn, it overlooks the Bohai’s silt,
its roots grasp the Huai and Yi Rivers.

The sacred precinct winds through grotto palaces,
the blessed land opens its lofty shrines.
Why does the stone inquire of the lingering mist?
Jade fragrance lingers in the year’s first moss.

Yu’s circuits and gazes lie buried,
Zhou’s hunts fill the Hall of Light.
Far be it—seventy sovereigns,
their records and tablets hang with empty names.

The First Emperor lacked divine aura,
Emperor Wu of Han had no immortal’s talent.
The pines of the Feng rites grow dense with boards,
the wutong trees of the south brim with foliage.

I arrive in the spring moon,
when layered peaks part the clouds.
I tread the Gate of Heaven’s vast expanse,
winding along the serpentine path.

I seem to pay homage to the Azure Radiance Sovereign,
to rinse my mouth in the Jade Maiden’s Pool.
Murmuring, I clutch the jade tablets,
stroking the cliffside steles.

Beyond the clouds, the constellations align,
my spirit roams, riding the clam and oyster.
At dawn, I ascend Sunrise Peak—
the sun rises from Fusang’s branches.

Breathing transforms mist and haze,
the world below moves with wind and thunder.
Gazing down, the vapors stretch boundless—
how can I discern the isles of Ying?
In the distance, I imagine riding a yellow crane,
round or square, following wherever it leads.

---

**Educator Wang Yu’s Stone Tablet**
The *chai* and *wang* rites once heralded peace—
who knew the wind would stir the stench of salted fish?
Only the right tablet remains,
its creeping vines and cold mist aglow in the sunset.

---

**Vice Commissioner Zhang Kun of Junzhou Ascends the Peak**
The Dao borrows Qi’s threefold emergence,
form precedes the Five Peaks.
The jade altar gleams with cloud-wreathed trees,
the shell palace glistens with dew and frost.

I hear of the hunts of Yu’s era,
I see the Feng steles of Han’s years.
Turning once more to gaze,
the purple aura lingers over the imperial homeland.

Twilight returns to the vast heavens,
spirit light gathers gods and ghosts.
The hall stands empty, clouds and mist seeping out,
the gates neighbor the Dipper and Ox.

Phoenix pipes come and go,
immortal fungi bloom anew each autumn and spring.
The fasting palace knows no sleep—
my heart yearns to cultivate the true.

---

**Zhang Bangjiao, Attendant Gentleman of Deng Prefecture, Ascends Mount Tai**
This is the land where the eastern pillar rises—
through successive dynasties, its rituals diverged.
Year-round, I bow in devotion,
praying across the nine provinces.

Its power subdues gods and ghosts,
its borders surpass the phoenix’s domain.
Eight paths connect to towering peaks,
incense clouds blaze, nearly flowing.

---

**To Tai’an Prefecture**
When the Heavenly King set forth on his hunt,
ten thousand states followed with jade and silk.
The *chai* and *wang* rites followed Yu’s model,
his grace and might aligned with Yu’s decrees.

The Qi lord’s sacrifices were ultimately abandoned,
what did the Ji heir accomplish?
A thousand years preserve the ruins—
the vernal sun still obeys his command.

---

**Zhou’s Hall of Light**
A thousand fathoms of jagged cliffs,
even birds and sparrows seem to grieve.
Vast and hazy, it spans the ancient road,
ethereal, it meets the flying towers.

The moon’s palace at dusk,
the apes’ cries in autumn’s grass and trees.
In this enlightened age, harsh governance has ceased—
sitting or standing, I revere Ni Qiu.

---

**The Towering Pavilion: Where Confucius Heard a Woman Weep**

---

**Section Chief Zheng Shanfu of Min County Ascends the Peak**
The Eastern Peak stabilizes heaven and earth,
the Yellow River threads a single strand.
The sun parts the Ying Sea’s waves,
heaven enters the clouds of Ji Gate.

The roads of Lu wound my heart,
the Qin stele still smolders at dusk.
My distant gaze cannot bear to wander—
ten thousand *li* brim with dust and haze.

---

**Vice Commissioner Fang Hao of Guan Pass Ascends the Peak**
In the third month, windless, I ascend Mount Tai,
rock flowers and valley birds keep me company.
Pitying old Zheng’s mountain-climbing obsession,
he bound himself in mist and haze, scaling despite illness.

*Author’s note: My friend Zheng Weizhi once ascended in the sixth month.*

Atop Sunrise Peak, the purple dew unfurls—
suddenly, I turn to gaze at Penglai.
The rustic is naturally a child of mist and haze—
surely the divine will descend with the moon.

---

**Attendant Gentleman Yang Ku of Qiantang Ascends the Peak**
How towering is this mountain!
Its winding paths stretch a hundred *li*.
Bird trails carved by the Five Ding,
cloud-crowned, the Three Observances rise.

Snow lingers without winter or spring,
mist and haze shift between blue and purple.
Stars hang beyond the cliffside doors,
people tread within the azure heavens.

Sunlit branches bask in radiance,
shaded valleys weave brocade from haze.
Here the immortals dwell,
its wonders defy description.

Mount Tai stands like a wall, reaching the sky,
its seventy-two peaks bristling in the ether.

Below the peaks, clouds and rain nourish the earth;
above, they pierce the constellations and sway the Purple Palace.
From sheer cliffs, ancient wutong trees shed their emerald hues;
across ravines, perilous pines span distant rainbows.

I ascend to gaze down upon the vast sea,
sitting through the night to watch the sun rise over Fusang.
In this distant land, the Double Ninth arrives—
from this lofty height, the wind scatters distant sorrows.
The fields of Han and seals of Qin are but bygone affairs;
purple asters and yellow chrysanthemums mark deep autumn.
The sky clears, pavilions brighten the Three Observances;
the wilds stretch wide, mountains and rivers define the Nine Provinces.
Yet alone lingers the longing for kin and concern for the realm—
white clouds and the vast sea share the same boundless sorrow.

At night, Mount Tai reclines in autumnal stillness,
all sounds hushed beneath the lone bright moon.
Why does an immortal ride a white deer,
at the Azure Radiance Cave’s mouth, softly playing the sheng?

At Sunrise Peak, Qin’s peaks are banners of dawn’s glow;
from Fusang, the night tide surges at the sea’s gate.
When will the fangshi of the towering ships return?
Jade tallies and golden scripts lie in desolate silence.

**Vice Minister Chen Yi of Ningbo Ascends the Peak**
A soaring pavilion perches on the summit’s edge,
hanging steps wind ever onward.
Valley echoes merge with the wind through pines,
the sky clears as sea mists dissolve.
Jade palaces encircle the Purple Pole,
jade tablets descend from the azure heavens.
The path points beyond Heaven’s Gate,
where distant chimes and qing welcome the wayfarer.

Once on the path of the Feng and Shan rites,
heaven and earth part ways from here.
All peaks converge in the primal qi,
scattered rocks form constellations in stone.
Craning upward to climb the jade steps,
turning back to glimpse the white clouds.
A flying bridge spans the deepest ravine,
the rush of waters resounds through the four mountains.

**Censor Zhu Jie of Shanyin Ascends the Peak**
The dusty world daily stirs in turmoil,
in dreams and waking, only clouds and mountains remain.
This morning, the wind of heaven is cool,
layered clouds guard the immortal’s pass.
I long to ascend and knock at its gates,
driving my carriage beyond the mortal realm.
Step by step, I scale sheer cliffs,
my body lost amid mist and haze.
From the ravine’s depths, the sound of jade pendants,
a gentle breeze carries the murmuring stream.
□
The clustered peaks seem within arm’s reach,
as if arrayed in an immortal’s procession.
The grand vista cleanses the dust from my heart,
how could I shrink from the difficulty of ascent?
The gibbons and cranes of my homeland still await,
when will this worldly carriage return?

**Censor-in-Chief Hu Zunzong of Shaanxi Gazes Upon the Peak**
Suddenly, the sound of sheng and songs, a flock of black cranes—
at once, I see the palaces adorned with purple radiance.
At the Dipper’s edge, fine dew beckons the new moon;
beyond the crows, a lone peak is steeped in evening’s fragrance.
The Han emperor’s golden altar sings of stone steles,
the Qin emperor’s jade inscriptions fade beneath moss.
Where now is Li Bai, who rode dragons?
At Sunrise Peak and Heaven’s Gate, only white clouds remain.

**Tiao Tiao Gazes Upon the Peak from the Vermilion Empyrean**
Riding the wind at the Purple Pole’s edge,
I gaze upon the peak from the cinnabar heavens.
Half the cliff’s Qin pines suspend sun and moon,
while the central vista of Zhou emerges from cloud and mist.
The peaks of Mount Hua soar like startled birds,
their shadows falling upon Fusang in graceful flight.
Crossing three streams, I glimpse a pair of cranes—
suddenly, from the Azure Emperor, a host of immortals descends.

Below the mountain, autumn’s sun still gilds the silk;
above, autumn’s rain shrouds all in darkness.
By night, stars hang beside the cliffs;
at dawn, thunder rumbles from the ravine’s depths.
Yin and yang shift in an instant, ever strange—
between heaven and earth, the vast and numinous.
When may I build a hut here to dwell,
facing these green lotus peaks day after day?

**Ascending the Peak**
At spring’s midpoint, the mountains are already green—
brushing my robes, I first reach the Five Pines Pavilion.
Dawn divides sun and moon, suspended on mossy cliffs;
clear skies array dragons and serpents, encircling emerald screens.
Heaven’s gates stand tall, aligned with the Northern Dipper;
clouds lift the Three Observances, illuminating the eastern lands.
The Qin emperor and Song sovereigns passed through in vain—
on sheer cliffs and distant peaks, their inscriptions lie broken.

The imperial palace is crowned with crimson clouds,
the immortal’s altar bathed in daylight.
A thousand winding paths lead to the summit,
a single melody plays as I near the hall.
Leaning on the railing, I survey Qin and Yue;
carved into the cliffs, the traces of Han and Tang fade.
□ Suddenly, I sit as if in heaven,
my spirit soaring, longing to take flight.

At first glance, sea and sky stretch boundless—
thoughts of the Eight Extremes drift endlessly.
Mount Hua appears no larger than a pellet,
Fusang but a ladle afloat on water.
Qin’s pines stretch unbroken in clouds,
Song’s jade tablets lie empty in vain.
The setting sun still draws my gaze,
the Yellow River winds in distant grace.
Sheer cliffs follow the crows’ flight,
the summit barely grazed by passing clouds.
Looking up and down, heaven and earth seem small,
the stars and constellations hang low.
The Sun Peak glows crimson over the sea,
the Jade Observatory pierces the rainbow.
At midnight, I sit plucking the qin—
the Celestial Palace stirs with the dawn’s crowing.

All peaks array beneath the eaves,
a single pillar stands at the world’s eastern edge.
Stone steles gather a thousand deeds,
Heaven’s Gate winds through a hundred turns.
On the mountain, the Yuanxiao moon lingers;
in my sleeves, the setting sun brings no wind.
Too restless to sleep,
the sea’s clouds glow crimson at midnight.

Towering into the azure heavens,
soaring above the azure sea.
The wind rises, the turtle stirs,
clouds part as the phoenix takes flight.
Layer upon layer, the lands of Qi and Lu unfold,
peak upon peak, they enter the celestial patterns.
Flowing radiance passes from a fair hand,
drunk, I lean upon the Five Dragons’ slumber.

**Minister Yang Zhixue of Changsha, Following Hu Kequan’s Gaze Upon the Peak**
The crimson empyrean soars beyond Heaven’s Gate,
a flying waterfall hangs high beside Sunrise Peak.
Stars and constellations hang low at the summit’s edge,
Peng and Ying lie distant, veiled in blue mist.
Twin dragons spew foam, stirring a thousand cliffs;
a lone crane rides the wind, soaring ten thousand li.
I, too, have always loved these peaks and ravines—
from this day forth, I shall learn to be an immortal.

Immortals in heaven are naturally peerless,
dragon scripts trail in the Great Mystery’s patterns.
On the Qin emperor’s terrace, rain has just cleared;
west of the Han emperor’s altar, the sun has yet to warm.
Ancient pines, lush and deep, halt the crane’s chariot;
sheer cliffs, towering and steep, are embroidered with moss.
Young attendants, their hair bound in green,
rise at dawn on the mountain to pay homage to the white clouds.

**Ascending the Peak**
With solemn reverence, I gaze upon Mount Tai,
ascending straight to its highest peak.
In an instant, clouds shift a thousandfold;
the winding mountains stretch ten thousand layers.
The Qin stele bears golden characters,
the Han tally is sealed with purple clay.
These storied traces now fade,
while the mountain flowers grow lush with each passing day.

**Visiting Bamboo Grove Temple**
The western heavens open this gate once more,
halfway up the mountain, a spring runs warm.
Cloud-wreathed cliffs stir at times,
the dragon’s pearl turns daily.
Li Bai’s verses take flight,
Kong Rong’s cup is overturned.
The return path is lovely in the evening sun,
a freezing wind blows across the broad plain.

**Editor Li Xueshi of Pingdu State Ascends the Feng Altar**
I imagine the Feng rites, the Ming Hall’s splendor,
the Altar of Sunrise Peak lies desolate.
The altar emerges from white clouds, still a Han omen;
the pavilion’s green canopy could not be Qin’s pines.
In humility and breadth, I see Liu Guangwu;
how does my capacity for listening compare to Tang Taizong’s?

When the realm is governed with the sagacity of Shun and Yu,
Kui and Long no longer offer eastern seals.

**The Joy of Three**
Light and easy, the heart finds joy in three,
while the world’s path weighs heavy with hardship.
Who would not tread the rugged cliffs’ way,
yet who knows the joy of these three?

**The Ministerial Pines**
All under heaven, the people grow gaunt and weary,
while five pine trees alone are ennobled as ministers.
Inverted was Qin’s care for people and creatures—
no wonder the masses once raised their staffs together.

**Yang Weicong, Top Graduate of Gu’an, Ascends the Feng Terrace**
Seal-rites of old were lavish for many a lord,
the *shengzhong* once made this place rich with ceremony.
Golden mud long gleamed with buried jade,
stone seals nest in clouds of bright day.
Purple qi idly spreads, palace gates appear,
white rays vie to show the old man’s toil.
How can one repay heaven and earth’s loft and depth?
Gazing afar toward Chang’an, dawn and dusk’s fragrance.

**Secretary Wang Shu Ascends the Mountain**
This crag was cleaved to reveal its beauty,
its form holds the honor of our Dao.
In mystery, it turns sun and moon,
beyond form, it is heaven and earth.
Fool’s Valley links the Qi road,
spirit’s light discerns Lu’s gate.
This floating life drifts now,
I would cry out to the gates of heaven.

Heaven and earth yet stand high and low,
rivers and mountains coil in grandeur.
The *fanzhai* rites of Yu, the hunting canons,
the *chenbi* seals of Han’s Feng Altar.
Breathing in wind and cloud’s qi,
the void’s halls and pavilions grow cold.
The slanting sun sinks into deep ravines,
I crane my neck toward Chang’an.

**The Inscriptionless Stele**
Atop Mount Tai’s peak stands a wordless stele,
they say it dates from Qin’s time.
The phoenix chariot’s eastern journey left only desolation,
wild grasses and flowers grieve spring’s passing.

**Censor Jiang Yu Ascends the Mountain**
Night reaches the Azure Mist’s heavens,
sleeping in the ganoderma chamber by moonlight.
Listening to scriptures, white cranes arrive,
pill-refining smoke rises in cinnabar plumes.
Grand music drifts from the clouds,
bright stars hang beyond the bells.
