Riding the wind, I would soar,
to the Three Isles to meet the immortals.

**Censor Zhang Duo of Suzhou Ascends the Mountain**
Winding steps coil through green moss,
jade palaces and shell halls rise in jade-green tiers.
The long sky leans against the peak’s cracked veins,
the cold sun follows the mountain’s shadow in slow drift.
Incense and fire—since when have they passed from Han’s time?
Wind and cloud forever guard the Qin stele.
Startled to find myself on this layered sky,
from the summit, I pity the crows’ slow flight.

**Gazing at the Mountain**
The Eastern Peak of Tai comes to guard the ancient mounds,
from afar, among the clouds, it overlooks fragrant isles.
Evening embraces the distant Terrace of Zong,
spring melts the snow, green trees float.
Gazing wistfully at the dusty world, I scratch my short hair,
the frozen season’s stir awakens homesick longing.
Silver palaces and jade halls appear in tiers,
dimly, I ascend again the sea’s high tower.

**Prefect Shao Jingji of Renhe Ascends the Mountain**
I tread the steps of Sunrise Peak,
at its summit, the sun is just at noon.
Beyond the eastern sea’s east,
towering stands the Fusang tree.
Fusang dries its morning dew,
the sun-bird bathes its sacred wings.
Heaven’s pole reveres the dawn’s spring,
the sun’s light suddenly fills the universe.
This great sight is ever before me,
not a rare glimpse to treasure.
Yu’s abyss once raised its glory,
midnight truly plumbs its depths.
I rest on Ying’s grass, feast on bright mist,
compose verses, drink from the Dark Garden.

**Censor Liu Huai Ascends the Mountain**
Once I wandered Mount Tai’s heights,
treading clouds for forty li.
The Bohai Sea came into view,
Sunrise Peak rose from the lower world.
Walking the void, I brushed the red clouds,
turning, I saw the western sun’s end.
Beneath the pines, I met a feathered man,
his weary face gladdened at the sight.
He gave me a thousand-year-old lingzhi,
eating it, one need not die.
The pines, ancient since Qin’s seal,
have weathered wind and rain through the years.
Golden baskets and jade tablets remain—
who will seek the elixir of life?
Ascending this small world under heaven,
I recall the wind’s path of my steps.

**Academician Liao Daonan of Puqi Gazes at the Mountain**
Tai’s peak rises in honored majesty,
a cluster of summits pierces the purple vault.
Sunrise Peak’s shadow leans on Fusang,
the moon’s toad glows dimly.
Waterfalls rush below,
like twin white dragons.
Above lies the Jade Maiden’s Pool,
the Silver River pours a long rainbow.
The Jade Maiden scatters heavenly flowers,
ten thousand blossoms of blue lotus.
The immortal Wang Ziqiao,
crimson pennants attend the upper palace.
He left me a golden-sealed letter,
bidding me follow him afar.
I would journey with him,
but the cloud-path is steep and heavy.
When may I cast off the dust’s yoke,
wash my hair east of the Xian Pool?
The Xian Pool holds a weary land,
beside the Emperor’s throne.
The Purple Void suspends jade eaves,
crimson gates gleam with gemstone.
Curved jade hangs in openwork,
misty vapors sway the starry array.
Auspicious mists curl through the groves,
fragrant blooms drape the trees.
Anqi and Han Zhong,
ride twin cinnabar phoenixes.
Gathering golden radiance herbs,
blending them with purple mist’s nectar.
Morning soars through Heaven’s Gate Pass,
evening rests in the Emperor’s mulberry.
Looking down on the world’s muddied men,
they rush like horses through a crack of light.
I wish to ride the flying waves,
roam the Eastern Sea’s expanse.

**Gazing at Sunrise Peak**
Creation’s work knows no pause,
yang’s brightness begins its cycle.
The slender waning moon sinks,
the bright morning star rises.
Night mist settles on the riverbanks,
morning mist covers the altar.
The *Yangpi* governs the eastern Yi,
the *Chunshou* divines the inner scribe.
Heaven’s image holds true essence,
human culture shines anew and fair.
Supporting the heroic, scattering the year’s withered vines,
the sun’s flower blooms in splendid grace.
The River Lord rides a dark whale,
the Mountain Spirit drives a green ox.
Pool’s reflection startles the dragon’s scales,
forest’s light graces orchids and angelica.
I envy the sun’s chariot wheels,
layered jades gleam in my gaze.
Ascending the steps is not my place,
leaving the wall is its principle.
With bare hands, I support the sun’s wheel,
my cinnabar heart threads heaven’s order.
I wish to be twin flying rainbows,
riding clouds a thousand li.

**Wang Chong of Wu Commandery Ascends Mount Tai**
Of the Five Peaks, none ranks like the Eastern Peak’s honor.
Six dragons open the imperial path,
three summits pierce heaven’s gate.
Raising my hand, Penglai draws near,
my chest swallows Qi and Lu.
Anqi’s jade-refining place—
only five-colored clouds gather.

**Surveilling Censor Chen Fengwu of Luling Ascends the Mountain**
A sharp wind blows to the highest layer,
cold qi, keen and clear, chills even the bones.
Clouds rise midair, about to rain,
the sky above the summit suddenly clears.
Sitting, I listen to the pines’ roar through a thousand crags,
walking, I watch the five-night brilliance of Kui and Bi.
I trust this journey is truly no common chance—
my sleeves flutter lightly as feathers.

**Surveilling Censor Zeng Xian of Yangzhou Ascends the Mountain**
Stone walls join clouds in layers of purple and green,
heaven’s craft carved out a jade lotus.

The snows of Gongfeng’s peaks feed unceasing streams,
a rainbow of ten thousand spans hangs ever on the ridge.
If Mount Tai’s spirit prospers the nation’s fate,
what can a court minister add but prayers for yearly harvests?

Ascending, I feel my dust-laden heart shed its weight—
nine points of Qi’s haze lie all within one glance.

**Minister Cai Jing of Houguan Ascends the Mountain**
Stone steps coil through eighteen winding turns,
heaven’s wind blows snow, and day itself grows cold.
Half-erased moss covers cliff-carved words,
slanting green grass invades the Fengshan altar.
Sun Viewing Peak looks down upon the Blue Sea,
Lotus Summit presses close to white clouds’ edge.
From this perilous pavilion, river and mountain grandeur—
I long to take up my brush and hymn the age’s peace.

**Five Pines Pavilion**
Beside the ridge, the imperial tent was once unfurled,
the jade parasol and golden chariot came here long ago.
Five pines still claim the flow of grace,
but who now knows the second emperor’s grassy grave?
Only white clouds drift idly to and fro,
while a lone green peak still stands in solemn height.
Vast plans lie desolate, leaving only sorrow—
ancient trees, crying birds, their voices full of grief.

**Yue Lun, Bureau Director of Xuanfu, Ascends the Mountain**
A thousand coils lead to Tai’s summit,
each turn crossed by streaming clouds.
From Yue View, the vast sky’s expanse,
from Qin View, the stars’ patterns spread.
Bell tones scatter through empty valleys,
pine and catalpa hold the evening’s fragrance.
Penglai seems near enough to see,
purple qi swirls in misty union.

**Nie Jing, Supervising Secretary, Ascends the Mountain**
Beyond the lone city at the mountain’s end,
I walk the peaks and hear the dawn bell.
Empty cliffs bear Han dynasty steles,
ancient paths line Qin dynasty pines.
Stone steps turn like the Silver River,
jade terraces weigh down auspicious haze.
No need to fear the setting sun—
I still climb to the highest peak.

**Zhou Liu, Yang Zhixue, and Hu Zuanzong Compose Linked Verses**
**Zhou, Supervising Secretary of Yingcheng, at the Tai Mountain Administrative Office**
A day of frozen rain, four seats grow clear,
five-blossomed court trees stir with mountain winds at dawn’s clearing.
Stone cliffs of Tai’s thousand crags—moon about to rise,
Zu and Lai’s ten thousand ravines—pines just beginning to sigh.
**Yang**
At Kequan, songs praise the white ramie’s grace,
dances love the rainbow skirts’ lightness beneath bamboo.
**Hu**
Five-blossomed hall’s long day, sparse curtains delay the guest’s sitting,
purple flutes, dark cranes descend from jade capital.
**Zhou**
Stone cliffs—
slanting wind, fine rain sit in the locust courtyard,
stacked peaks, layered ridges press close without a gap.
**Yang**
At Kequan, beneath the flowers, wine cups urge the drum’s last beat,
before the lamps, song and dance open the cloud screen.
**Hu**
Five-blossomed governor—heavenly steed comes from the western edge,
Minister of Justice—autumn roc rises from northern Qi.
**Zhou**
Stone cliffs yet envy the golden gate’s incense-case clerks,
five-clouded jade portals green within the gaze.
**Yang**
At Kequan, frozen sun, clear goblets pour pure hearts,
golden winds, green trees stir high chanting.
**Hu**
Stone cliffs—
sparse curtains drift past blue-black birds,
ancient halls glow bright against green peaks.
**Zhou**
Five-blossomed hall—
before the seat, Qin peaks in gentle haze,
across the stream, Han ministers in lush verdure.
**Yang**
Fellow officials tire not of shared purpose in delight,
**Hu**
at Kequan, ten thousand li of clouds and sky envy the gathered pins.

**Hu Jing, Vice Minister of Luiling, Ascends the Mountain**
Heaven and earth open this land,
eastern Tai stands tall in primordial chaos.
Already marveling at the Three Terraces’ nearness,
truly fit to be the four peaks’ ancestor.
Clearing skies, clouds vast and still,
rising sun, seas warm and bright.
All phenomena free of dust’s thoughts—
lightly I leave my traces here.

**Zhang Yan, Libationer of Jiangyin, at the Cliff of Abandoning the Body**
Cliff of Abandoning the Body, Cliff of Abandoning the Body,
a thousand fathoms deep, truly a stair to disaster.
People call sons and daughters foolish and ignorant,
often casting their living bones into the abyss.
Do parents not love the children they cradle?
How can they bear to sever the three years’ embrace?
In broad daylight, feathered wings remain dim,
in all directions, green careers lie vainly askew.
One morning, the foolish awaken to carve stone and ponder the Dao,
customs shift, ears and eyes open to know there is teaching.
People’s norms, heaven’s principles are naturally so—
why not die as loyal subjects, as filial sons?

**Ascending Sun Viewing Peak**
Sun Viewing Peak stands above the clouds,
Fusang’s shadow just emerging.
Mountains and rivers hold their finest scenes,
yet sorrow and sighs belong to me alone.
Jade tablets of the Qin king’s secrets,
golden caskets of the Han emperor’s texts.
A hundred years of Fengshan ground—
what are their merits and virtues now?

**Pan Tian, Surveillance Commissioner of Huai’an, Ascends the Mountain**
Vast is the virtue that nurtures life,
endless the heart that repays its source.

**The Wind and Clouds Converge in Grand Sacrifice**
Wind and clouds unite in sacred feast,
sun and moon rejoice in ascent.
Vast qi drifts above the imperial pole,
spirit descends to the stone forest.
Graceful, a pair of cranes draw the chariot,
soaring to the azure clouded peak.

**Pan Zhen of Ziyuan, Southern Heavenly Gate, in Reply to Chen Shifeng**
A thousand gates, ten thousand fathoms high, lean against heaven’s opening—
to ascend the void is swift and joyous.
Clouds veil the mortal world from sight;
stepping out, one laughs and descends from the sky.

**Xiao Hao’s Leisure, Qin Song of Jiangxi**
Lush pines stand tall upon the cliff,
cherished by divine principle.
Their boughs would drive the gates of heaven,
jade canopies shielding from summer rain.
They raise their ambition to the mysteries of the dark,
no longer envying gold and purple.
Yet they bear the title of Grand Master—
a thousand ages bear this deep shame.

**Hu Shen: Qin Song**
Five pines tower, piercing the heavens,
for a thousand years still favored by the Qin emperor’s grace.
Grass and trees rejoice at the dragon’s passing,
while scholars nurse their grievous wrongs.

**Long Zhui of Jiangdong on Qin Song**
The Second Emperor vainly schemed for all under heaven,
Xianyang’s palaces now lie in ruins.
Where once his imperial progress halted for the eastern rites,
only the gray-bearded Five Grand Masters remain.

**Bai Shihui, Assistant Minister of Shaanxi, Ascends the Mountain**
Donning clogs, I climb the heights,
a poet’s joy in shared wandering.
At the fifth watch, the sun appears,
in mid-summer, autumn’s chill arrives early.
Rain rises from the mountainside,
springs flow from stone’s eyes.
The mountain’s spirit shifts and transforms,
spanning ten thousand li across the divine land.

**Yao Kui, Vice Minister of the Court Stables, of Changping, After Snow on Mount Tai**
Dawn’s crimson sun breaks through the clear sky,
I sit in the mountain sedan, treading the snowy path.
Frost-laden trees wrap blossoms—spring draws near,
frozen streams form jade, silent in their flow.
Mist clears from the summit, peaks emerge,
wind sweeps the empty cliffs, a thousand sounds arise.
The old monk, deep in clouds, knows my passing—
a few clear chimes of the bell welcome me from the pines.

**Song of the Five Pines**
From Black Dragon Pool, the serpent-mother emerges,
her frost-scales shed, the reeking clouds damp.
Her matted beard bristles with ten thousand needles,
her towering frame stretches three thousand feet.
Divine power guards her, primal qi concentrated,
she battles storms and rain, shaking the azure sky.
Her steadfast integrity shakes past and present,
yet she once accepted the Qin king’s reckless title.
Waves surge, yin winds rise,
a thousand sounds howl in harmony.
Fit to pillar the state, yet never tested—
forsaken in the empty mountains.
Her verdant hue knows no autumn or winter,
swallowing ice, spitting snow through trials.
If a master craftsman should one day meet her,
she would be offered to Penglai’s palace.
General Meng Tian and Prince Fusu,
for ten thousand li, their merits recorded—yet no reward.
Instead, the title was bestowed on five pines—
the First Emperor’s folly thus revealed.
Xianyang’s flames brought the Second Emperor’s fall,
yet the five pines endure, touching the vault of heaven.
When the True Ancestor’s six dragons once toured here,
they too named them "Imperial Canopy," their glory unfurled.
How fortunate, O pines, to meet a knowing lord!
Alas, how many extraordinary men in this world—
endowed with talent, defiant in integrity—end in obscurity,
while even the cold pines fare better.
I come again and again to sit in their cool shade,
green shadows carpet the earth, mist swirling.
Stroking their long trunks, I sing a mournful song—
the setting sun in the empty mountains, what sorrow it brings!

**Zhang Chen, Vice Minister of the Court Stables, of Kuaiji, Ascends the Mountain**
Behold the revered Mount Tai,
firmly anchoring the nine provinces.
Empty light merges with the azure sky,
the inverted reflection of the Yellow River flows.
Friends gather, unrestrained in their ascent,
jade pendants clinking as they scale the clear autumn.
Gazing up, the nine heavens stretch boundless,
looking down, the eight directions lie in view.
Confucius left his distant traces here—
my heart drifts in longing.

**Zhang Peng, Censor of Qinyang, Ascends the Mountain in the Style of Du Fu**
The slanting sun lingers over rugged paths,
the day’s ascent is not yet done.
I wander among the peaks,
chanting and admiring from dawn to dusk.
I seek the immortal boy on the rocky crag,
soaring high in pursuit of the flying crow.
Such sublime journeys are hard to repeat—
youth does not return.

**Zhou Lang Ascends the Mountain**
A thousand peaks cluster in folds,
ten thousand ravines wind in succession.
The sacred map marks the earth’s axis,
the grand vistas explore the sealed boundaries.
Dew moistens the three magic mushrooms, their splendor fresh,
light congeals on the eight stones, their hues vivid.
I recall the sorrowful Song inscriptions,
the Qin era’s trees planted for the rites.
Venturing to trace the ancient paths,
I feel the cliffs to read the old carvings.
Now, imperial tours are rare,
how many times has the Feng and Shan been performed?
From the terrace, a flying rainbow seems to fall,
the hanging veil holds the inverted scene.
The wonders are boundless—
I would pay homage to the true immortals.

**Zheng Datong, Minister of the Court Stables, Ascends Mount Tai**
Of the Five Peaks, this is the finest,
its divine power proven for ten thousand years.
My dreams have long reached here,
the sacred shore was first scaled by sages.
Qi and Lu stretch empty for a thousand li,
the stars seem but a single layer away.
Our august dynasty honors the grand rites—
no need to invoke the Han era’s praise.

**Yang Fu, Prefect of Yuyao, Ascends Mount Tai**
Famous mountains exist under heaven,
but none compare to the Great Peak.
Deep valleys cradle stars,
mid-heaven unfolds a painted scroll.
A thousand shifting scenes in a single glance,
one view encompasses all within the realm.
I seek the traces of Yu and Zhou—
the woodcutter laughs at my folly.

**Mei Shoude, Vice Education Commissioner of Xuancheng, Ascends Mount Tai**
A lifetime of longing for this towering peak—
today, at last, I climb the Heavenly Gate.
Layered ridges rise beyond the azure sky,
the winding path makes the white sun seem low.
Clouds stretch east beyond Penglai’s sea,
misty light rivals the western Hua’s grandeur.
I regret my inability to compose a fu—
lingering all day, my thoughts grow lost.
Dawn’s mist swirls, opening the grotto palace,
rock’s glow bursts forth from the cloud roots.
Jumbled halls cling to the crimson ravine,
purple-green vines drape the stone gate.
The vast sea’s waves float the sun and moon,
morning and evening winds and rains divide heaven and earth.
Step by step, the mortal world grows small—
of the Five Peaks, only this stands supreme.

**Leaning on the perilous railing of the Jade Emperor’s Summit,**
a thousand acres of mist and rosy clouds fill the grand view.
Immortal music seems to play in rainbow plumes,
the celestial wind brushes the cold of Dipper and Ox.
Nine heavens guard the ancient Qin altar,
a thousand years of moss seal the Han steles.
Year’s end brings many emotions to this ascent—
I cannot bear to turn and gaze toward Chang’an.

**Bao Ming, Provincial Surveillance Commissioner, Ascends the Mountain**
Step by step, Mount Tai rises,
heaven and earth compressed to a foot’s span.
Staff and sandals follow the clouds and thunder,
stars and constellations snag the piled-up caps.
A single glance scatters the dusty vapors,
a pure breeze stirs beneath both arms.

A second glance unfinds the heart and spirit,
rivers and springs fill the liver and diaphragm.
The Hall of Everlasting Service stands in emptiness,
the Hall of Resting Steeds faces the azure void.

Lofty the Southern Gate of Heaven,
stark the Stone of Self-Abandon.
The mountain palanquin descends past towering trees,
drums and pipes lead the way for the foremost halberd.
Dusk deepens as we reach the trackless end,
the sacred shrine soars atop the sky’s ridge.
The radiant numen terrifies this heart—
how could it be less than gazing at the towering walls of the celestial capital?

Feasts and offerings gather from all directions,
mountains and seas store gold and silk.
A single couch rests in the mountain’s embrace,
pines and springs harmonize with strings and leather.
At midnight, the eastern sky glows with reproach,
the sea’s depths marvel at the sun’s crimson.

**Xu Yingyuan, Vice Censor-in-Chief, a Man of Qiantang, on Mount Tai**

Mount Tai, solemnly marking the eastern meridian,
its summit falsely rumored as the court of immortality.
Steles recall the Han’s triple seals, three visions distant,
trees preserve the Qin’s five pines, ever verdant.
The Sun Pool’s daily bath reveals depths unseen,
the Yin Grotto’s flowing clouds suddenly become audible.
On this day, wind and mist briefly stir—
cease sighing over Mount Xian’s obscurity.

**What is Mount Tai like?**
Joyous at dawn, emerging beyond the clouds.
Ascending here, I look down upon Meng and Yi,
I long to behold the path of Lu.
Queli, deep and lofty,
where the ancients once arrayed their ranks in grass.
Still I imagine the admonitions of the Wu Gate,
now I know the world is small.

**Accompanying Attaché Cai on Ascending the Huansui Pavilion at Haoli**

A distant rider halts in the verdant woods,
ascending the terrace, the emerald meadows renew.
Clouds and mountains harbor the reclusive official,
poetic elegance awaits the kingly visitor.
Flowers bloom as the sun pauses at noon,
orchid standards vie to adorn the spring.
I cherish your bamboo-stream enthusiasm,
throughout the evening, facing purity itself.

**Revisiting Mount Tai**

Once I served as an official in the mountain city,
a decade later, I ascend its perilous heights again.
My heart’s desire lies in hills and valleys,
the years have whitened my temples in sorrow.
Worldly sentiments briefly meet with wine,
my nature still delights in poetry.
Truly I am but a stubborn old man,
eccentric as in former times.

**Farewell to My Disciples at Mount Tai**

At dawn, I depart through the Qianfeng Gate,
crossing the floating waters of the river.
Crimson sunlight adorns the first glow,
journeying clouds—how swiftly they race.
Looking back, I recall the distant past,
the scenery once more resembles it.
Mount Lu remains in sight,
my journey begins anew from here.

**Fan Se, Compiler, a Man of Licheng, Ascends the Mountain**

Clouds and rivers, vast and still, nestle by the cliffs,
wind’s shadows, delicate and clear, on the Eighteen Bends.
The Jade Maiden’s Spring flies, moistening the mountain,
the Hibiscus Peak, though summer, remains chill.
A century in the dusty world—a springtime dream,
ten thousand miles of heaven and earth—a single glance.
At dusk, leaning on the stone railing, stars draw near,
unaware that my body rests amid white clouds.

**Ma Lin, Prefect, a Man of Shaanxi, Ascends the Mountain**

Sublime Mount Tai, revered above all,
on this day, my ascent stirs boundless emotion.
Ten thousand ravines roar with wind through grass and trees,
the mountain’s cloudy vapors soak my robes.
The Qin’s seals and Han’s era take shape in its contours,
the lands of Lu and Qi’s hills stretch into the distance.
A single path gradually leads to the celestial realm—
where might I inquire of the Azure Emperor?

**Huang Shengzeng, a Man of Wu, Longs for Mount Tai**

Qi and Lu open to the eastern peak,
its distant blue stretches endlessly.
Chang’an once framed my gaze,
the grand assembly of Wu once filled my eyes.
I await the mountain parrot’s report,
alone, I watch the sun flow over the sea.
If Master Ji Qiu were still here,
I would take up my zither and wander with him.

**Cai Runan, Vice Minister, a Man of Deqing, Accompanies Xu of Tai’an in Ascending the Huansui Pavilion at Haoli**

The Huansui Pavilion, a place of ancient beauty,
wind and flowers, spring’s tender embrace.
Again I follow the immortal official’s footsteps,
able to wander with the white clouds.
Swords vie like lotus blossoms,
cups float with bamboo-leaf wine.
How is it that Ge Hong’s abode,
with its starry constellations, overlooks the Mushroom Hill?

**The Ancient Wutong Tree at the Mount Tai Academy**

Its shadow reaches near the fragrant incense,
its sound sways the windows and doors clear.
In the void, white clouds ascend,
over the sea, the ancient dragon’s spirit.
Briefly resting amid spring’s verdure,
I recall the phoenix’s song.
As evening comes, clouds begin to rise,
the numen stirs, the mountain’s peaks tower.

**Gao Hui, Judicial Commissioner, a Man of Hefei, Ascends the Mountain**

Emerald peaks carve a thousand hibiscus blossoms,
auspicious mists coil around the immortal terrace.
After the jade pool’s feast, golden youths depart,
a purple phoenix arrives before the moonlit screen.
Rain clears, returning clouds perch on treetops,
at night’s depth, the sun emerges—Penglai is seen.
In times past, I had not reached the Gate of Heaven,
the nine points of Qi Zhou were but a guess.

I tread upon a thousand hibiscus peaks in autumn’s decay,
the Maker, without cause, wanders with my heart.
The Dipper’s handle joins the northwest, the celestial pivot near,
the sea splits the southeast, the earth’s axis floats.
Frost’s shadow spies the couch beyond the clouds,
the cold wind fills the tower by the crows.
The dust in my breast is wholly swept away,
a single pillow of pure spring flows unceasing.

Stone steps, ten thousand turns, scale the great heights,
layered peaks and ridges, their green unending.
Precipices and flying waterfalls plummet from midair,
glittering ice flowers congeal at the forest’s edge.
Turning southward, the eye’s reach expands,
mist and haze settle, the world grows small.
My spirits rise, I feel the wind stir beneath my arms,
at the mountain’s summit, I circle to view the Qin stones.

Leaning from the Sun-Watching Peak, I gaze toward Penglai,
at dawn, the golden crow bathes in the crimson sea.
Lifting my head, the divine capital lies to the northwest,
five-colored fair-weather clouds occasionally drift.
The azure sky is within reach, stars can be plucked,
soaked and dripping, the eastern wall glistens.
I bow in reverence to the Jade Emperor, presenting my jade tablet,
the mountain’s height, the wind’s dew, my robes grow cold.

Vast and distant, the sky descends with pipes and cranes,
the cosmos gathers within my broadened breast.
At the Peach Blossom Valley’s mouth, the path runs deep,
strange rocks, phosphorescent, hang as if about to fall.
The Five Pines gnaw at the Han, exhaling purple mist—
where might I seek the immortal?
Golden mud and jade seals lie buried in autumn grass,
the seventy-two elixirs, scattered and lost.
Cold crows caw upon the wild pear branches,
the frozen moon, delicate, ages the mountain stones.

**Li Jiongran, Vice Minister, at the Cliff of Self-Abandon**

Beneath the Cliff of Self-Abandon, depths unfathomable,
I often wonder at those who lightly cast away their lives.
I too have a body, yet I value it dearly—
I would abandon it only for my lord and kin.

**Cheng Zhou, Registrar, a Man of Wuxi, Ascends the Mountain**

Towering Mount Tai, first among peaks,
its gaze surveys heaven and earth, leaving all void.
It swallows and spouts mist and clouds, confounding the lower realm,
it forges and tempers sun and moon upon its lofty summit.
The Qin steles stand wordless, their fame still intact,
the Tang’s cliff carvings, sealed by moss.
An exiled wanderer, I climb in sorrow over past affairs,
my emaciated frame cannot endure the unyielding wind.

**Zhou Jin, Imperial Censor, a Man of Cixi, on the Bright Hall**

The Zhou dynasty endured eight hundred years,
its eastern progresses and court assemblies before the Bright Hall.

**Meng Ke’s Legacy Lingers Still**

The ruins remain—Meng Ke’s strength endures,
to this day, those who ascend and gaze preserve his true transmission.

**Zheng Yun, Imperial Censor, Ascends the Mountain**

Unfinished worldly affairs,
I briefly take leave of the White Jade Pass.
Parting clouds to follow the moon’s gate,
riding a crane down to the mortal realm.
Worldly flavors fade like water,
while dreams and spirits dwell ever in the mountains.
Lingering in Dragon Vale to rest,
when shall I climb again?

**Tang Shaoxun Ascends the Mountain**

Dawn clears, the Heavenly Gate releases distant radiance,
the spirit of Mount Tai keeps its promise, fortunately unbroken.
Mountain clouds embrace the Dao, welcoming the immortal’s canopy,
the sea’s sun parts the mist, rising over embroidered robes.
A thousand miles of imperial maps adorn the age of Tai,
the nine heavens’ celestial patterns bow at the sacred portal.
Recalling the ancient *feng* rites of ascent,
evening haze veils the abandoned terrace in emerald twilight.

**Fu Zhen, Imperial Censor, Ascends Mount Tai**

The Tai Palace leans into autumn mountains,
high amid purple and green.
Stars and court descend to greet the sun,
immortals’ palms tread clouds in ascent.
Cliffs stand—heaven lowers its eaves,
clear skies unfold, illuminating the realm.
Embarrassed to receive the imperial commission for the provincial inspection,
I return in reverence, having performed the rites for the gods.

**Li Lun, Food Officer, Ascends the Summit**

After rain, the joy of climbing revives,
a few peaks emerge in fresh green.
Wind stirs the ornate pillars, swaying the empty sky,
the sun embraces the jade palace, pressing close to the great void.
Auspicious omens still linger from Yu Shun’s grace,
the lamp’s transmission belongs solely to Lu’s *Xuan* scriptures.
Gazing upon heaven and earth, what bound can be known?
A single envoy star floats across ten thousand miles.

**Wang Tinggan, Messenger, a Man of Jing County, Ascends the Mountain**

Mount Tai presses close to the central heavens,
ascending, all things hang suspended.
Terraces and halls frame the sea’s sun,
palaces brush the purple haze of the celestial pole.
Who rivals this fame of mountains and rivers?
Heaven and earth’s splendor is uniquely claimed.
How can joy at dawn be exhausted?
My brush stirs the trailing white clouds.

At the summit, testing my ascent,
amid wind and mist in the ethereal distance.
Shun’s progresses left their altars,
Yu’s chisel shaped the ancient rivers and mountains.
The moonlit path to the Heavenly Gate,
the *zhi* chambers by the Azure Sea’s bay.
Heroic spirits exhaust the eight directions,
this place alone secludes itself from the mortal world.

**Liu Dao, Minister, a Man of Cangzhou in Zhili, Ascends the Mountain in the Second Month, Blocked by Snow**

Spring’s orioles and flowers still linger before my eyes,
I follow the imperial horses up the winding mountain paths.
Clouds drift past the jade hall, incense smoke delicate,
snow blankets the green cliffs, the trees’ hues turn cold.
The Qin ridges must pity the traveler’s perilous road,
the Han palaces seem as if descending immortals were difficult.
At Sunrise Peak, gazing east toward the sea,
I vainly recall the flying rosy clouds and the chariot of the colored phoenix.

**Wang Ruxiao, Compiler, a Man of Dongping, Ascends Mount Tai**

Leaning on my staff at dawn, I step upon the layered peaks,
my gaze widens as I look afar.
Sheer cliffs bite the sun, breaking it,
stone steps brush the clouds, deafening.
Qi and Lu’s thousand-year splendor,
heaven and earth held in a single fingertip.
The *feng* rites once took place here,
the joy of climbing and gazing knows no end.

**Guo Jian, a Man of Hongdong, Ascends Mount Tai**

Peaks and ridges stand like walls, green clouds massed,
the Supreme Ultimate first divided—this mountain endured.
Ancient pines, lush and dense, coil beneath the imperial canopy,
layered stone steps ascend to the Heavenly Gate.
Mountain peaches and wild cherries vie in bloom,
a winding stream’s square spring flows warm.
The *feng* rites of Qin and Han leave traces of the past,
returning as the sky’s hues turn to dusk.

**Jing Yanyan, Vice Minister of the Court of Imperial Sacrifices, a Man of Quanzhou, Ascends the Mountain**

Mount Tai’s accumulated greenery rises thick at dawn,
on a spring day, I ascend to the azure heavens.
At my ear, I faintly hear the celestial words draw near,
the peak’s summit levels with the Jade Emperor’s court.
No need to envy the flaunting of jade phoenixes,
I shall see the soaring chariot challenge the Dipper’s handle.
How might I rise on emptiness to traverse the eight directions,
conveying the people’s sufferings to the divine Yao?

**Zhong Yan, Prefect of Yongzhou, a Man of Baoying, Ascends the Mountain**

Tiered cliffs and lofty pavilions open to the clear radiance,
after ten years, I return—my dream unbroken.

**Lin Yinglin, Vice Prefect, a Weary Recluse Visiting the Stone Chamber**

The jade maiden presents blossoms, snow-like nectar unfurling,
the immortal elder imparts his secrets, bestowing a robe of rosy mist.
This day in the azure heavens, I gaze upon the Three Luminaries,
in what year was a single gate built beside the jade-green stream?
The revelry deepens as the moon of kinship ascends,
distant wind through the pines carries the faint evening bell.

**The Jade Emperor’s Pavilion**

A perilous pavilion clings to the layered heavens,
mountains and rivers stretch into the distant view.
Crows cross the frontier passes beneath the sky’s expanse,
the sun cradles the tide at the sea’s gate.
Mist and dew part to reveal crimson truths,
clouds and rosy hues drift past azure flutes.
This serene delight arises naturally—
no need for village monks to summon me.

**Lin Yinglin, Vice Prefect, a Weary Recluse Visiting the Stone Chamber**

The celestial gentleman’s refined spirit delights in secluded quests,
together we seek immortal whispers, entering the emerald forest.
A brocade cliff suddenly opens to a cinnabar cavern,
a sacred spring seems to pour from the depths of a grotto-heaven.
Cloud steps spiral in the empty sky,
below, mist-laden blossoms cast shadows in the distance.
Long have I been broken and adrift—
only now, amid the dust of the world, do I recognize my original heart.

**Pu Yinglin, Compiler, a Man of Wuxi, Visiting Mount Tai**

A thousand peaks converge in lush beauty,
the numinous source murmurs with myriad sounds.
The borders of Lu open to boundless wilds,
the lands of Yu are anchored by this lofty mountain.
The Milky Way hangs near overhead,
mist and clouds scatter before my eyes.
At ease, I hold the world in miniature—
how might one scale its ancient traces?

**Du Tai, Presented Scholar, a Man of Changqing, Ascending the Mountain**

This mountain alone coils mightily above the earth,
golden stalks and jade grasses guard its sacred altar.
To the west, Kunlun fades into misty clouds,
to the east, the Eastern Sea merges with the boundless cosmos.

**Gu Jizong, Presented Scholar, a Man of Licheng, Ascending the Southern Slope of Mount Tai on New Year’s Day**

At the immortal’s altar, I test my brush with fresh wine—
who among the wild grasses would recognize a court poet?
First, I pray for a thousand years of longevity to the Southern Mountain,
then gaze upon the Northern Dipper, heralding spring across ten thousand li.
Snow embraces emerald screens where eagles transform,
cloud-swept cinnabar ravines teem with tame deer.
Wang Qiao, in the end, became a master of the reed pipe—
daring not ride the simurgh to audience in the purple court.

**Liu Ermou, Presented Scholar, a Man of Dongping, Ascending the Mountain**

The Azure Lord’s true source stretches far,
rosy fragrance and vital breath harmonize.
Valley winds stir the sea’s trees,
the sunlit day guards the mountain’s thunder.
Golden gates emerge beyond the clouds,
the Jade Cord hangs low past the constellations.
Who says the earth’s limits are small?
Yu’s tribute records all lands, even those tattooed at the edges.

**Tao Xingao, Censor, a Man of Pengze, Ascending Mount Tai**

The southern lands’ beauty gathers at Heng and Lu,
Mount Tai stands alone in majesty, never in vain.
Today, immortal spirits descend with swords and pendants,
mid-heaven’s towers and terraces overlook the palace steps.
Azure mists enfold the Qin pines’ shadows,
crimson banners hang in pairs before the Jade Emperor’s abode.
The stone chamber’s path is now lost—
where might a courtier seek the cinnabar script?

**Distant immortal envoys accompany the village spring,**
everywhere, celestial winds scatter upon rocky streams.
In the ravine, no yellow calves drink,
at the peaks, only white clouds seal the heights.
Who pities the poet singing of spring trees?
Slowly, he listens to the mountain monk’s midday bell.
I dine on sesame, content in solitude—
turning, I am sure to meet the jade grasses again.

**Yuan Kui, Educational Commissioner of Huizhou, a Man of Suzhou, “Song of Dreaming of Mount Tai”**

I have heard of Mount Tai,
foremost of the Five Peaks, towering and vast,
its heights piercing the azure vault.
Sun and moon at Heaven’s Gate retreat in its shadow,
its might presses upon the nine domains—how grand!
Fusang and Jieshi lie far below,
how could one speak of Yi and Gui, Lian and Guimeng?
In night’s dream, I ride six dragons, treading lightning, driving the wind.
I grasp the stars, tread the well, ascend Sunrise Peak,
soaring to pay homage at the Palace of the Primordial Sovereign.
White elms and red cassia flank the imperial way,
amid them, one with a face like peach blossoms.
Jade-pure, snow-green, she reveals gleaming teeth,
a pair of fifteen-year-old golden youths hold her hands.
She imparts to me a sacred talisman, bidding me read the tadpole script—
its strange characters defy the comprehension of mortal bones.
My worldly frame cannot be exchanged—I awaken,
lost in the eastern dawn’s tide.
A blue-black bird from the sea invites me,
a distant journey to Mount Tai, the ancestral peak, unfolds its scroll.
Kneeling, I read the starry script again and again,
its cloud-seal script blurs with the dream’s traces.
Shang Ping’s marriage ties remain unfinished,
Sima Xiangru lies ill, his letters left blank.
When might I grow wings in broad daylight,
and fly to Mount Tai’s first and highest peak?

**Zha Bingzhi, Vice Minister of the Court of Judicial Review, a Man of Haining, Ascending Mount Tai After Summer Rain Clears**

The fiery brightness of summer passes, rain stills the mountain mists,
the peak’s hues blend with the evening’s warmth.
Leaning on my staff, I sit and watch the forest’s moisture,
parting my robe, I still point toward the clouds within the grotto.
The Lion Peak’s waterfall cascades through empty space,
the Dragon Gully’s springs murmur along both banks.
They say the new clarity offers an evening vista—
the nine fields’ farmers must now be full of joy.

**Tang Yu, Surveillance Commissioner, a Man of Haining, Ascending Mount Tai**

Jade seals conceal the cinnabar chamber,
jade tablets stand in the upper realm.
Climbing cliffs, I enter Dragon Gully,
threading paths that wind like a sheep’s intestines.
Stones loom perilously, their shapes threatening to fall,
springs flow as if poised to take flight.
At dawn, I ascend Sunrise Peak—
faintly, I glimpse Fusang.

**Xu Shen, Censor, a Man of Jiande, Ascending Mount Tai**

I have heard of the Jade Emperor’s palace in the heavens—
here, crimson banners and starry altars meet.
At midnight, sunlight shimmers on the sea,
through all four seasons, incense and mist swirl with the celestial winds.
Golden caskets and jade seals connect to all emperors,
first among the Five Peaks and Three Mountains.
Turning, I see the cities and towns below—
how many layers of clouds and ravines lie between?

**Wu Zun, Censor, a Man of Haining, Ascending the Mountain**

Mount Tai’s sheer heights press against the azure heavens,
its shadowed cliffs know wind and waves even in broad daylight.
To the west, the Raven Path at Heaven’s Gate stretches far,
to the east, Sunrise Peak points toward Fusang.
Qin’s trees still line the imperial procession route,
Han’s altars stand empty before the Jade Emperor’s court.
From here to Chang’an must be a thousand li—
the Northern Dipper’s handle, how weary the longing gaze!

**Wu Bopeng, Minister, a Man of Yiwu, Ascending the Mountain**

Mount Tai has ever been a grotto-heaven,
brushing my robes, I ascend its perilous summit at dawn.
Beyond a thousand years of Qi and Lu’s pilgrimages,
the ten thousand li of rivers and mountains lie within a hand’s span.
Han’s and Qin’s seals leave only trailing grasses,
verdant pines and emerald peaks mingle with the clouds.
Suddenly, I am filled with the urge to take flight—
pouring rosy mist, I call to the banished immortals.

**Again, After Wu Chuquan’s Rhyme**

The steep cliffs of Pengxuan pierce the cinnabar heavens,
the Dragon’s Mouth’s flying springs spray white waves.
The sky reaches Fusang, the Eastern Sea vast,
the earth nears the Wen and Ji, the rosy mists high.
Having just ascended Yueguan, I think of my homeland,
then turn my gaze toward Chang’an, longing for the imperial court.

The cosmos fills my gaze, yet all is warhorses,
unbearable the weariness of north and south.
My hacking cough seems to echo in the crimson heavens,
the murmuring streams entwined with pines’ roar.
A thousand peaks, rain passed, vie in celestial radiance,
the Three Observances chill in wind, the sun’s hue aloft.
Having read every cliffside stele, I pity distant ages,
no *feng* and *shan* rites—this pure dynasty stirs lament.

**Spring mountains, orioles cry beyond the winding paths,**
the homeward road, though rugged, brings no sense of toil.

**Fang Zhengxiu, Registrar, Changcheng native, ascends the mountain**
The mountain’s brow lowers in solemn gaze,
the illusory world all dust and haze.
I recall Master Xianmen,
who from layered skies surveyed the nine realms.
Tao Kan dreamed of eight wings,
then soared through the Gate of Flying Clouds.
The Azure Mists seem near—
I bow my head to ask the Heavenly Granddaughter.

Sun and moon hang like twin pellets,
the cosmos a vast wilderness.
At the highest peak’s summit,
I sit in reverence, sovereign of all.

**Shen Yinglong, Censor-in-Chief, Wucheng native, ascends Mount Tai**
Of the Five Peaks, Mount Tai is hailed as foremost,
mighty it stands on Qi and Lu’s border.
Unyielding, it guards the eastern pillar,
where the Central Plains’ *qi* converges.
From distant lands, all turn in awe,
yet my longing remains vague and dim.
Holding the jade tablet, I fulfill my long-held vow,
my journey marked by solemn truth.
With companions, I ascend the perilous summit,
my spirit ever vigilant.
If prayers are offered, they shall be answered,
for the gods’ power is truly vast.
The drought ends, timely rains descend,
crimson clouds spread in misty veils.
The river’s silt chokes the roads, the sweet springs flow clear—
all by the Son of Heaven’s command.
The court relies on the gods’ favor.
The rites completed, I gaze upon the pure scene,
the Six Directions truly seem confined.
The mountain empty of worldly clamor,
I hear the celestial melody.
Weary of flight, the immortals beckon me,
suddenly I ride the simurgh on a distant journey.
They teach me the secrets of the Three Mysteries,
feasting on rosy mist, sipping the night’s essence.
From Sunrise Peak, I look down on the vast seas,
crimson light spills like an unfurled canopy.
The lands of Wu and Yue blur in the distance,
the Yellow River winds like a sash.
In the wind, I pluck jade mushrooms,
on stone I chant beneath pines and cypress.
The seals of Qin and Han remain only beyond withered grasses,
ancient steles lost in the wild.
Mourning the past, I grieve for the present,
stroking my breast, my sorrow deepens.
The northern barbarians still rampage,
the Japanese pirates bring chaos and ruin.
I bow my head to ask the spirit of Mount Song,
when shall peace and prosperity return?

**Zeng Jun, Censor-in-Chief, Zhongling native, *Record of a Journey to Mount Tai***
The eastern peaks rise alone, towering and majestic,
a thousand fathoms of numinous light touch the celestial terrace.
Golden lotus petals carve the sun’s ascent,
jade pavilions open against the sky.
Incense smoke, wind-warmed, drifts past Qin’s trees,
stone seals, aged deep, lock Han’s altars.
One glance spans the cosmos through ten thousand kalpas,
rosy clouds’ hues fly into my wine cup.

**Yong Dao, Censor, Linzhao native, ascends Mount Tai**
A thousand *li* of Qi’s cities gaze toward Mount Tai,
green mountains coil in grandeur, lofty and sublime.
The Sunrise Peak overlooks the vast sea,
the mountain’s might spans the realm like Heaven’s Equal.
A hundred generations’ *feng* rites mark glorious deeds,
ten thousand lands’ incense bears the gods’ mysterious power.
From the sacred Lingyan Peak, I survey the pure court,
clouds contend, winds still—the vast firmament empty.

**Heard long this mountain’s height,**
once ascended, its towering majesty stirs my gaze.
Dragon Gully’s gaze spans ten thousand fathoms,
Heaven’s Gate, a hand’s span, brushes the layered skies.
The *shengzhong* tablets of Qin and Han endure,
no one now praises the rites of Yu and Tang.
Surveying the peaks, all seem dwarfed in boundless space,
clouds and mist stretch distant as sea and sky.

**He Tinggang, Censor, Shaowu native, ascends the mountain**
Ten thousand fathoms—startled, I behold its sheer heights,
one man’s ascent taxes a hundred’s labor.
My long-held vow fulfilled, the people’s strength spent,
yet my heart’s delight finds bold expression.
Exploring wonders, I tread the cinnabar steps,
after toasting, I gaze where others have inscribed.
I recall Confucius’ ascent and contemplation—
who since has grasped his silent teaching?

**Ma Sancai, Censor, Renhe native, ascends the mountain**
Layered peaks, ten thousand fathoms, part to new-fallen mist,
I seize the moment to ascend, my carefree spirit boundless.
Mountains rise beyond the clouds where birds take flight,
deep forests hold spring’s end, fallen blossoms before.
Heaven’s Gate stretches far along the cinnabar path,
the sea’s sun hazy amid azure trees’ smoke.
From the twelve gates of Qi’s lands, I seek—
wheat fields lush, waters brim the channels.

**Surveying the sights, I come from Wancheng in spring,**
weary palaces fade into clouded heights.
Qin’s pines still sway in lingering shade,
Han’s emperors’ *feng* altars stand empty.
Stone cliffs gleam with poets’ verses,
Mount Tai’s majesty outshines a minister’s talent.
The vermilion court, white-haired, I turn back—
on the peak’s summit, each of us lingers in melancholy.

**Jade Maiden Pool**
What year did the Jade Maiden depart?
Her name lingers by the water’s edge.
Her eyebrows, perhaps, were shaped like orchids,
the moon seemed to wash her face’s glow.
Beyond the wind, I hear her phoenix pendants,
at heaven’s edge, I recall her phoenix carriage.
Not meeting the immortal’s descent,
I vainly dust the mirror’s grime.

**Duan Guyan, Censor, Yan native, *Continuing a Dream***
Step by step, the Eighteen Bends—
suddenly, I marvel at walking midair.
Today’s tracks follow the wheeling clouds,
yesteryear’s dreams stir old emotions.
Pines arch in a sky of jade,
grasses grow lush in ten thousand ravines.
*These lines were composed in a dream in the gengzi year.*
The mountain spirit does not favor me—
yet surely it will honor this pact.

**Jiang Lianghan, Minister of Personnel, Jinhua native, *Rhapsody on Mount Tai***
Mount Tai surges like a sail in mid-heaven,
its rugged vastness spanning the divine land for thousands of *li*.
The Black Road winds in sixty-six bends,
the Dragon Tower coils in three thousand terraces.
Rumbling, it rises through lingering mist,
a brocade screen of flying waterfalls woven in silk.
I scale sheer cliffs to pluck white jade elms,
peer down from hanging crags at green snail-shell peaks.
Yet more wondrous is the Sunrise Peak’s east—
Fusang’s misty waves stretch into the distance.
Rosy clouds ripple like crimson cinnabar,
the dawn sun blazes on green lotus.
Penglai’s isles dot the jeweled mat,
the Bohai Sea seems but a floating goblet.
Midair, I forget the stars’ remoteness,
striding the formless, I chase the primal chaos.
Suddenly, thunder shakes the mountain’s base,
lightning streaks, stars race, shaking forests and valleys.
In an instant, the sun sets, the cosmos tilts,
ten thousand acres of wind and waves—ghosts and gods weep.
Clouds obscure the perilous path, unclimbable,
each step, each turn, I fear my axle will snap.

**What peak of Mount Tai greets the dawn?**
Towering, it stands distant and remote.
Qin’s palaces, Han’s banners—mist and clouds drift,
heroes gone, their splendor faded,
only broken steles and scattered bamboo slips remain.
I come from north of Kunlun,
seeking the southern pole among the Three Mountains.

Unbidden, I slip and fall into the imperial capital,
longing to return yet lingering—endless sighs.
There are those who stack stones on Green City,
eating sesame rice as their cinnabar furnaces grow cold.

In southern commanderies, moss chokes Zhuge’s hut,
on eastern peaks, vines overrun An’s retreat.
Azure cliffs pour forth the Silver River,
mountains plunge deep into trailing creepers.

By chance, I ascend the celestial steps through the sieve of war,
jade immortals and fairy maidens permit my passing.
Yet I cannot shake free from the gibbons’ bonds of return,
so I follow dancing sleeves and sing in spring’s harmony.

Mountains and rivers, the vast earth—all illusion in the end,
worldly affairs stretch on, how can they be resolved?
I walk the rows of lingzhi fields, a hundred thousand furrows,
resolved not to disappoint the elders of Shangshan.

Zha Bingyi, Prefect of the Heavenly Repository from Haining, ascends Mount Tai:
Towering, it pierces the purple heavens,
the Azure Emperor’s stars wheel into view.
Fragrant traces alone mark the sacred Confucian rites,
jade scrolls lie sealed in the Han-dynasty altar’s vault.

A thousand peaks bow to the northern pole,
clouds embrace the Yellow River as a single thread.
This above all was my lifelong sunflower resolve—
by night I seek the Sun-Watching Peak, leaning in restless vigil.

Meng Yang, Minister of Justice from Xinyang, ascends Mount Tai on the Double Ninth:
The winds of Mount Tai are fierce, unbearable,
and how much more so on this day of climbing.
Cups tilt, reflecting the twilight’s deepening hue,
hats tilt, nestling close to the Northern Dipper.

Over Lu’s plains, wind and clouds drift with the wild sun,
at Ji’s gate, wild geese and horses vanish into mist and frost.
Grand ambitions and noble deeds—all relics now,
cities and wilds alike lie desolate beneath the boundless sky.

Luo Hongxian, Zhuangyuan from Jishui, presents to Governor Zhu Zhenshan, Military Inspector of Shandong:
In spring’s radiance, jade trees adorn the vermilion court,
as the Jade Axe ascends the terrace, the Dipper’s stars remain unseen.

At dawn’s approach, Mount Tai brims with light,
as winds sweep the Eastern Sea, leaving no dust nor gloom.
To live long, one need not relocate Qi’s grain—
still heard are odes praising Lu’s well-tended herds.

For governance, a pure order is essential;
would but a single word reach Lord Gai’s ear?

Xu Wentong, Policy Advisor from Yongkang, on Mount Tai’s Peak:
Purple qi surges skyward, shielding the Han capital,
mountains and rivers fade into mist—none can be seen.
Heaven and earth suddenly converge in the east,
while sun and moon return to support the Northern Pole.

Autumn hues linger in the migrant geese’s wings, touching the traveler’s temples,
a clear cup, sealed by rain, rests in the thatched hut.
From such heights, ask not of bygone dynasties—
the Emperor’s son never returned, leaving only the Great Master in vain.

Wang Shizhen, Vice Minister from Wu Commandery, ascends Mount Tai:
The vast expanse borders the ethereal hues of Mount Tai,
where fiery steps mark the boundary of azure haze.
Peaks and ravines intertwine in mutual embrace,
split rocks and trailing pine-moss hang suspended.

After rain, twin dragons vie within the jade gorge,
while a lone vulture, cleaving clouds, props up the blue sky.
I have long harbored lofty aspirations—
to know you, one must trace back to the primordial beginning.

Spirits soar, poised for flight,
as the opening and closing of yin and yang unfold.
A thousand cliffs suddenly reveal the Central Plains’ sun,
while in the sixth month, the imperial envoy’s frost endures.

Once, the Celestial Emperor sat in the Azure Palace,
now, the sacred precinct lies in the realm of white clouds.
Having traversed all Five Peaks,
I beg to taste the fire dates of Anqi.

Rushing cliffs cascade like thunder in sunlight,
as stone paths drive dragons to clear the way.
A bolt of silk unfurls from the Terrace of Heaven,
golden seals gleam as the Han envoys return from their rites.

Rivers, laden with rain, stretch like a thousand ribbons,
the sea’s hue trembles in the sky, no larger than a cup.
Speak not of royal qi at the sacred altar—
only in this mortal world does immortal talent reside.

I still recall when Qin pines detained the imperial carriage,
and to this day, wind and rain have not fully subsided.
The Heavenly Gate inverts, pouring the Milky Way’s waters,
while Sun-Watching Peak hangs upside down, a flowing sapphire sea.

Seeking to turn through a thousand coils, lost in the dense mist,
who can discern the nine points of Qi from afar?
Wherever one treads, the ruts of Xiangcheng remain—
gazing into the vast blue, sorrow arises unbidden.

I long to lie in coarse robes at Heaven’s Gate,
leaning on the railing at midnight, lost in thought.
Half the cosmos cradles me in embrace,
while stars hang low, nearly within reach.

Wildly, I call for the immortal’s dice,
thirsting to ask the Jade Maiden for three cups of wine.
They say Kunlun is even more wondrous—
I shall seek it from afar, tracing the river’s source.

Cliffs stand like lotus petals, timeless in view,
carved pines and cypresses coil around lofty bends.
The central peak’s emerald dwarfs Zulai’s hues,
while the summit’s blue gathers the cold of Jieshi.

Having composed the *Song of Liangfu*, I harmonize with myself;
the *Annals of Maoling* completed—who shall inscribe them?
If by chance there remains a trace of Wu’s fame,
I would ask the autumn winds about wings.

Li Song, Vice Envoy from Guide, humbly follows in the ascent:
The imperial envoy climbs the Terrace of the Great One,
clouds part to reveal the Han court’s attire.
Nine heavens stir, driving jackals and foxes far,
while in the sixth month, frost chills grass and trees.

From Sun-Watching Peak, the mortal world appears cramped,
but gazing north from Heaven’s Gate, the imperial court feels vast.
Only in inspecting the realm can one devise plans to aid the times—
I align my aspirations with the royal map and Tai’s peace.

Wang Lin, Minister from Beiping, on Jade Emperor’s Summit:
Ever sighing at the clamor of worldly dust,
with no way to escape its snare.
Only by scaling the highest peak
do I grasp the vastness of heaven and earth.

**Sun-Watching Peak**
Rippling, it cradles the golden crow,
at dawn, piercing the dark earth.
Would that my five-night vigil
could be witnessed by all under heaven.

**Han Enclosure Terrace**
Since ancient times, Mount Tai has stood,
while Emperor Wu’s glory now lies empty.
His phoenix carriage entered the western pass,
leaving moss to green the terrace’s stones.

**Jade Maiden Pool**
Born in the Yellow Emperor’s court,
her Dao matched the Heavenly Sister’s.
A sacred spring spills into the square pool,
as if jade pendants chimed faintly.

**Qin’s Broken Stele**
Hegemony flows like water,
grand designs vanish like clouds.
Who knew that after the embers cooled,
this culture would endure in ruins?

**Immortal’s Bridge**
A perilous bridge spans the abyss,
yet no immortal crosses it.
When shall they return from the sea?
Only leaving past admirers in vain.

**Sheer Cliff**
Since heaven and earth first opened,
who among men does not die?
What matters is not the self—
beneath the cliff, jackals and wolves prowl.

**White Cloud Cavern**
Creation’s spirit gathers here,
how deep does this cave descend?
No azure phoenix returns,
only white clouds drift away.

**Eighteen Bends**
From youth, I harbored lofty dreams,
now I climb the ladder to the clouds.
Once within Heaven’s Gate,
I look back—how low the green peaks seem.

**Five Great Men Pines**
The Emperor’s son never returned,
leaving the Great Men standing alone.
At dusk, the north wind howls,
as they weep toward Shaqiu.

Li Panlong, Surveillance Commissioner from Licheng, on Mount Tai:
Within the realm, the famed mountain is Mount Tai—
I turn eastward, yearning to follow.
At dawn, the river hangs like a thread from Heaven’s Gate,
while autumn’s high seas glow at Sun-Watching Peak.

Who now delves into the golden caskets of Han’s strategies?
For a thousand years, white clouds have guarded Qin’s seals.
Having lingered beyond the vines and creepers,
when autumn comes, the western wind tolls through ten thousand ravines.

**To Historian Yin Zhengfu on Ascending Mount Tai**
Of old, the Son of Heaven ascended the altar,
his imperial path graced by the Han court’s splendor.
The distant sea stirs the Three Terraces,
while spring’s chill lingers over the Five Pines.

White clouds suddenly emerge from the sacred enclosure,
but who now peers into the jade scrolls?
Today, the court gathers for the feng sacrifices—
when will Sima Xiangru return to Chang’an?

**Upper Palace**
Since what year has spring graced this place?
How many grotto-heavens lie within the divine chambers?
I carry the three sacred herbs in my satchel,
and once composed the *Four Sorrows* in my heart.

The Han’s ox-shooting traces remain,
while tethering horses at Wu’s gate seems long lost.
Of the seventy-two families debating rites,
upon returning, I shall present them to the Sage.

**Matching Prefect Wei’s Escort on Mount Tai**
The central sky cleaves open, revealing Heaven’s Gate,
where the Emperor’s towers stand in homage to the imperial grandson.
Five horses arrive together at Wu’s Terrace,
while all peaks defer to the Venerable One’s grandeur.

Qin pines briefly lend their verdant hues,
as the sea’s sun distantly gathers purple qi.
They say the Yellow River appears like a sash—
yet know that to the northwest lies Kunlun.

Li Xianfang, Vice Minister from Puzhou, on Mount Tai:
The Eighteen Bends rise high, cradling the imperial capital,
while Zulai and Liangfu vie for prominence.
The Divine Maiden visits beneath the moonlit toad,
as immortals converse at Mount Tai’s edge.

**Heavenly Cocks summon the sun to float above the Three Isles,**
**Sea cranes nest in pines, five trees in every grove.**
I long to draft Sima Xiangru’s *Fengshan Memorial*—
yet the Han altars and terraces lie long abandoned in weeds.

Atop the Supreme Peak stands the Jade Emperor’s shrine,
where clouds rise at Heaven’s Gate and staff and sandals slow.
Here once the Qin and Han performed their sacred rites—
still, jade-like grasses whisper doubts upon the stone.

The sun gnaws at the Three Observances’ gold and silver palaces,
while heaven pours the Milky Way into the Jade Maiden’s Pool.
At dawn, gazing into the void to spy the isles of the sea,
I see Fusang’s reflection drift within the waves.

---

**Wang Shaoyuan, Imperial Censor from Jinxixian, ascending Mount Tai**
Palaces of petals and towers of pearl rise steep and grand,
their gates leaning on azure skies, draped in emerald vines.
They lock mid-mountain, encircling sun and moon,
while the gaze spans a thousand leagues, girdled by rivers.

The Qin altars’ imperial *qi* soars in mystery,
as Han apocrypha’s golden script pierces the Great Harmony.
In this illustrious age, sage kings emulate Shun and Yu—
joyous that no *feng* memorials trouble the mountain’s folds.

---

**Sun Yingkui, Left Administration Commissioner from Yuyao, inspecting the renovation of the Tai Temple**
Step by step I ascend the lofty peak,
where ten thousand summits array the earth and white clouds run deep.
The Lute-Tuning Ravine pours the Milky Way’s waters,
while the Verdant Terrace parts the moonlit trees’ shade.

Gazing across the seas, all things stir in unison;
at the Central Terrace’s completion, both hearts inquire within.
When the sun’s chariot welcomes the long night’s end,
I lean alone on the heights, gazing toward Kong’s grove.

---

**Wei Lianggui, Surveillance Commissioner from Xinjian, reporting on his visit to Mount Tai**
Leaning on my staff, I seek the Jade Maiden’s Peak,
parting the clouds to glimpse the Azure Radiance Palace.
The mountain holds rain’s intent, its misty light stirring,
while the sun strikes Heaven’s Gate and purple *qi* thickens.

Sheer cliffs seem to preserve the Han’s traces,
but where to find the Qin’s seals among broken steles?
From this height, I raise my hand to move the Six Directions—
Confucius’ legacy lies plain before my eyes.

---

**Yang Zongqi, Surveillance Commissioner from Shaanxi, ascending Mount Tai**
Majestic Mount Tai anchors the east of Qi,
and today, as I ascend, heaven and earth feel boundless.
Westward, Hangu Pass and cloud-wreathed ridges stretch straight,
while eastward, the Bohai’s dawn glows crimson.

The Qin steles vanish into the void above the clouds,
as Lu’s halls stand uneven in my sight.
Now and then, recluses ride white deer,
riding the wind, poised to mount the azure heavens.

---

**Pei Shen, Assistant Education Commissioner from Puzhou, ascending Mount Tai**
Thirty-six bends—how steep their iron faces!
Yet at dawn’s climb, weariness forgets itself.
My eyes see the summit, doubting the path exists,
while my body, lost in clouds, remains unaware.

Are Qin’s five pines still here? Or mere relics?
Tang’s thousand-*ren* cliffs bear a worn stele.
Rise and fall through ages—only commonplace,
yet the golden tablets’ celestial script remains too strange.

---

**Wang Jiao, Assistant Commissioner from Huating, ascending Mount Tai**
What marvels lie in Mount Tai’s towering heights?
Thirty-six winding bends coil the path.
The golden crow bathes in the sea at midnight,
while peach trees by the thousand bloom beside the pool.

Qin pines and Han wutong shade the imperial tent,
as golden tablets and jade tablets linger by the scripture terrace.
In spring’s second month, I offer incense and bow—
a breeze, clear sunlight, and Heaven’s Gate swings wide.

---

**Mou Chaozong, Assistant Commissioner from Binzhou, ascending Mount Tai**
The Supreme Peak’s sheer majesty leans eastward,
its sacred registers and seals honoring solemn rites.
Qi and Lu’s lands, though remote, shape unique grandeur,
while through all ages, reverence remains the same.

Ruined terraces point to Qin emperors’ steles,
and secluded ravines coil with pines of Song palaces.
I long to trace its origins but scarcely grasp them—
so I entrust myself to the heights, riding the eternal wind.

---

**Zha Bingtie, Evaluating Officer from Haining, paying homage at Mount Tai**
Mount Tai’s stern cliffs have long been famed,
and today, I see them guarding the divine capital.
They guide the flow of canals and the Ji, linking like eels,
while presiding over cloudy pavilions, now paired as kin.

Timely rains spread the emperor’s grace at dawn,
as Fusang’s morning sun illumines all under heaven.
Who will grow wings upon their sides?
To soar to the peak’s summit and enter the Great Purity.

---

**Yu Xian, Policy Advisor from Wuxi, composing atop Mount Tai**
So remote it startles the heart—
through ages, it has been called the Supreme Peak.
Ditches divide the Wen’s waters,
while hollows overlook the clustered summits.

At times, a clear canopy catches the rain,
and windswept clouds stir the breast.
Heaven and earth converge in splendor,
as halls and terraces embrace the twilight’s glow.

With a glance, Qi and Lu shrink small,
while Zou and Lu regain their weight.
Abandoned steles mark the Qin’s traces,
and ruined times bear the Han’s footprints.

In reverence, I recall the *Book of Documents’* first lesson,
as my ascent nears the evening bell.
Fortunate to live in an age of self-governance,
I need not debate the eastern *feng* rites again.

---

**Zhao Xun, Assistant Administrator from Panyu, ascending Sunrise View**
The moonlit Daoist arrives from Lingyan,
and at midnight, I ascend the *fengshan* terrace again.
The Silver River spans the sky, gazing north at the Dipper,
while golden waves ripple, heralding the sun’s return.

The Fire Mountain appears yearly, burning the eastern sea,
as the sun’s chariot startles the terrace with sudden radiance.
Before the light reaches ten thousand leagues, auspicious *qi* appears—
crimson clouds surge, unfolding in the distance.

---

**Cao Jin, Vice Minister from Xiangfu, ascending Mount Tai**
After rain, the morning’s glow stills the mountain altar,
as a century’s gaze lingers on spring’s decline.
First passing the imperial tent at dawn’s Fanghu,
then entering Heaven’s Gate, where the cosmos feels vast.

A pair of flutes and pipes reach the jade palaces,
while I seek the *fengshan* rites, leaning on the cloud-wreathed slopes.
At the ancient jade terrace’s temple, the wine cup lingers late—
viewing bamboo, chanting in the wind, my mood remains unspent.

---

**Frosted banners rise into the emerald haze,**
**startlingly detached, as if severed from the world.**
A few clear chimes drift—from where?
Several idle clouds reflect upon the traveler’s robe.

The Jade Maiden’s Pool stirs with spring grasses,
while weary cranes nestle beside the rosy clouds.
Only mountain monks may dwell among these layered peaks—
let orioles and blossoms face the fading light alone.

---

**Qing Shouli, Prefect from Fenghua, ascending the mountain**
Through the grotto’s curtain, I change robes and enter the purple dawn,
where wind stirs the imperial tent and pines roar.
Heavenly cocks summon the sun to float above the Three Isles,
as sea cranes nest in pines, five trees in every grove.

I long to draft Sima Xiangru’s *Fengshan Memorial*—
yet the Han altars and terraces lie long abandoned in weeds.
Atop the Supreme Peak stands the Jade Emperor’s shrine,
where clouds rise at Heaven’s Gate and staff and sandals slow.

Here once the Qin and Han performed their sacred rites—
still, jade-like grasses whisper doubts upon the stone.
The sun gnaws at the Three Observances’ gold and silver palaces,
while heaven pours the Milky Way into the Jade Maiden’s Pool.

At dawn, gazing into the void to spy the isles of the sea,
I see Fusang’s reflection drift within the waves.

---

**Wang Shaoyuan, Imperial Censor from Jinxixian, ascending Mount Tai**
Palaces of petals and towers of pearl rise steep and grand,
their gates leaning on azure skies, draped in emerald vines.
They lock mid-mountain, encircling sun and moon,
while the gaze spans a thousand leagues, girdled by rivers.

The Qin altars’ imperial *qi* soars in mystery,
as Han apocrypha’s golden script pierces the Great Harmony.

In this enlightened age, sage kings are all like Shun and Yu—
joyful that no memorials of grievance reach the mountain’s folds.

**Sun Yingkui, Left Provincial Administration Commissioner from Yuyao, inspecting the repairs of the Dai Temple**
Step by step I ascend the lofty heights of Tai,
where ten thousand peaks array the earth and white clouds run deep.
The Lute-Tuning Stream pours the Milky Way’s waters,
while the Verdant Terrace divides the moonlit trees’ shade.
Gazing across the seas, all things stir in unison—
on the Central Terrace, two hearts question their place.
Yet when the sun’s chariot opens the long night,
I lean alone in the heights, gazing toward the Kong grove.

**Wei Lianggui, Surveillance Commissioner from Xinjian, on visiting Mount Tai**
Staff in hand, I seek the Jade Maiden Peak,
parting the clouds to glimpse the Azure Radiance Palace.
The mountain holds rain’s intent, its misty light stirring,
while the sun strikes the Heavenly Gate, deepening the purple *qi*.
A sheer cliff seems to preserve the Han’s traces,
but where among broken steles may one find the Qin’s seals?
From on high, I raise my hand to encompass the Six Directions—
Confucius’ legacy lies plain before my eyes.

**Yang Zongqi, Surveillance Commissioner from Shaanxi, ascending Mount Tai**
Majestic Mount Tai stands guard over Qi’s east—
today, as I ascend, heaven and earth seem void.
Westward, the Hangu Pass and cloud-wreathed ridges stretch straight,
while eastward, the Bohai’s dawn glows crimson.
The Qin steles vanish into the empyrean,
yet the halls of Lu stand scattered in view.
At times, a recluse rides a white deer,
borne on the wind, as if to mount the azure heavens.

**Pei Shen, Associate Education Commissioner from Puzhou, ascending Mount Tai**
Thirty-six hairpin turns—how iron-hard the climb,
yet at dawn’s ascent, weariness is forgotten.
Eyes scan the summit, doubting any path remains,
while the body, lost in clouds, knows not itself.
Are the Qin’s five pines still here?
A Tang-era stele, a thousand *ren* high, bears a polished inscription.
Rise and fall through the ages—mere commonplace,
yet the golden tablets in their jade casket seem too wondrous.

**Wang Jiao, Associate Commissioner from Huating, ascending Mount Tai**
What marvel is Mount Tai’s height?
Thirty-six winding turns coil and return.
The golden crow bathes at midnight in the sea’s depths,
while peach trees a thousand strong line the pool’s edge.
Qin pines and Han wutong shade the imperial tents,
golden tablets and jade tablets mark the scripture terraces.
In spring’s second month, I offer incense and bow—
a gentle breeze, a clear day, the Heavenly Gate opens.

**Mou Chaozong, Associate Commissioner from Binzhou, ascending Mount Tai**
The sacred peak of Dai rears steep in the eastern sky,
its register of imperial seals steeped in solemn rites.
Though Qi and Lu’s lands lie remote, their form is peerless—
through all ages, men’s reverence remains the same.
A ruined terrace points to the First Emperor’s stele,
while deep ravines cradle the Song emperors’ palace pines.
I would trace its origins, yet know not where to begin—
so I entrust myself to the heights, riding the endless wind.

**Zha Bingtie, Evaluator from Haining, visiting Mount Tai**
Mount Tai’s stern crags have long been renowned—
today, I see how they guard the divine capital.
The Grand Canal’s waters link like bream in season,
while the Cloud Pavilion stands near, newly adorned.
Morning rains spread the emperor’s grace far and wide,
as the Fusang sun bathes the world in dawn’s light.
Who could grow wings upon both arms
and fly to the peak’s summit, entering the Great Purity?

**Yu Xian, Assistant Administration Commissioner from Wuxi, composing atop Mount Tai**
So remote it strikes awe in men’s hearts—
through the ages, it has been called the Sacred Peak.
The Wen River’s channels divide its slopes,
while valleys cradle the clustered summits.
At times, a sunshade is touched by rain,
or winds and clouds surge through one’s breast.
Heaven and earth converge in grandeur,
as halls and terraces rise in stately grace.
With a glance, Qi and Lu seem small,
yet turning back, Zou and Lu weigh heavy.
Abandoned steles bear the Qin’s traces,
while ruined altars mark the Han’s passing.
In reverence, I recall the lesson of the first robe,
as my ascent nears the evening bell.
Fortunate to live in an age of self-governance,
I need not debate the rites of eastern homage.

**Zhao Xun, Assistant Administration Commissioner from Panyu, ascending Sunrise Peak**
The moonlit Daoist comes from Lingyan,
climbing again at midnight to the Feng and Shan altars.
The Silver River hangs mid-heaven, the Dipper to the north,
while golden waves reflect the returning sun.
The Fire Mountain appears yearly, burning the eastern sea,
as the sun’s chariot suddenly gleams atop the terrace.
Before the light reaches ten thousand *li*,
crimson clouds surge, unfolding in the distance.

**Cao Jin, Vice Minister from Xiangfu, ascending Mount Tai**
After rain, the morning’s glow stills the sacred altar—
a century’s end, this springtime vista is mine.
First passing the imperial tents at dawn’s hour,
then entering the Heavenly Gate, the cosmos expands.
A pair of flutes and pipes reach the jade palaces,
as I seek the Feng and Shan rites, leaning on the cloud-wreathed slopes.
At dusk in the jade terrace’s ancient temple,
I watch the bamboo, chant in the wind, my spirit unspent.

Amid frost’s purity, I sit on emerald slopes,
suddenly adrift, as if estranged from the world.
From where do those clear chimes drift?
A few idle clouds mirror the traveler’s robe.
The Jade Maiden’s Pool stirs with spring grasses,
while weary cranes nestle beside the rosy clouds.
Layered peaks permit only mountain monks to dwell—
let orioles and blossoms face the fading light.

**Qing Shouli, Prefect from Fenghua, ascending the mountain**
Through the curtained grotto, I change robes and enter the purple clouds,
where wind stirs the imperial tents into a roar of pines.
The mountain stair descends in the slanting sun, overlooking the high spring,
while a stone ravine’s spring waters chime in jade-green tones.
The imperial progress’s green banners are met by bowing pines,
and the bright era’s traces are sealed in jade.
Sweeping clouds, I sit beneath the front peak’s moon,
while monks, braving rain, descend to the world’s bell.
A wanderer’s heart finds momentary ease—
might I meet a flying immortal, jade pendants chiming?

**Yin Pan, from Jinan, at Sunrise Peak**
Eastward, the land of Fusang,
where boundless seas churn.
Waves toss purple *qi*,
isles scatter crimson clouds.
The Silver River’s stars still gleam,
as heaven and earth divide the day.
Here, where the celestial writ was bestowed,
only the Jieshi stones stand apart.

**Xu Lin, Transport Commissioner from Huating, ascending Mount Tai**
Arduously I climb Mount Tai,
a long whistle stirring endless thoughts.
The Yellow River’s sash seems slender,
while the sea’s hue floats like a cup.
Incense from Qin trees curls,
as Han terraces bear autumn’s weight.
How might one shed the world’s dust
and ever roam with the sunlit deer?

**Zhu Mingshi, from Huating, ascending Mount Tai**
Mount Tai’s first peak to ascend—
the mountain’s spirit shines in purple hibiscus grace.
Ancient steles still bear the First Emperor’s traces,
while imperial carriages once bore the Han emperors’ tread.
The winding Heavenly Gate veils in mist,
as Sunrise Peak’s crags bristle with dense haze.
I pray to gain Sima Xiangru’s skill,
daring to claim my talent fits to draft the Feng and Shan rites.

**Records of Mount Tai, Volume Seventeen: Accounts of Ascents**
From the *jia-yin* year of the Jiajing reign onward, the poems of various eminent officials and scholars follow the old gazetteer’s order, arranged by generation.

**Li Chunfang, Grand Secretary from Xinghua in Yangzhou, ascending Mount Tai on a summer day, rejoicing in the rain’s clearing**

**Gao Gong, Grand Secretary from Xinzheng, ascending Mount Tai**
Through boundless skies my troubled heart unfurls,
where suddenly the Azure Emperor rides the rainbow’s curve.
Half-veiled in mist, the rainbow’s bay unfolds,
as clearing winds sweep Dragon Vale with dawn’s pure gold.
Through ages past, heroic dreams in sunset glow,
while heaven and earth’s fresh life sprouts midst the young green row.
The Sacred Peak abounds in royal grace,
its timely rains and sun the virtue’s work embrace.

---

**Gao Yi, Grand Secretary from Qiantang, ascending Mount Tai**
Of all the peaks so fair, none match the Sacred Peak,
where distant Heaven’s Gate ascends to hibiscus sleek.
The imperial path still winds where horses turned,
yet no inscribed stone marks the First Emperor’s yearned.
Star-laden skies hang low o’er Jade Emperor’s hall,
while Ageless Peak stands firm through time’s unending thrall.
At midnight’s end, the crimson sun from seas will rise—
how many layers lie to Penglai’s paradise?

---

**Wu Yue, Minister of War from Wenshang, ascending Mount Tai**
Crag upon crag soars high to pierce the azure dome,
where deep ravines and cliffs in misty veils entwine.
From hanging cliffs, cold springs in torrents gleam,
while autumn trees that brush the clouds blush red with rime.
The pines of Qin still sing on stones with dragon scales,
as Han’s mossed steles fade where ravens’ scripts grow pale.
At summit’s height, my robes I shake, lost in thought’s vast sea,
then glimpse the dawn’s first light where chaos first took form.

---

**Cloud Steps Newly Hung**
New-hung cloud steps wind through emerald cliffs,
where pine boughs brush the purple rocks apart.
Through misty peaks, the path of crows winds far,
as sheep-track turns bring winds through vales that sigh.
The earth meets heaven’s vault where Dipper gleams,
my gaze follows the dawn to Penglai’s dreams.
This fleeting journey wakes the floating life—
I’d gladly leave the world to rest on mossed stone rife.

---

**Visiting the Azure Emperor’s Temple**
Temple gates and halls in autumn clouds so fine,
the Azure Emperor’s palace blends with village line.
From empty vales, voices drift on jade-green walls,
while horses’ shadows fall on crimson stairway’s calls.
I trace the hidden altars where immortals trod,
then wander deep in woods where wild paths nod.
This pure delight fulfills my secluded quest,
as I seek a stone cell to share with monks at rest.

---

**Liu Ziqiang, Minister of War from Fugou, ascending Mount Tai**
Vast and hazy, the azure sea embraces half the mountain’s frame,
each step up the sky’s sheer wall brings toil and strain.
I feel the winds and clouds rise at my feet,
then doubt if I’ve escaped the mortal plane.
My temples in the mirror startle me—age’s trace,
while courtly cares still chain me to this place.
For now, I pause my dusty steps to follow Xie’s tread,
and seek the immortal’s gate in Penglai’s cave instead.

---

**Zhu Heng, Minister of War from Yuzhang, ascending Mount Tai**
Winding stairs and spiral paths stretch far to heaven’s height,
where clouds and mist soak robes in midair flight.
The golden halls and silver courts draw near,
as orioles sing sweet and flowers scent the sphere.
The Jade Void’s palace stands in lonely grace,
where midnight’s wonders call me to retrace.
A distant crane’s cry rides the moon’s pale beam,
while white clouds near the sands in level gleam.

---

**Ma Sen, Minister of War from Fujian, ascending Mount Tai**
Of all Five Peaks, the Sacred Peak stands lone,
where layered peaks and trees in emerald depths are sown.
The winding stone steps lead to Heaven’s Gate,
while misty clouds and dawn adorn Sunrise’s height.
Its mighty sway was marked in Shun’s ancient tome,
yet why recount the Qin’s vain seals of stone?
The endless longing that high mountains bring—
Confucius’ footsteps here still cling.

---

**Lodging at a Daoist Abode on the Summit**
Beside the Azure Clouds’ shrine, a humble cell,
where mountains beyond clouds seem void and swell.
The Jade Maiden’s pool holds waters pure and bright,
while Ageless Peak’s snows gleam in scattered light.
Seated, I watch the floating mists transform,
then wake to find the true and still more warm.
At midnight’s hour, the boundless realm is hue-less,
as moonlight spills upon the steps so flawless.

---

**Yin Tai, Minister of War from Yongqing, gazing at the Peak from the Dongping Road**
This mighty peak commands the eastern land,
its lofty heights obstruct the starry band.
From chaos first, it marked the earth’s embrace,
its towering might defies the heavenly space.
In Yu’s grand tour, its omens first were shown,
while Xia’s records carved its name in stone.
Nearby, immortals left their traces bright,
yet none may linger long in rock-hewn light.
Its sacred deeds are chronicled of old—
seventy-two kings’ tales the annals hold.
How vast this mountain’s legacy unfurled,
how desolate the chapters of the world!
The mists obscure the Qin’s far-distant reign,
while clouds recall the Han’s enduring chain.
I ask of things that once were here—
they say the pines and catalpas still appear.
The wild expanse cradles the spring’s embrace,
while peaks in haze fade into distant space.
At dawn, the hibiscus blooms in morning’s glow,
its beauty fit to feast the eye below.
By night, the moon flows o’er the golden hall,
at dawn, the flowers grace the altar’s wall.
Who shares the cloud-borne chariot’s flight?
I lift my head and sigh in longing’s plight.
Since youth, I’ve cherished seclusion’s call,
and longed to wander every sacred hall.
The *Liangfu* hymns still echo in my ear,
as I recall the *Taishan* songs held dear.
The joys of Qiu’s retreat still tempt my heart,
as Penglai’s isles stir thoughts of Anqi’s art.
Though narrow paths crisscross the land so wide,
this place alone invites my cap aside.
The long winds lift my feathered sleeves to soar—
I long to scale the Heaven’s Gate once more.
Upon the Ageless Stone my sandals leap,
by Jade Maiden’s Pool my robes I steep.
Heaven and earth in cycles open wide,
as sun and moon in dawn and dusk abide.
I’d seek the Hermit of the Nest to share,
but deep emotions cannot find compare.
The Sacred Peak’s hues stretch a thousand *li*,
where Lu’s plains meet Qi’s and Jiaodong’s sea.
The sun at Fusang’s shore draws near,
while Ruomu’s boughs bow low to heaven’s sphere.
The Eastern Emperor’s robes I’d grasp in hand,
the Northern Dipper’s handle lift as planned.
I raise my hand to summon the immortal’s song,
