as dawn’s first cockcrow rings from Azure Clouds’ throng.

---

**The Sacred Peak**
The sacred peak stands towering in the skies,
its radiant halls illumine the Eastern Lord’s guise.
Qin’s pines and Han’s cypresses entwine the land,
while jade tablets and golden caskets record the kings’ command.
A single pillar props the sky where dragons tread,
three peaks surge like the phoenix’s flight o’er ocean’s spread.
I lift my gaze and marvel at the clouds’ art,
as spring’s soft mists embrace the palace’s heart.

---

**Yang Wei, Minister of War from Haideng, ascending the Eastern Peak en route to the Southern Capital**
I rein my horse to climb the Eastern Peak,
from lofty heights, the four horizons seek.
At last I know the mortal world is small,
while this great mountain stands eternal, tall.
The watchtowers rise in autumn’s lonely might,
as rivers and plains fade in day’s dim light.
I’d seek Sun Fu’s secluded retreat,
then forget the pressing journey’s heat.
The name of Liangfu still resounds,
while Feng and Shan rites stand unbound.
I meet the locals, trace the ancient ground,
then long to sing in rapture’s sound.
The Wu Gate’s silk-like waters near,
while Han’s grand steles still appear.
I stretch my aged eyes to see afar—
the boundless waves of the azure sea.

---

**Zhang Jiaying, Minister of War from Tongliang, ascending Mount Tai**
Spiral steps coil like heaven’s endless stair,
where clouds and mist soak robes in midair.
The golden palaces draw near,
as orioles sing sweet and flowers scent the sphere.
The Jade Void’s halls stand lone in splendor’s glow,
where midnight’s wonders call me to bestow.
A distant crane’s cry rides the moon’s pale beam,
while white clouds near the sands in level gleam.

Zhang Heng once penned his *Four Sorrows*,
now I gaze eastward, joining him in this hour.
Emerald cliffs spiral with autumn’s turn,
crimson stairs hang like a thread from heaven’s bower.

By chance I pluck a jade casket—divine script within,
scarlet pennants soar where the Jade Maiden’s shrine begins.
My satchel holds the map of Five Peaks’ form,
their true shapes faintly glimpsed by earth’s spirit’s storm.

Cold dew drips on lotus blooms in the azure chill,
I lean on my cheek, resting at Heaven’s Gate on Tai’s high hill.
Han grass still bears Sima’s brushstroke trace,
Qin’s palace lingers where the Grand Master’s pines embrace.

Three temples rise in uneven tiers, my eyes grow weary,
a thousand crags’ lore demands a staff so airy.
Though I’ve sought all famed peaks within the mortal sphere,
only in late years do I meet the Venerable Peak so near.

The celestial cock crows—dawn soon parts the night,
my sword at the summit gleams with tenfold light.
The mountain’s sigh stirs the white waters below,
as crimson clouds ascend where the eastern sea’s glow.

My body enfolds three thousand fathoms of mist,
seventy sovereigns’ *Feng-Shan* texts I’ve assisted.
Why then does my robe bear five hues so bright?
For the mountain’s *qi* has ever been rich and light.

Sun and moon hang suspended from Tai’s crown,
each drawn to the imperial throne’s azure gown.
Qin’s steles jut into the blue heavens’ height,
while fairy isles fade in the vast sea’s light.

My gaze lingers on Wu Park’s steeds so fine,
I bend to discern the fields of Wen’s design.
Though I’ve lost my carriage in Xiang’s ruined town,
still I escape the dust of the marketplace’s frown.

---

**Chen Jingbang, Minister of War from Putian, resting by White Dragon Pool**
A hundred-foot pool, icy and deep, cradles jade peaks,
where the dragon’s spirit once stirred these sacred leaks.
Now Qi and Lu’s greenery fades to a trace,
when will clouds rise to soothe the farmers’ plight and grace?

---

**Ascending Mount Tai**
Of all earth’s peaks, this one stands supreme,
through ages past, its grandeur none dare deem.
Half its slopes bathed in sun, half in shade,
twin peaks where sun and moon their courses wade.

Since ancient times, the Queen Mother’s jade pool gleams,
when did the Golden Gate welcome the imperial dreams?
I hear of elixirs that grant long life’s span—
would that I could present ten thousand scrolls to the Yellow Lord’s plan!

---

Heaven’s Gate, ethereal, crowns the myriad peaks,
each step upward deepens the verdant steep.
No lone crow soars where the azure vaults hang,
but five pines clasp the cold torrents’ clang.

For ages, the spring hunt’s rites lie unfulfilled,
yet daytime clouds still rise where Han’s seals were sealed.
Where do the divine halls and towering pavilions hide?
I long to ask Anqi, if but to confide.

---

Grasping the heights, the mountain’s might I survey,
heaven and earth shrink to a primal spray.
Beyond the shimmering dots of Qi’s domain,
Lu’s hills fade in the setting sun’s soft reign.

The Yellow River winds endlessly below,
three fairy peaks surge and vanish like snow.
Yet I fail to grasp Confucius’ intent—
can I claim kinship with his dances, joyful and bent?

---

Leaning on my staff, I knock at the Emperor’s Gate,
shaking my robes, I chant, the world grown strait.
My eyes sweep the vastness of three thousand lands,
my body stands on Kunlun’s foremost strand.

How many have witnessed the seas turn to mulberry fields?
While the immortals of Penglai ever upward yield.
Youth and age pass in a fleeting breath,
turning back, even fame seems a tranquil death.

---

**Accompanying Prefects Zhang and Jiao on a weary pilgrimage to the Stone Classics Gorge**
Our quest for hidden wonders left incomplete,
we join hands once more on this journey sweet.
Who carved these classics with steadfast hand?
By candlelight, old friends’ kindness we understand.

Evening’s veil gathers in the forest’s haze,
spring springs murmur over stone’s maze.
High mountains and flowing waters—ah, the strain,
as if I hear the echoes of ancient refrain.

---

**Lu Guangzu, Minister of War from Pinghu, seeking leave to return east—spring ascent of Mount Tai**
With sleeves swept clean, I compose a distant roam,
Tai’s splendor stirs my Wu-honed poem.
Spring winds, flowers, birds greet the Morning Sun Cave,
dawn’s mist and rosy clouds the Queen Mother’s pavilion pave.

The imperial tent once graced the emperor’s ride,
the Hall of Light’s traces stir thoughts wide.
My heart, boundless in its quest for the rare and old,
yet my homeland’s white silk fills me with longing untold.

---

**Zhu Dasu, Number One Scholar from Shanyin, ascending Mount Tai**
At the Azure Clouds Palace, the loftiest height,
where Qin and Han’s altar mounds lie deep in the night.
The setting sun casts a desolate glow,
fleeting clouds drift past shadows below.

I sigh at the fleeting schemes of mortal kings,
doubt if autumn winds ever regret their stings.
Alone I tread the level terrace’s vast expanse,
a single clear chime rises from the clouded trance.

---

Spring’s warmth spreads in harmony far and wide,
as I recall my visit to the Azure Lord’s abode.
Wild hues shift with the mist’s caprice,
mountain light swells though no rain has kissed.

To the southeast, white silk blurs the sky’s edge,
to the northwest, crimson clouds surge and pledge.
Yet I marvel at the five pines’ lingering green,
their late verdure mirrored in the stone screen’s sheen.

---

**Wang Honghui, Vice Minister from Meinan, chanting of Mount Tai**
I seek the Azure Lord to ask the Way’s true source,
an immortal invites me to ascend Heaven’s course.
Where does Heaven’s Gate soar so high?
Beyond the Sun Pool’s north, Tai’s plateau nigh.

Stone steps coil in eighteen winding bands,
cloud roots stretch nine hundred leagues across the lands.
Who first carved this chaos into form?
When yin and yang split, the Five Peaks took form.

The Emperor sent Tai Hao to fix this realm,
a towering pillar to guard the vast and calm.
Grotto heavens and blessed lands lean on its might,
layered skies where lotus blooms unfold in light.

The Yellow River a sash, the Bohai a cup,
at midnight, dawn’s sun appears in a flash.
Qi’s nine dots, faint in the mist’s embrace,
Wu’s white silk startles the eye’s chase.

Alas! Tai’s height knows no bound,
to climb it is to ride the wind, beyond the dust’s ground.
Of the seventy-two who sealed this peak,
Yu, Zhou, Qin, Han—only their names speak.

Since then, the rite has faded from sight,
gold seals and jade tallies lost to time’s blight.
Where now are those who sought the Way?
Even trees cannot mark their stay,
nor steles record their day.

Only the fleeting clouds before the cliffs,
whispering the rise and fall of a thousand years’ gifts.
Endless pasts I cannot fully tell,
I shake my robes and greet the immortals well.

From afar, the Jade Maiden’s pool exhales sweet scent,
the Immortal’s Cave swirls with *qi* heaven-sent.
Rainbow banners and scarlet pennants intertwine,
said to be the Jade Emperor’s Azure Cloud Divine.

Purification halls and prayers for blessings rise,
maiden flutes and River Lord’s drumming vie.
Sacred fungi bring their gifts of grace,
though unseen, I wander in blissful space.

By my side, a Black Crow Messenger appeared,
bestowing upon me the *Scripture of the Yellow Court*.
I perused it yet grasped little—
in a flash, it vanished into the void.

My lingering wonder at these wondrous sights knows no end,
while the dust of the world’s affairs clings to my palms, unceasing.
When may I bathe my hair and wander here again,
turning back to bid farewell to the carefree ones?

**Ascending Mount Tai**
Stone steps and cinnabar ladders lead to the Purple Palace,
among the Five Peaks of the realm, none rivals its majesty.
Seventy *feng* and *shan* rites echo through ancient ages,
three thousand kalpas stretch into the void’s expanse.
Pines, ancient still, hold the rains of Qin’s time,
peach groves, deep, evoke the winds of Jin’s men.
Seeking the hidden, I reach Penglai’s summit—
the world’s wonders stir boundless delight.

At the peak’s lofty heights, the Lord of Heaven reigns,
the *qi* of kingship over the Central Plains bows to the southeast.
White clouds coil ‘round a thousand converging peaks,
emerald crags, sheer, send ten thousand ravines rushing.
At dawn, the Golden Crow surges from the Eastern Sea’s mirage,
at dusk, jade cranes pierce the clouds to pass Cloud Gate.
Speaking of heaven, one need not mock Zou Yan’s wild claims—
ninefold winds truly bear one aloft.

In this world, indeed, Penglai’s isles exist,
let me wander here in carefree ease.
Jade tallies and golden caskets lie desolate,
while jade flowers and coral grasses bloom through spring and autumn.
The Oxherd’s shot needs no scholar’s debate,
the Horse’s trace may be sought in sacred marks.
Since the *Grand Vision* faded from these old eyes,
I point out the sights of Qi as if they were commonplace.

**Ode to the Venerable Man Peak**
Towering high, it stands alone before Heaven’s Gate,
its majestic form commands reverence.
Of the Five Peaks, Mount Tai is eldest—
all other summits must be its descendants.

**Ode to Sunrise Peak**
Before the peak at the fifth watch, dawn’s hues arise,
a dim glow first emerges east of the sea.
Who lends a crimson hand to aid the Sun’s chariot,
early to illuminate the Nine Provinces?

**Ode to the Jade Emperor’s Summit**
Ethereal cinnabar steps ascend through ninefold heavens,
here the Jade Emperor conceals his sacred traces.
Seeking truth, I climb straight to the Court of Primordial Dawn—
my body now rests on Penglai’s foremost peak.

**Ode to Master Lü’s Grotto**
A green serpent brushes his sleeve, *qi* brimming with autumn’s might,
inscriptions in the dark cave may be left at will.
Do not say the red dust’s folk seldom recognize him—
beyond the pines, Hua Prefecture looms faintly.

**Ode to the Minister Pine**
Two dynasties’ rivers and mountains have shifted,
yet its five branches still rise as when first enfeoffed.
Proud and towering, it must blush at the stain of an empty name,
leaving sighs for the four purple mushrooms of Shang’s crags.

**Ode to Peach Blossom Vale**
Flowing waters hang like rainbows in the sunlit ravine,
peach blossoms in spring rival those of Wuling’s stream.
I imagine myself following the Queen Mother of the East—
even without a fisherman’s guide, the path remains clear.

**Song of the Leap-of-Faith Cliff**
*Preface:* Ascending the Leap-of-Faith Cliff, I dreamed at night of a divine being who lamented the folly of common folk leaping to their deaths. I was commanded to stop them. Having reported this to the authorities for prohibition, I now compose this poem—its words plain and easily understood—to save countless innocent lives.

Life is truly hard—why seek death in joy?
A child wishing to repay parents must think of them first.
If the aged lack support in their final years,
this is great unfiliality, a defiance of heaven’s principle.
Some, in despair, pray for a better next life,
hoping to join the Buddha’s lotus assembly.
Wealth and honor bring many sorrows; joy is but suffering—
only those who see through the body’s illusions ascend to truth.
From a thousand-fathom height, a single leap like a bird’s fall,
flesh turns to mud, the soul drifts into oblivion.
A woman’s fame on the Wind-Cleansing Cliff brings shame,
a man’s lost soul at Heaven’s Bounty Pavilion is no glory.
The Azure Lord of the Eastern Peak cherishes life—
who dares deceive the gods with such inventions?
Riding clouds, clinging to delusions, they lead each other astray,
through a thousand autumns and ten thousand ages, preying on the foolish.
Now I sing this song to warn those who come after—
the dream’s message from the divine is no lie.
Weigh life against Mount Tai, light as a feather—
cherish this body, do not cast it away.

**Encountering Rain While Approaching the Peak**
Misty, chilly clouds darken the green peaks,
pine vines and rocky ravines deepen in verdant hue.
The mountain spirits test the joy of ascent—
morning rain steels my resolve to press on or stay.

**Ascending the Peak**
A thousand-fathom cinnabar ladder hides amid creeping fig,
layered skies rise in towering majesty.
Ancient pines echo crane cries through misty clouds,
the upper grotto’s dragon hoard stirs with wind and rain.
The Golden Horse’s fate may yet be reversed,
but what news of the Rainbow Phoenix?
Mists shift and change beyond past or present—
I linger, time fleeting like a swift shuttle.

**Passing Great Dragon Gorge**
Floating clouds stretch a thousand miles, weaving autumn’s gloom,
a thousand-fathom waterfall leaps through distant forests.
I often marvel at how wind and rain rush upon climbers—
the lotus casket holds a dragon’s roar.

**Record of Ascending the Sacred Peak**
A Daoist’s bearing holds mist and rosy clouds in his bones,
a myriad burdens dissolved—he loves only the mountains.
The red cord of office long bound him to the world’s edge,
but one visit to Penglai’s isles brings a smile.
Qin’s seals and Han’s sacrifices—ancient steles remain,
autumn grasses and spring robes idle in this immortal realm.
The Five Peaks’ pilgrimage begins here in this life—
I urge the lingzhi to age me among the white clouds.

**Dawn’s Clear Skies at the Peak’s Lodge**
A night of wind contends with misty veils,
stars and constellations gleam by the eaves like purple asters.
From a thousand-fathom height, I shake my robes beneath the vast sky—
a host of peaks arrayed, vying in the dawn’s glow.

**Ascending Sunrise Peak**
Misty fog veils the sea’s hues in murky vastness,
a single thread of dawn breaks through the verdant east.
Who lends a crimson hand to steady the Sun’s chariot,
early to illuminate the world below?

**Gazing from the Jade Emperor’s Summit**
Ethereal cinnabar steps ascend through ninefold heavens,
here the Jade Emperor conceals his sacred traces.
Seeking truth, I climb straight to the Court of Primordial Dawn—
my body now rests on Penglai’s foremost peak.

**Passing the Scripture Rock of the Tang Monk**
Amid jagged rocks, tigers and leopards crouch,
in the gurgling stream’s depths, dragons and serpents hide.
How many secluded and wondrous places exist in the world—
yet the red dust ever obscures them before our eyes.

**Five-Character Ancient Verse by Attendant Gentleman He Yuan of Jiangxi**
Soaring above a thousand winding paths,
climbing perilous ladders of ten thousand fathoms.
Gazing upward, the boundless expanse—
as if brushing the very heavens.

**Gazing from the Summit of Sun-Viewing Peak**

Only vastness meets the eye—so boundless, so wide,
the very forms of law lie low beneath my gaze.
Halfway up the mountain, a pair of crows spread wings,
while everywhere, how many pines stretch forth their boughs?
The lotus cliffs stand carved as if by skillful craft,
while tigers and leopards race through filth and foulness.
Beyond the waterfall, the dragon rests secure;
in jade gardens, the crane returns at dusk’s delay.

Palaces and towers rise in distant, staggered heights,
while stars near and far diverge in their celestial paths.
White clouds rise from every earthly place,
and purple qi fades into the setting sun’s haze.
The sky-bridge to Heaven’s Gate is perilous indeed,
as layered cliffs resound with ironstone’s song.
Though autumn has not come, the chill already freshens;
though night has not fallen, moonlight streams with radiance.

This floating life drifts without bound—
do mountains and rivers not know it too?
Lofty and steadfast, I follow Master Lu’s Dao,
like a jade wall, I gaze up at Zou’s noble bearing.
The Yu sacrifices first began at Mount Tai,
while Qin’s seals left steles scattered in vain.
Ascending here stirs many a sigh—
I but shake my robes and stand alone.

---

**Gazing at the Sea from Sun-Viewing Peak**

Braving the cold, I climb and gaze with unrestrained delight,
welcoming dawn’s glow as I sit where the fire burns bright.
Rosy hues blaze with dazzling splendor,
the sun’s essence glows red, as if aflame.
The Fusang wheel turns in sudden motion,
at heaven’s edge, the sea begins its tide.
Undulating golden waves surge and seethe,
yet still the mirrored reflection trembles faint.
As darkness rises across the ten thousand lands,
this place alone is first to receive the light.
Not yet yielding to Xihe’s reins,
I pity only Kuafu’s futile toil.
The heavens’ course moves swiftly in its rounds—
at midday, the great brightness reigns supreme.
The yang force now waxes in its season,
as we meet the dawn of Tai’s beginning.
What prayer may this humble servant offer?
The sea-sun presents its auspicious omen.

---

**Inscription by Attendant Gentleman Yu Shenxing of Dong’e on Ascending Mount Tai**

Since ancient times, this famed mountain has anchored the great East,
ever gazing from cloud and river toward its towering heights.
A thousand peaks flicker between light and shadow, high and low,
while ten thousand valleys shift through clear and clouded qi, lush and dense.
The stars’ earth revolves as the primal transformation turns,
while immortal groves wind round, where a hundred spirits commune.
Truly roaming the Five Peaks, I shall traverse them all—
first treading mist and vine to ascend the azure sky.

Jade towers and crimson pavilions crown the ten-thousand-fathom summit,
where the Six Dragons’ chariot path clings to steep and jagged cliffs.
Emerald steps wind through clouds,
while cascading red springs are glimpsed beyond the treetops.
The sea’s hues blur in dawn’s threefold gaze,
and autumn’s voice sighs cold through the Five Pines.
Heaven’s Gate lies but a footstep away—you should see it—
yet compared to the roads of the human world, it is harder still.

Suddenly emerging from the dusty realm, I compose a verse of grand roaming,
testing my sight to discern the nine points of the divine land.
Floating clouds rise straight to the peaks’ colors,
while the setting sun hangs long over ten thousand miles of autumn.
The Purple Barrier lies east, where the azure sea breaks,
the Yellow River rolls north through the vast wilderness.
Qin’s seals and Han’s sacrifices have crumbled to mounds of earth,
leaving endless sorrow for the world of men.

Leaning on my staff, I stand high above the ten thousand jade peaks,
where mist and vapor from the land-sea scatter like lotuses.
Half the cold sound falls as rain from the heavens,
while dusk’s hues hasten the bell’s toll from the valley’s depths.
Who now seeks the golden tablets of Qin’s imperial decrees?
White clouds still rise where Han’s seals once stood.
Behold the lands of twelve marquises and kings—
which of them could emerge from the divine palace’s innermost chambers?

At the summit, autumn’s heights house the Emperor’s palace,
where a single vast qi looms over the mortal realm below.
The earth’s basin holds the He and Ji rivers, three provinces’ end,
while the sky embraces Qin and Wu, ten thousand miles of void.
Jade towers’ light connects to the stars above,
cinnabar peaks’ shadows fall east of the sea gate.
I know the true Lord grants much favor—
permitting even the two sword heroes to lean on the rosy clouds.

On the ten-thousand-fathom jade altar, evening incense drifts,
while beside the Dipper, the thirty-six heavens divide.
The immortals’ grotto-palaces hang like twin gates,
the jade maidens’ divine chambers touch the jade clouds.
Visitors sigh the Liangfu lament,
while court poets do not draft Maoling’s texts.
The Eastern Emperor once held the records of all life,
while the sea-bound land and rivers adorn the sagely lord.

Gazing east from the three peaks—how majestic indeed!
The sea’s colors stretch far, opening ten thousand miles.
The Three Isles’ spring waves cradle sun and moon,
while the Five Cities’ immortal qi exhales towers and terraces.
At the wine cup’s edge, shadows drink in gold and silver’s dance,
while beneath the staff, clouds fly in purple and emerald hues.
The misty waters stretch on—Xu Fu has departed,
and to this day, no letter of return has come.

---

**Night on the Terrace**

The night’s colors shimmer, vast and boundless,
as the moon traverses the layered heavens’ twelve balustrades.
The earth’s rivers and mountains become a sea of silver,
while mid-heaven’s towers and altars are wrought of jade.
The ethereal spirit-realm’s flute music fades,
and the misty autumn light chills the silk’s reflection.
The immortal’s palm and lotus seem near at hand—
yet only from the Northern Dipper can I recognize Chang’an.

---

**Song of Sun-Viewing Peak**

Atop Mount Tai’s peak, a single slab of stone,
where the heavens appear, distant and deep in empty blue.
I come at night to sweep the clouds from the stone,
and before dawn, I see the sun’s tenfold radiance.

The sun rises a thousand miles east of the sea,
where mist and water blur indistinguishably.
The celestial rooster crows over the ocean,
while the eastern sky’s rosy qi half glows purple.
Suddenly, the glassy waves surge in dazzling brilliance,
as a single pool cradles the red jade disk.
Though I strain with a long rope, I cannot haul it up—
only after half a day does it reach Fusang’s summit.

Fusang’s branches and leaves shimmer in five colors,
while the sea’s waters flicker with a single white line.
East of the sun, clouds gather like linked mountains—
in my gaze, I seek the land of the merfolk.
When the sun stands high at noon, the sea’s waters dry,
and the entire sky glows with crimson qi.
Where now flow the golden towers of the Three Mountains?
The six turtles’ backbones chill with autumn frost.

I recall the year Qin’s emperor sealed the East,
when he longed to sail the seas in search of immortals.
He drove stones to build a bridge, yet could not cross,
while golden branches and kingfisher plumes returned in vain.
When shall I see the sun rise three thousand fathoms from the sea,
casting off my sandals and family like floating mist?
Before the Xiang Prince was born, there were true heroes—
tilting their hats, they shouted wildly and slept upon the stones.

I too wish to take giant stones and fill the Eastern Sea,
wielding my halberd to halt Xihe’s whip.
The Six Dragons do not pause—the sun flies like an arrow—
I look to the heavens, crying out, my ears burning with wine.

---

**Scripture-Exposing Stone**

At dawn, I descend Heaven’s Gate Pass,
at dusk, I rest upon Scripture-Exposing Stone.
Since what year has this stone stood,
leaning against the ten-thousand-fathom cliff?
Tiered ridges scatter flying streams,
a bolt of silk stretching over ten feet.
Beneath the water, jade scripts divide,
clear as if woven into black patterns.
Its script is of highest antiquity—
reading it, I am lost, unable to decipher.
Who has fathomed Xuedou’s Chan,
or drawn near the golden immortal through water’s guidance?
The green pool cradles precious trees,
where the Auspicious River’s flow is faintly seen.
Sitting motionless, I listen to the tide’s sound,
washing my ears until my heart grows still.

---

**Ascending Mount Tai in Summer with Colleagues**
*By Assistant Minister Zhan Yangbi of Anxi*

Hand in hand, we ride the fragrant winds on purple simurghs,
on the Venerable One’s Peak, we spread our cloud-borne wings.
The mist clears at Sun-Viewing Peak, a thousand mountains dawn,
while at Heaven’s Gate, the sixth month brings a chill.
The meditation terrace stands high and tranquil, unswept,
ancient inscriptions on the cliff eroded—who now reads them?

Alone, I cherish the traces left by the Master of Niches,
hand-picking fragrant tea to offer at the Apricot Altar.
After rain clears, we gather to drink beside the Immortal Palace.
Ascending the clouds, we push open eight jade-green windows,
where caps and carriages seem to descend from heaven.
Seated afar, mountain light shimmers like swords and halberds,
while rain-washed hues stir the pavilions.
We tune our flutes to the sound of stone cascades,
and pluck rosy clouds to steep in our wine cups.
How many times in life does one witness such grandeur?
Seated, we rise with the sea-borne sun, lingering in shared awe.

---

**Li Jie, Hanlin Academician, Ascends Mount Tai on the Ninth Day and Visits Puzhao Temple with Remembrance**
Fading sunlight gilds half the forest’s jagged peaks,
where Master Sun’s old lecture terrace still stands.
Sun Mingfu once taught here in life.
Bamboo and silk have crumbled, the academy lies in ruins,
while the resonant chants of the Buddhist hall ring clear.
Autumn dew spills wine into brimming cups,
and melodies carry spring’s voice to our seats.
The pure scene detains us—homeward paths grow late,
as azure clouds and crimson leaves embrace the mountain’s edge.

---

**Zhang Yuan, Zhuangyuan of Shanyin, Observes the Sun**
The Milky Way gleams bright in autumn’s high clarity,
from Sun-Viewing Peak, my distant gaze is sent forth.
Dawn’s light has yet to part the azure cliffs,
when sea-borne clouds first stir with crimson glow.
Soon, a bright mirror rises beyond the Three Isles,
and I long to spread its radiance across the Nine Provinces.
In past ascents, I gazed with lingering regret—
this wondrous sight does not betray my journey here.

---

**Reascending Mount Tai**
Three years, twice I’ve wandered the Eastern Peak,
and this return reveals scenes yet more marvelous.
Autumn’s pure sequence dissolves miasmic mists,
as from the summit’s height, I point to Hua and Yi.
The sun ascends Fusang as the cock crows,
while crimson towers stand empty in the high wind.
Looking up and down, I laugh at the boundless vastness—
only now do I grasp the time before all divisions.

---

**Zhang Yigui, Hanlin Academician and Imperial Tutor of Xiangfu, Ascends Mount Tai**
Of the Five Peaks, I now climb the foremost realm,
first purifying my heart to honor Jianwu.
Books since Han times tell of Sima’s legacy,
while pines from Qin endure as venerable ministers.
Layered cliffs soar, sundering sun and moon,
a wisp of cloud, a footstep away, veils Penglai.
Do not marvel at my halted carriage—
ask if any weeping wives of Shanyin remain.

---

**The Mighty Mount Tai**
I’ve long heard of its majesty as the foremost of peaks,
rising ten thousand fathoms to dwarf all others.
Floating dust parts three thousand worlds,
while elders still speak of seventy sovereigns.
The earth’s axis stretches east in ceaseless succession,
and from Heaven’s Gate, southern clouds dissolve into nothing.
Qin’s pines and Han’s relics lie near at hand,
as dusk’s haze repeatedly shrouds the verdant peaks.

---

**Endless Wandering**
Jade cliffs and cinnabar crags never weary my gaze,
where scorching summer yields to autumn’s cool.
I grasp chestnuts and sing the Three Joys,
facing wine, I need not compose the Four Sorrows.
Gentle clouds dampen my sleeves,
while the dazzling sun drenches sea and sky.
Our sovereign has long set aside the eastern feng rites—
even young Sima Xiangru now wears a white head.

---

**Misty Haze**
Ethereal mist and rosy clouds fill the path,
as clear bells and chimes drift through jade space.
The Eastern Emperor governs the realm of spring,
while the Jade Maiden dwells in the Crimson-Tasseled Palace.
Moss obscures broken steles, leaving only crow’s traces,
as I lean into primal qi to shatter primordial chaos.
With ample leisure, I share Master Zhuang’s delight—
why trouble to ride the void and harness the wind?

---

**Jia Sanjin, Censor-in-Chief of Fengyang, Ascends the Peak in Winter**
My gaze wanders the heights of bitter cold,
where myriad mountains encircle the sacred peak.
The feng rites are lost in Han’s overgrown grasses,
while Qin’s pines bear witness to the ages.
Ten thousand valleys merge in mist and haze,
as layers of purple and emerald cloak the heavens.
By palanquin, beneath the bright moon, we descend—
already, the upper realms echo with bells.

---

**Hu Rugui, Assistant Minister of Jinxiang, "Song of the Stone Tablet"**
Heaven’s Gate soars, wreathed in misty clouds,
where emerald ridges vie in dark intricacy.
A thousand cliffs, ten thousand ravines dazzle the eye—
a day spent gazing, yet the mountains remain unexhausted.
At midnight, I reach to touch the stars,
singing loudly at Sun-Viewing Peak to greet the dawn.
At the summit stands a solitary stone pillar,
pristine and pure, piercing the heavens.
Its edges sheathed, its blade concealed—seemingly artless,
unshaken by wind or thunder, it stands firm.
Fools prattle of a Qin-era stele,
but closer inspection reveals only emptiness, a hollow treasure.
Here, my heart holds not a single word—
all carved inscriptions appear as hasty scrawls.
The perfected one has never worn the guise of folly—
how could ornate phrases ever sweep this place clean?
Countless souls have ascended through the ages,
yet only Confucius deemed the world beneath him small.
The Great One left this to reveal the mystery—
a staff to uphold heaven and earth, forever unaging.

---

**Dreaming of Snow on the Journey**
White snow graces my dark limbs,
a sacred grace requiring no divination.
Heaven bestows its jade nectar,
washing my dust-laden self.
The path glistens with jade-like steps,
while the sacred peak gleams with crystal terraces.
Suddenly, spring’s thunder transforms all—
sweet rains nourish the verdant moss.

---

**Delight in Snow Upon Ascending the Mountain**
The sacred mountain’s auspicious snow swirls in coils,
escorting me through jade grottoes and celestial realms.
A jade palace radiates, suffused with purple mist,
while a tower of quartz stretches toward the Great Purity.
Vainly do tales speak of the Ten Isles of Penglai—
I envy not the immortals of Kunlun’s distant peaks.
Embracing the void, I partake in creation’s work,
as spring’s warmth blesses Qi and Lu with bountiful years.

---

**The Minister Pine**
From a sheer cliff’s summit, its lone trace appears,
a straight trunk piercing the clouds, its emerald shade layered thick.
For a thousand ages, its pure winds have graced Mount Tai—
yet alone, it once received Qin’s imperial seal.

---

**Casual Inscription at a Mountain Lodge**
Stone steps ascend steeply, half-touching the heavens,
as the majestic temple bows to the Azure Radiance Immortal.
A white rainbow hangs like rain in a clear sky,
while purple qi envelops the peaks at dawn.
I lean on my staff beneath Kunlun’s sun and moon,
gazing down upon the Eastern Sea’s Dipper and Ox.
At the summit’s pure heights, I wander at leisure—
at midnight, the primal chaos bows to the Lord of Creation.

---

**Lu Shude, Censor-in-Chief of Songjiang, "Occasional Composition on Mount Tai"**
With a sigh, I look down upon the lesser peaks,
approaching as if through mist and haze.
Clouds and rosy mists rise and spread,
while the celestial river nears my climbing grasp.
The Eastern Sea’s cup is fit for toasting,
as the Yellow River winds like a sash.
I ascend ever higher, yet refrain from composing—
in vain, I glimpse but a leopard’s flecked hide.

---

**Jia Menglong, Court Gentleman for Ceremonials of Fengyang, "Observing Sunrise at Sun-Viewing Peak"**
Standing at Sun-Viewing Peak’s summit,
radiant clouds scatter brocade hues.
A thousand mountains lie in ice and snow,
while ten thousand lands float in water and mist.
The sea’s reflection inverts the crows’ flight,
as the dawn’s pearl ascends the void.
The palanquin urges the traveler onward—
relying on the temple’s morning bells.

---

**Tu Xiying, Minister of Rites of Wanling, "Ascending Mount Tai"**
For hundreds of years, Zou and Lu have passed down their legacy,
while Mount Tai and the Eastern Sea endure unchanged.

**Yu Menglin, First Runner-Up in the Imperial Examination, of Qimen, "Ascending Mount Tai"**
Who among those who ascend is a true man?
A single lineage now debates who came before and who after.
Fifty-odd years—a dream of dust—
for whom did I chase, for whom did I return?
Awakened, I gaze at Mount Hua and the vast sea,
alone embracing the discourse of cinnabar amidst the cosmos.

---

**Xu Zhenming, Junior Guardian of the Imperial Seal, of Jiangxi, "Ascending Mount Tai"**
Weary of worldly bonds in recent years,
I cast myself free, my spirit wholly at ease.
Venerable elders dwell in empty valleys,
while immortals riding deer pluck purple lingzhi.
I seek faint traces, knowing they date to Han times—
not a single character remains from Qin steles.
At midnight, bathing in the sun’s splendor,
ten thousand miles of clouds all seem wondrous.

---

**Qin Song**
Through kalpas, its roots half withered,
yet how does this green pine still bring joy?
Sparse branches slant, stretching far across a thousand crags,
its verdant hue towering, solitary above ten thousand ravines.
It stands boldly by the Gate of Heaven,
and once bowed before the imperial tent as vanguard.
Unchanged through the cold, its steadfast heart endures—
the world’s fleeting fame calls it "Great Minister."

---

**Sheng Tang, Imperial Censor, of Jiacai, "Composed on the Return from Mount Tai, Encountering Snow"**
Lofty and towering, I gaze up at the Sacred Peak,
where imperial banners float, leaving no trace of dust.
Before my eyes, heaven and earth seem narrow—
beyond the seas, I watch the sun and moon traverse.
Clouds seal the waterfall like a dragon’s spittle,
snow blankets the imperial tent, turning the horses back.
My sightseeing now complete, my ascent fulfilled,
I pray the mountain spirit eternally guards its might.

---

**Li Dai, Governor and Censor-in-Chief of Shandong, of Mi’an, "Upon First Arrival During Drought, Personally Ascending Mount Tai to Pray for Rain"**
Anxious for the people, my heart hangs heavy—
I knock at the mountain’s spirit, ascending its lofty summit.
Wind carries thunder, shaking the halls,
clouds brew rain, filling the mountains and streams.
Myriad ravines cascade like flying silk,
countless peaks shrouded in emerald mist.
If only sweet rains would blanket the Nine Provinces,
farmers everywhere would celebrate a bountiful year.

---

**"Ascending Sun-Viewing Peak"**
The sun soars high, ten thousand miles without dust,
yet each day borrows the vast sea’s twilight glow.
With cinnabar hearts, men constantly bathe—
a single crimson wheel pierces heaven and earth.

---

**"Inscribed on the Independent Great Minister Pine"**
Through the Zhou, how many times has this ancient tree endured?
From old, the imperial tent has admired the Five Pines.
Only this lone one by the roadside,
upright and resolute, evades Qin’s seals.

---

**"Viewing the Sunning Sutra Stones"**
Who cleaved the mountain cliff to make this sunning platform?
The characters stand clear, like a mirror unveiled.
The waterfall hangs as if with intent—
ever and again, it flies to wash away dust.
*(North of the stone lies the Water Curtain Cave.)*

---

**"Playing the Listening-to-the-Spring Pillow"**
Who named it the "Listening-to-the-Spring Pillow"?
I say it is truly a platform for expounding the Dao.
*(For before it lies the Stone Sutra.)*
The ancient monk’s bones have long since crumbled—
only traces remain, left to conjecture.

---

**"Viewing Wan Gong’s Inscription on the Cliff"**
The cliff rises like a stone screen, bright in the sun,
a small pavilion perched high, the noon breeze cool.
The zither player is gone—who knows when?
Yet the strains of "High Mountains and Flowing Waters" linger.

---

**Feng Shan, Imperial Censor, of Runing, "Ascending Mount Tai"**
At dawn, I burn incense by Mount Tai’s radiant edge,
in high summer, the ascent glows with auspicious hues.
Frigid waves from ten thousand miles away surge from the vast sea,
a thousand crags’ pure tones cascade from flying springs.
My robes brush white stones as azure clouds entwine,
my sword hangs from green pines, linked by colored mists.
Who says Penglai is unreachable?
Here, my perch feels as if it brushes the heavens.

---

**Mount Tai’s grandeur soars like a soaring bird—**
from its summit, the sky clears at dusk.
Gazing north, the palace clouds billow,
while the Central Plains stretch endlessly into the distance.
The golden altar gleams, dawn breaking over a thousand cliffs,
the stone chamber’s winds chill even in the fifth month.
Clinging to cliffs, suspended in emptiness—no end in sight—
at the peak, the setting sun hangs inverted.

---

**Wu Ding, Imperial Censor, of Yexia, "Observing the Customs and Sacrificing at Mount Tai"**
The autumn wind rustles,
on the sacred terrace, footsteps echo.
Men and mountains blur in dark patches,
sky and water merge in distant brightness.
A crimson sun cradles the window,
white clouds rise before my eyes.
The stone inscriptions are endless—
through the ages, they hold a single sentiment.

---

**Huang Shiyan, Imperial Censor, of Min, "Visiting Yellow Flower Cave"**
The path winds deep into yellow blossoms and creeping fig,
staff in hand, I seek the pass where others tread.
After rain, a thousand ravines deepen their emerald hue,
ten thousand pines’ winds carry the sound of strings.
Mist swirls around scarlet banners, the day hushed,
clouds shield the dark lotus, even in clear skies.
The frost is too thin to bear a silver brush—
the crows’ caws seem to urge my verses.

---

**Tan Yao, Imperial Censor, of Lingnan, "At the Jade Emperor’s Summit"**
Without borrowing the wind’s wings,
how did I enter the azure void?
In furs in the sixth month, I feel the cold,
leaning on my sword, my mouth agape at the rainbow.
The jade palace seems ever nearer,
the golden mud’s craftsmanship in vain.
If Hu Mountain can be visited,
I would ride the wind there at once.

---

**"Sun-Viewing Peak"**
All say the peak is wondrously unique—
the sun’s crow seen at midnight.
It wheels like jade trees in flight,
bathing in a golden platter’s ripples.
Its roar resembles Qin’s moving stones,
its light sways Han’s altar of meditation.
My sunflower heart is not yet sated—
the earth awaits the unveiling of the dusty realm.

---

**"The Venerable Man Peak"**
It stands behind the central peak,
its layered ridges yielding to its sole supremacy.
Caressing it, I forget the years,
reclining, I embrace heaven and earth.
Crane-feather robes brush the clouds,
creeping vines’ skirts trail the moon.
All vajras have faded away—
only this elder remains to this day.

---

**The Two Vice Censors Wang and Li Invited Me to Drink at the Palace of Transmitting the Mandate.**

**At the Palace of Transmitting the Mandate, Ascending the Void with Sandals, Uncorking Wine to the Evening Breeze**
Where sandals tread the airy height, we raise our cups to the dusk wind.
The Gate of Heaven brings the flying crow near,
the azure sea refines the art of wine.
Beyond the curtain, misty rain lingers;
within the clouds, a thousand forms unfold.
Each roams the realm of immortals, heart at ease—
spare not the staff, ascend again.

---

**Zhang Hun, Historiographer of Shu, Ascends Mount Tai**
The peaks of Mount Tai bear the weight of tortoises’ crowns,
yet now we scale their sheer and trembling heights.
Their roots stretch far to Yan and Ji, lost in clouded depths,
their shadows pierce the void like jade pillars tall.
Below, all things are dwarfed—even Confucius’ gaze;
eastward, the sun’s rise honors Yu’s ancient praise.
To witness such grandeur is no vain worldly quest—
reach the summit, and the spirit soars at once.

---

**Sun-Viewing Peak**
The loftiest of Dai’s peaks reveals the eastern sea,
where drops of night’s last leak yield to the dawn.
The crow’s shadow drifts with the clouds’ sway,
the water’s gleam now levels with the sun’s.
Five-hued dawn blooms as the azure brightens,
waves surge a thousand fathoms, startling hidden beasts.
If Kuafu should return to ask the way,
tell him: to ride the whale is now within reach.

---

**Han Shilong, Vice Minister, a Man of Wu, Ascends Mount Tai**
Mount Tai soars high, its summit brushing the azure vault,
a thousand winding paths traversed, all wonders claimed.
The Celestial Pillar stands above the layered clouds,
the sea surrenders its dawn glow, and all things float.
From Qin to Yue, the gaze now spans the cosmos;
the Cloud Pavilion’s feng rites echo ancient springs.
From Wu’s gates, the golden stalks gleam bright—
suddenly, one wheels and soars, resting by this jade height.

---

**Gao Yingfang, Censor, a Man of Jiangxi, Ascends Mount Tai**
Towering, Mount Tai leans against the vault of heaven,
today’s ascent confines the eight wilds.
The cloud-canopied pavilion hovers o’er the mortal realm,
the dawn’s light flashes, striking the eastern sea.
Receiving Qian’s virtue, it endures through ages;
emerging from Zhen, its sacred power nurtures all lands.
The nine seals of Qi—who can discern their trace?
This peak, standing mid-plain, is mightiest of all.

When did Confucius ascend and gaze?
The sheer cliffs still bear his lingering threads.
With eyes unbound, the world shrinks small;
in stillness, the mind nears the primal dawn.
The Two Modes—clear and turbid—fix heaven and earth,
the Three Luminaries hang sun and moon on high.
What scene can rival this grandeur?
Auspicious clouds layer the mountain’s crown.

---

**Gou Ying, Censor, a Man of Sichuan, Ascends Mount Tai**
On the traveler’s road, I meet this famed peak,
ascending at the year’s first step.
By day, the world is clear and small;
by night, the Dipper and Ox grow cold.
Moss guards the steles’ inscribed words,
clouds shroud the altar of feng rites.
Pity this wondrous, peerless place—
how many times may one behold it?

---

**Sun Menglu, Censor, a Man of Changyi, Ascends Mount Tai**
For years I longed for Tai and Dai—
today, at last, I pause my steps.
Ancient trees soar high, piercing the Han,
strange peaks thrust straight into the void.
I wander, seeking Confucius’ traces,
pointing out Qin’s imperial seals.
Standing alone on the sheer summit,
heaven and earth lie within one glance.

---

**Deng Dong, Vice Commissioner, Ascends Mount Tai**
The eastern peak’s sheer cliffs pierce the sky;
at first ascent, one feels the clouds’ embrace.
Lotus-like, its sharp ridges rise like towers,
jewel-bright, its vastness veiled in mist.
Seven steps recall the Yellow Emperor’s chariot,
five pines still whisper of Qin’s reign.
Why climb straight to the Gate of Heaven?
Here, even worldly cares dissolve to nothing.

---

**Zou Shan, Academician, a Man of Anfu, Ascends Mount Tai**
From afar, Mount Tai looms,
its heights not lightly gained.
Towering into the clouds,
how can the clouded path be fathomed?
Through summer’s heat, I press on to ascend,
shaking my robes at dusk’s repast.
Should I not heed the rugged climb?
This longing has burned deep and long.
The stone path winds through emerald haze,
now open, now blocked, in twists and turns.
How old is this pine?
Its verdant hue bears the ancient world’s mark.
In a moment, I step through the Gate of Heaven,
lingering by the Sun-Viewing Peak’s side.
Is this not all of Qing and Xu?
In leisure, the nine realms shrink small.
The waves of the Pu and Lan merge with the clouds,
gazing down, it seems I lean upon a chariot’s rail.
I urge the scholars of Lu:
the climb of ten thousand feet lies in your own strength.

---

**An Autumn Day’s Ascent of Mount Tai**
Uneven stone steps coil like smoke,
phoenix pipes and cranes beckon from the clouds.
Flying waterfalls soak my robes, mistaking rain,
jagged peaks thrust green, nearly piercing the sky.
The Han altar, Qin’s trees—now brambles and thorns,
the imperial tents and bright halls—long silent and still.
To ride the qi and mount the wind awaits another day;
this pure journey surpasses even carefree wandering.

---

**Sun-Viewing Peak Again**
Shaking my robes on the sheer summit, chasing autumn’s clarity,
I wait on Sun-Viewing Peak for the dawn’s first glow.
Before the light divides, a thousand peaks merge,
suddenly, the sun stirs, and all lands grow bright.
To the east, the Qin stele stands tall;
to the south, the Han plains stretch level.
I ask the cliff’s edge, where the transformations begin—
how many can shrink Penglai to this small?

---

**Gu Dadian, Vice Commissioner, a Man of Wujiang, Ascends Mount Tai**
Facing the sacred peak, I look down on famed lands,
a thousand valleys, ten thousand cliffs, where the crows’ path winds.
Yu’s realm of rivers and mountains lies within a glance,
the Gate of Heaven’s halls touch the void.
The books record two Han-era Sima,
the trees stand as Qin’s five great pines.
Breathing here, I nearly commune with the imperial throne,
as a crane’s chariot, light and lone, enters the clouds.

High and winding, it seems to pierce the sky,
treading the steps, grasping the vines, my spirit unspent.
Emerald mists cling to the imperial plain, never scattering,
cold lingers on the immortal’s palm, where snow just melts.
Who can discern the nine seals of Qi?
This peak, standing mid-plain, is mightiest of all.
In the fourth month, the ascent still bears frost’s trace,
its chill clings close to the lord’s ear.

Layered peaks cluster like dark hibiscus,
my clogs strike the first peak of Pengxuan.
The dawn’s light slowly reveals the eastern sea’s sun,
sacred texts ever guard the white clouds’ seal.
The Jade Lad and Jade Maiden remain unseen,
but jade grasses and magic flowers may yet be found.
When will Xiangping’s marriages be done?
I ask the rosy clouds to trace old wanderings.
Gazing high, where does the heart break?
A bolt of silk—Wu’s gates—is my homeland.
In an instant, mists and haze shift endlessly,
my floating, sinking life rests in the faint and vast.
I turn, imagining a melody heard in the azure,
then bow on the terrace to the Jade Emperor.
If only clouds could rise in measureless layers,
bringing timely rain to the parched fields.

---

**Wang Feng, Vice Commissioner, a Man of Jiahe, Following Inspector Gu’s Rhyme**
Emerald cliffs tower, anchoring this vast domain,
to seek its fame, the path winds far.

The Dao unfolds, then circles back to close,
streams spill pearl-blossoms—now seen, now gone.
On stone I shake my robes with feathered guests,
in woods I watch chess played by woodcutters.
I wonder if Prince Jin was my past self,
recalling how he played his flute in lone moonlight.

Towering cliffs pierce the clear sky,
all day I climb, yet paths stretch endlessly.
Clouds part from purple skies, the mountain glows,
tides rise in sapphire seas, sunlight melts.
Looking up, I feel the roots of heaven near,
looking down, I startle at the earth’s vast might.
Ancient pines still span the Way—
why not let travelers strike their homeward chimes?

The sky lifts emerald peaks like lotus blooms,
a sacred stair guards the great summit.
At midnight, radiance bathes the peak,
midway, the setting sun seals white clouds.
Daring to embrace the six directions, heaven feels close,
in misty realms, immortals seem about to meet.
All around, mountains and rivers serve as sashes and whetstones—
I ride a dark crane, treading the traces of transcendents.

At dawn, winding paths twist like sheep’s guts,
straight up to Heaven’s Gate, gazing toward the Emperor’s realm.
A hundred warblers and flowers deepen their hues,
five-colored clouds and misty trees blur faintly.
Looking up, only the moon atop the peak,
mourning ancient emperors of bygone ages.
My gaze takes in endless scars of suffering—
I long to send down dharma-rain to parched lands.

**Accompanying Censor Tan on the Summit, Following the Previous Rhyme**
This famed mountain, blessed by cosmic order, anchors the realm,
its thousand-zhang cliffs draped in purple and green.
From distant isles, weary gulls still linger,
by clear springs, the clamor of the world fades.
I idly recall the flute-playing Qin consort,
vainly sigh for the grand ode of the minister.
What fortune to ascend again, dispelling summer’s heat—
deep in pines, cranes cry beneath the lone moon.

Mount Tai stands half in the sky,
its heights offer boundless vistas.
Heaven’s Gate, ten thousand *ren* high, glows with mist,
Sunrise Peak, at midnight, melts into dawn.
Beneath flowers, birds sing by jade-green streams,
beneath pines, dragons rest by split peaks.
Layered ridges stretch endlessly—
I grow weary of asking guides the way ahead.

Climbing stone steps, I move with ease,
not counting the twelve peaks of Wu Mountain.
Misty valleys blur the Han era,
five pines scatter, revealing Qin’s seal.
Turning, the world seems small,
craning my neck, I meet the Heavenly Consort at last.
In ancient grottoes, spring lies silent,
deep in white clouds, only immortals’ traces remain.

In the chilling sixth month, my heart feels clear,
mountains and rivers encircle the imperial homeland.
Clouds gather, the azure sky shines boundless,
waves settle, the dark sea glows faintly.
Why seek the three isles of immortals?
My floating life drifts toward the Highest Emperor.
Delighting in this royal escort, my heart is full—
sweet rains rise, reviving distant lands.

**Xu Zhongxing, Provincial Governor of Wuxing, Ascends Mount Tai**
Vast Heaven’s Gate opens to sun and moon,
carved cinnabar cliffs embrace towering peaks.
The Yellow River’s host, Mount Tai, turns west,
mountains bow to the divine capital from the north.
Dull spring mists veil Jieshi,
subtle auspicious vapors touch Penglai.
I hear the Jade Maiden’s three cups remain—
I wish to raise them for the emperor’s ten thousand years.

The Eastern Peak stands unmatched,
its central summit wreathed in sacred mist.
Heaven’s Gate, snow melted, rivers converge,
Sunrise Peak, in spring’s clarity, parts the sea’s hues.
Winds stir Qin’s pines like rain,
qi steams Han’s cypresses, forming clouds.
The traces of a thousand years of hegemons fade—
yet they still speak of Sima Xiangru’s *Fengshan* text.

**Xu Tianzeng, Minister of Revenue, of Guhuai, Inscribes the Blank Stele**
A giant stone climbs eighteen turns,
palace roads and Daoist paths fill a thousand hills.
Had not the *feng* and *shan* rites exhausted the people’s strength,
why would the Han founder have entered the pass?

**Shao Xian, Academician, of Yixing, Visits Puzhao Temple**
The monastery nestles against towering peaks,
its halls encircle the Prajñā Terrace.
Slanted stones, short steps, mountain paths curve,
a stone bridge, flowing water, the temple gate opens.
The stupa’s enlightenment proves illusory,
Confucian and Daoist origins have their own sources.
A thousand years of pure winds honor Sun and Shi—
only the hall’s foundation remains, facing the cliffs.

**Yang Cai, Censor-in-Chief, of Shuntian, Ascends Mount Tai’s Summit**
I shake my robes, alone atop Mount Tai,
my ancient heart opens in one sweeping glance.
By the Jade Maiden’s Pool, clouds never break,
below White Crane Grotto, rain just ceases.
Western dispatches bring urgent border alarms,
eastern grain transport strains the people’s strength.
Do not speak of the *fengshan* rites of old—
they have misled the common folk to this day.

**Wang Daohang, Censor-in-Chief, of Taiyuan, Ascends Mount Tai**
I wander atop the sacred peak,
in autumn’s desolation, a thousand miles stretch before me.
The jade halls of the *shengshan* rites first among all hopes,
beneath my gaze, the finest details of the nine provinces.
Auspicious signs gather in this divine realm, home of gods and ghosts,
dawn’s light shimmers where sea and sky float.
Since Confucius ascended and gazed,
who has continued such sublime journeys with mountains and rivers?

**Jin Jie, Gentleman of the Interior, of Nanhai, at Sunrise Peak**
From the eastern sea, Fusang brings the sun,
I climb Mount Tai’s terrace in one bound.
The golden wheel’s light strikes Heaven’s Gate at dawn,
the Jade Maiden soars above the azure grotto.
Clouds veil lotus peaks, obscuring Han’s trees,
inscriptions linger in stone chambers, overgrown with Qin’s moss.
We hold the sunflower’s devotion—
from afar, atop the peak, we gaze longingly.

**Gazing at the *Wangzai* Stele**
The stele was carved to honor Mount Tai,
yet who, through a thousand years, recites the emperor’s merit?
Hearing of Epang Palace’s completion, the people were drained,
the *Fengshan* texts written, the loom’s threads empty.
I see only this stele hanging in the jade grotto—
where can one find the dark Penglai in the blue sea?
Is this ascent merely idle wandering and verse?
In the midst of ancient and modern rise and fall, I sigh deeply.

**Ascending Mount Tai**
How does this lotus rise halfway to heaven?
For a thousand years, its steepness honors Mount Tai.
Mountain veils drape the azure grotto’s depths,
I shake my robes on the ridge, sealed by white clouds.
The Qin stele lies scattered, its threads lost,
the Han altar stands high, proud in its own might.
I follow Confucius’s reverent example,
striving to scale the heights of Mount Zhu Rong.

**Immortal’s Bridge**
A rainbow thread spans the mortal dust,
once the path of transcendents ascending on emptiness.
At Prince Jin’s Peak, clouds nearly vanish,
weary travelers’ carriages turn back at day’s end.
In Azure Radiance Grotto, I hear cranes and flutes,
before the Jade Register Stele, I ask of Penglai.
I long to cross and seek the true secret—
yet worldly ties still hurry me along.

**Zhu Pengqiu, Registrar, of Yu, Ascends Mount Tai with Feeling**

**Auspicious Journey in the Season of Vermilion Brightness**

A journey most splendid in the season of Vermilion Brightness,
on the ridge still drifts wondrous white snow.
I long to enter Guanghan and gaze upon the world,
as if floating on the Silver River, looking down upon Feng Yi.
The Jade Hall awaits the guests of the Three Primes,
the Jasper Isles must house the dwellings of the Five Peaks.
I wish to harmonize and regulate the turning cosmos—
when waters and mountains bark as one, the time may yet come.

**Chen Qing, Minister of Rites of Jishui, Ascends Mount Tai**

Long have I looked up to lofty mountains,
today I wander Mount Tai.
Stars divide the borders of Qi and Lu,
the earth anchors the flowing dark seas.
In the third month, the immortal blossoms dawn,
in the nine heavens, the jade tones linger.
Gazing afar at the place of ascent,
I stand straight at the summit of Tai’s peak.

**Liu Xiao, Vice Minister, of Zuoren Ascends Mount Tai**

In the tenth month, high winds polish the colors,
Wang Qiao invites me to tread the celestial vault.
Clouds part at the Dragon’s Maw, clarifying the Three Realms,
stars array at the bridgehead, gazing upon the Nine Plains.
Moss-covered stones hold empty caskets of transcendent script,
cliff pines still bear the grace of imperial favor.
If one aspires to soar beyond the celestial walls,
since ancient times, the Yellow Emperor has had the ultimate discourse.

**The Minister’s Pine**

An ancient trunk coils by the stone steps,
once graced by the Phoenix Tower’s court.
Through frost, it thrives for a thousand years,
through dew, it stands proud for a hundred reigns.
Towering, its wood could serve as pillars,
its spreading branches cast a colder shade.
Beside it, the purple-robed officials
stand in ranks, each vying in fragrance.

**The Towering Pavilion**

A thousand fathoms of jagged cliffs rise,
one sits and fears even birds and sparrows may falter.
Vast and hazy, it spans the ancient path,
ethereal, it meets the soaring towers.
At moonlit dusk, wind and dust settle,
in autumn, apes cry amid grass and trees.
In this enlightened age, harsh governance has ceased—
in all actions, one looks up to Confucius’s hill.

**Qin Era**

At Liangfu, where the eastward procession passed,
a green simurgh adorned the resplendent banners.
The dew basin is overgrown with vines,
the cinnabar turtle lies buried in snail trails.
At dawn, riders chase the wind,
in autumn skies, the sea’s currents swirl.
In deep seclusion, I inquire of past and present—
the stone tablets half-sunk in sand.

**The Cliff-Carved Stele**

Carved a hundred feet high upon the cliff,
this stele records merit and virtue.
Its classical prose remains wholly ancient,
its moss-covered characters half-green.
It may yet outshine the sun and moon,
and need not fear thunder’s wrath.
A paean to a dynasty’s revival,
it endures, entrusted to the mighty spirit.

**Liu Yingshi, Envoy of Hongdong, Inscribes the Flying Cloud Pavilion**

Gazing at Mount Tai’s misty, towering heights,
at dawn, my bamboo sedan winds through creeping vines.
Who carved the Crimson Gate to link the azure heavens?
Inverted, one hears the Blue Stone pour the Silver River.
The path turns where horses shy, adding to the dread,
the sky opens where dragons soar, turning sighs to song.
Longing to pay homage at the Divine Empyrean,
I pause at the Flying Pavilion, briefly delayed.

**Inscription on Sunrise Peak**

At Sunrise Peak, I watch the dawn,
three points past the fifth watch, it bursts in crimson.
Unseen by those below, the sky at the window brightens,
on the ridge, it stretches far, merging with the sea’s breath.
Clouds and mist shift, light flickers and fades,
water’s glow ripples, color returns to emptiness.
In an instant, all things wear spring’s hues—
I stand alone, singing heartily to the distant wind.

**Inscription on Peace Summit**

At the summit’s heights, the scenery is unmatched,
clutching vines, I traverse ten thousand layers of clouds.
Looking up and down, the cosmos expands my heart,
in valleys and cliffs, yin and yang divide the atmosphere.
The vast sea sways like a single cup,
the nine points of Qi and Lu scatter like blossoms.
Even more, I cherish the lingering sun’s beauty over rivers and mountains,
ever supporting the sagely ruler in this clear age.

**Inscription on the Southern Heavenly Gate**

With incense held in reverence, I knock at the celestial gate,
an immortal breeze carries me up to Heaven’s Door.
Between the cliffs, stars seem about to fall,
from the earth’s depths, thunder occasionally roars.
My staff and sandals brush past the shadow of the Azure Bird,
my robes press into the verdant clouds.
Soon, I see the purple aura approach the palace gates—
before the golden hall, I bear the Supreme One.

**Inscription on the Imperial Tent Platform**

After a long journey, I arrive at the Imperial Tent Platform,
the spring wind awakens the Minister’s Pine.
What became of the Qin’s enfeoffment?
The Song’s imperial hunts were all in vain.
The ancient tree stands firm with a thousand years’ resolve,
the green mountains remain unchanged for ten thousand years.
By chance, I come to this blessed land seeking hidden wonders—
the jade records and golden books will not be found again.

**Inscription on the Wordless Stele**

Who... this stone tablet amid clouds and mist,
said to be the stele of the First Qin Emperor’s feng and shan rites.
It was meant to preserve the ancient trace through silence,
yet its lack of words now breeds doubt.
Catching heaven’s rain and dew, its moss stays damp,
near the celestial pivot, its shadow never shifts.
The seventy-two rulers have all faded away—
vainly do tales of hidden treasures bring sorrow.

**Inscription on Immortal’s Bridge**

Gray stones hang suspended over a ten-thousand-fathom abyss,
a hair’s breadth away, they draw the blue heavens near.
One dreads the Weak Waters, where no boat can cross,
yet it’s said Kunlun has plank paths connecting them.
I long to ascend lightly, like a bird in flight,
to soar high, paired with cranes in formation.
...must directly reach the golden and silver palaces,
secretly receiving the Yellow Emperor’s Grand Scribe’s scroll.

**Inscription on Jade Maiden Spring**

Where can one seek the Jade Nectar?
I beg a taste of the Eastern Grove’s stone marrow.
Drinking dew may purify worldly bones,
feasting on mist is enough to fill a poet’s heart.
On Joyful Immortal Rock, the ministerial clouds glow,
by Old Yang’s Garden, medicinal herbs grow long.
Since the numinous indeed gathers at a finger’s breadth,
I wish to become timely rain for the desolate lands.

**Inscription on Water Curtain Grotto #1**

Beneath the Heavenly Girdle Rock, the sacred source runs deep,
before the Gathering Beauty Pavilion, jade liquid flows long.
A white silk sash parts the Azure Emperor’s seat,
pearl curtains hang in the land of white clouds.
Clear tones play the solitary paulownia’s melody,
a chill lingers, though it is not the sixth month’s frost.
Gazing upon the scene, my pure inspiration stirs—
by the stream, I float several cups of purple mist.

**Inscription on the Queen Mother’s Pool**

Which Queen Mother of the West welcomes one to this summit?
The Yellow Emperor personally sent the Azure Radiance Immortal.
I scoop the stars’ waters from the lake,
pouring them to form a spring at Pengxuan Grotto’s mouth.
White cranes still nest by the bathing side,
flying simurghs dance before the jade rings.
In my life, I have had cloud-soaring aspirations—
I long to ride the currents and ascend to the nine heavens.

**Inscription on Old Gao’s Bridge**

At Old Gao’s Bridge, I pause my steps,
asking where the Azure Radiance hangs above White Cloud Hermitage.
In my life, how many pairs of clogs have I worn?
Only on perilous paths do I know the joy of the Third Heaven.
Sun dries the starry rainbow, I seek the Dao,
snow melts, misty trees dot the clear haze.
In the sacred grove, I happily meet a true monk nearby—
tea leaves and pine flowers accompany our laughter and talk.

**Inscription on the Eighteen Bends**

Step by step, I ascend three thousand fathoms,
winding and turning through the eighteen bends.
On the shady steps, snow congeals, making slips unavoidable,
at the stone gate, the wind howls, bringing a biting chill.
Lifting my feet and dragging my heels, I must watch my step,
clinging like wings, climbing like scales, one could hang one’s cap.

**Inscribed at the Cliffside Stele**

Mountain rocks steep as piled silk—how could they be ground away?
Yet in those days, what extreme efforts were made!
Golden mud now scatters with fallen moss,
jade seals lie broken, their fragments strewn.
Han steles and Qin inscriptions fade beneath the dew of grass,
Tang script and Jin calligraphy vanish in the river’s flow.
I come to climb and seek the traces left behind—
alone on the peak’s edge, I sing with deep emotion.

**Inscribed at the Cliff of Self-Abandonment**

Facing the abyss, one trembles—poetry offers a mirror;
knowing peril, one grasps danger—easy to inscribe a warning.
Why then cast oneself into a thousand-fathom precipice,
seeing one’s life as lighter than a single hair?
If body perishes and kin suffer, what is gained?
If bones shatter and the soul finds peace, who will bear witness?
Let this be passed to foolish sons—let them ponder:
to abandon life is still to betray the name of benevolence.

**Inscribed at the Venerable One’s Peak**

Again I stand on stone, gazing toward the immortal’s realm,
pointing across Wu and Yue, Zhou and Qin in a glance.
The azure ox of old eludes pursuit,
the white crane that flew here fades beyond reach.
The Eastern Sovereign carved jade lotus gates,
the Jade Maiden dwells deep within tiger-leopard passes.
Though Penglai lies but a footstep away, the heavenly path is barred—
seeking immortals in vain, I return empty-handed.

**Inscribed at the Small Dragon’s Maw**

A thousand ravines and ten thousand cliffs converge at this single gate,
where a coiled dragon sprays foam in its soaring flight.
The hanging waterfall sways like earthbound silk,
storm-tossed waves crash like an overturned basin.
Jade grottoes, veiled in cloud, obscure the moon’s cavern;
immortal crags, shaken by thunder, rock the roots of heaven.
Sitting here, I suddenly feel my soul take flight—
as dusk falls, my return is left unspoken.

**Inscribed at Mount Aolai**

Alone it towers in the southwest, this Mount Aolai,
its celestial gate and cavern halls standing amidst wild grass.
Twisting bamboo groves embrace the emerald peaks,
a crescent moon hangs high above the azure ravine.
Within the stone-walled gorge, clouds disperse,
where immortal’s soil bears the prints of cranes in flight.
Ascending, my lifelong joy knows no end—
yet facing this scene, I shamefully lack the words to compose a rhapsody.

**Li Bochun, Prefect of Songjiang, Inscribed at the Pine of the Qin Minister**

The Chancellor, for no reason, longed for his yellow hound—
thus allowing the Four Hoary Ones to claim the pure wind.
The Master’s cloud-soaring intent spans a thousand ages—
would he ever have accepted a seal at the Qin court?

**Zhang Yanting, Prefect of Binzhou, Autumn Ascent of Mount Tai, Passing the Water Curtain Cave**

Crimson maples, touched by frost, paint the autumn sky,
a hundred leagues of climbing—my soul wanders far.
The spring hangs like a curtain, its twin streams murmuring,
clouds grind the emerald cliffs, half the mountain afloat.
In the void, one imagines immortal songs,
across flying gorges, the road still seems under repair.
The traces of transformation endure through a thousand ages—
my teacher’s guidance now leads me to seek the return.

**Staying Overnight at the Summit Chamber, Following the Rhyme**

Wind stirs the eaves like autumn’s refining of horses,
yet how could I tire of this journey to explore wonders?
Heart startled by the crimson gorges—all heavens distant,
turning back, white clouds drift ten thousand miles.
Leaning on perilous cliffs, the ancient stele’s text is lost,
nearby, the new moon’s crescent could be hewn anew.
All my life, I never understood the dream of embracing mountains—
now I knock at heaven’s gate, hoping for a single answer.

**Passing the Celestial Gate**

With flying steps, I tread the Celestial Gate’s path,
suddenly, feathered wings seem to sprout.
Cloud-teeth rise from low peaks,
haze and ink wash the distant ridges.
I revere the sacred traces of those who first ascended,
the pines preserve the name of one who stood alone.
With a broad view, one should not fail—
through ten thousand ages, a single sentiment remains.

**Ode to the Jade Maiden by Cheng Gongchen, Bureau Director of Putian**

Radiant in the white clouds’ edge,
the divine maiden rides a purple simurgh.
Her pure form mirrors the Jade Pool’s waters,
her rosy face gleams like the Fusang sun.
At dawn, she feasts on bright auroras; at dusk, she sips dew,
her lotus robes woven, her crown forged from lightning.
I have heard of the Yellow Emperor’s daughter,
who cultivated truth until feathered wings grew.
Her jade leaves were passed down through Han,
in a stone chamber, she refined golden elixirs.
Facing west, she paid homage to the Queen Mother at Yao Pond,
her jade pendants chiming like coral strands.
By daylight, she flew away with Cao the Immortal,
leaving only a cinnabar turtle to guard the green peaks.
In the ancient cave of yellow blossoms, traces of the Realized One remain—
her slender fingers pressed into mossy stone.
There is also a rain-flower bed,
which in the Year of the Ox she pointed to as a thin meditation mat.
Silver lamps hang beside the Dipper,
shining like the seven stars in their brilliance.
Incense smoke curls around the rock corridors,
wafting jade-green mist.
Heavenly flowers do not furl the water-pearl curtain,
sweet springs gush forth as white jade nectar.
Suddenly, the wind sighs through ten thousand ravines of pines—
I wonder if it is the sound of scriptures chanting.
Once I recited Li Bai’s lines,
"Floating, floating, descending the nine heavens."
I have heard that when the Song sovereign came east,
the Purple Observatory opened.
Jade chimes rang beyond the empty sky,
phoenix flutes gathered at Phoenix Terrace.
Resplendent clouds of blessing descended with the imperial carriage,
crimson phoenixes of five hues soared above.
Majestic Mount Tai, foundation of the eastern land—
how divine, how luminous, is the Primordial Lady!
This mountain’s spirit enhances its numinous wonder,
throughout the realm, for a thousand ages, it is revered as towering and grand.
I, too, have long yearned to emulate such heights—
today, on the eastern mountain, I tread with clog-teeth.
Eighteen perilous stone steps, jagged and uneven,
a ten-thousand-fathom cloud ladder seen from midair.
Riding the wind, I ascend the Celestial Gate,
brushing my robes, I tread the starry tracks.
Immortal music welcomes me from the clouds,
my body seems to dwell among the celestial rivers.
Atop the Golden Lotus Peak, purple qi surges—
I bow before the wind, offering fragrant iris.
Her pale hands present me a cinnabar cup,
in an instant, I partake of white stone marrow.
She escorts me further up Sunrise Peak,
where the red sun first sings as the sky-crow rises.
Gazing west, Kunlun’s snowflakes gleam bright,
the Jade Pool connects directly to the River of Heaven.
That night, I dream of a stone casket and the *Jade Void* scroll,
beside which a feather-robed figure points with care.
From then on, I seek the purple mushrooms beneath the rosy clouds,
while worldly fame scatters like wind-blown dust.

**Wang Tingqing, Bureau Director of Jingmen, Ascending Mount Tai**

For years, I dreamed of wandering Mount Tai—
today, joyously, I stand at its highest point.
Clouds vie with the sun, emerging beyond the auroras,
peaks soar, and I float in the azure void.
Immortal crags array like screens, endless green,
waterfalls from hanging cliffs seem about to flow in jade.
Gazing in all directions, how could the world not seem small?
Only the ancient mound of Ni Qiu remains verdant.

Resting at the towering summit, I cough—
a clear wind carries the cawing of crows.
Ten years of love for hills and ravines,
a single laugh scatters the dust of the vulgar world.
At the cave’s mouth, clouds linger for the night,
the stream flows in communion with the moon.
On a stone bed, sleep comes naturally—
in dreams, I awaken to autumn insects.

**Tao Yunyi, Traveling Official of Guiji, Atop Mount Tai**

Mount Tai’s peaks, lofty, uphold the Jade Emperor,
Qin steles and Han tablets stand in twin antiquity.

Amidst the void, parrots and hounds bridge the realm of truth,
Beneath the sea, fish and dragons escort the rising sun.
Cloud-qi descends, veiling a thousand peaks in deep green,
Rain-flowers scatter, perfuming the sky with fragrance.

To ascend here is to defy aging,
Yet even the Five Peaks and Three Isles pale in comparison.
A hundred turns through Heaven’s Gate, the stone path rugged,
First to reach the summit, the breath suddenly eases.

Sun and moon hang at the waist like twin sacred mirrors,
Stars and auroras spread across the palm like a tray of pearls.
With a glance east and west, Qin and Yue stand divided,
Yet in an instant, radiance bathes the imperial capital.

Why need golden mud to unseal jade tablets?
The immortals’ ascent on the wind is no empty tale.

**The Azure Radiance Primordial Sovereign**
Where do the hosts of spirits gather across the heavens?
On lofty Mount Tai, the realm of Supreme Purity begins.
I hear that life and death are but dreams and illusions,
Yet how strange that rewards and punishments are so clearly meted.

In the void, golden light enfolds her form,
At midnight, the crimson-tasseled staff’s call resounds.
Truly, gods and mortals alike love their land—
Each year, a million offerings aid in peace and prosperity.

Overtly, officials oversee; covertly, spirits govern,
Human and heavenly fortunes intertwine.
If she were to rule the cosmos for all time,
Why then was this power vested in a woman’s form?

Her cliffs rival Putuo’s Guanyin,
Her halls stand equal to Hengshan’s Lady of the Southern Peak.
Day after day, how many in caps and robes
Gaze upward to her lofty heights, embracing the dust below.

**Zhang Cheng, Bureau Director of the Ministry of Rites, from Anfu, On the Hall of Heavenly Kings**
When the Heavenly King sets forth on his tour,
A myriad states follow with jade and silk.
The rites of *chai* and *wang* follow Yu’s ancient rules,
His grace and might harmonize with the ways of the Great Yu.

The Qi lord could halt destruction,
Yet what did the Ji and Lü clans ever achieve?
A thousand years preserve these ruins,
While the vernal sun still obeys his command.

**Jiang Jing, Traveling Official of Guiji, Record of Splendors at the Azure Radiance Palace**
Who carved this Buddhist temple into the azure peaks?
Clouds drift in and out, veiling half the mountain in shade.
Hidden streams trickle through jade-like stone steps,
Heavenly flowers scatter through the forest of jeweled blossoms.

Here, worldly cares dissolve in verdant ease,
And the search for beauty becomes a quest beyond the mundane.
Most wondrous is the Terrace of the Swallows—so near,
Its rosy glow mirrors the golden radiance of the imperial city.

**Ode to the Waterfall Cave**
Seeking wonders till dusk, weary of words on returning,
I shift my seat by the joyous spring, nestled in emerald haze.
White water cascades from a thousand ravines,
Blue sky transforms into five dragons in flight.

High upon mossy cliffs, silken banners flutter,
Inverted gusts from the crags seem to weave the wind.
Why seek Penglai’s isles elsewhere?
The source of living water is my own mechanism.

**Wu Tongchun, Gentleman for Thorough Counsel, from Gushi, Passing Peach Blossom Ravine**
A thousand layers of peach trees fringe the water’s edge,
Sacred cliffs wind a hundred turns beside the sloping hills.
In autumn’s height, the jade orchard bears fruit like the sun,
After rain, the Gate of Heaven churns waves into blossoms.

Dongfang Shuo often begged favors from the Han lord,
But where might a fisherman seek the immortals’ abode?
I arrive too late for spring’s waning winds,
Yet staff in hand, I tread lightly through the rosy clouds.

**Winter Ascent of Mount Tai**
Eastern Star towers open as if carved by heaven,
Crimson-tasseled staves hang high from a white jade terrace.
Two immortal peaks loom beyond,
Clouds drift from the Jade Maiden’s gorge.

A solitary pillar cradles the sun three thousand *zhang* high,
A sky-bridging path winds eighteen times through the void.
The sacred mystery feels worlds apart from mortal life—
Where in Red City might one visit Penglai?

**Gazing Upon the Primordial Chaos from the Blue-Green Summit**
From Pengxuan’s loftiest peak, I survey the vast expanse,
Of the Five Peaks, none rival mighty Mount Tai.
Cranes soar over jade ridges toward the Azure Emperor’s temple,
Men knock at Heaven’s Gate, seeking the Purple Tenuity Palace.

Stars align as the Three Origins converge,
The sea embraces the cosmos, all horizons empty.
Why do parrots cry from the layered peaks?
On Fusang’s branches, the sun first reddens.

**The Eight Wastelands Gathered in a Distant Gaze**
From afar, the earth’s edges seem to float,
A sliver of land drifts between day and night.
Han-era golden seals gleam in autumn’s clarity,
Qin pines and imperial tents sigh in the rain’s sorrow.

Stars coil halfway around the cloud-crowned cliffs,
The sea’s waters hang level with the Sun-Viewing Terrace’s flow.
Pity not the immortal bones for their distant cinnabar favor—
I long to ride the wind straight to the Penglai isles.

**Inquiring of the Spirit’s Abode**
How fares the numinous realm of late?
Grasping vines, I test the sheer cliffs.
Who would believe the sea’s edge trails white silk?
Suddenly, beneath my staff, the Yellow River plummets.

Clouds drift from the jade well, fragrant breezes delicate,
Flowers chime on the jasper altar, heavy with dew’s essence.
Who will transmit the secret arts to the Azure Flower?
Since ancient times, heaven and earth have hummed a mournful song.

**Traveling Through the Valley of Hidden Classics**
Seeking seclusion, I follow the path’s opening,
My sedan chair facing all directions, drinking in the celestial winds.
Deep in the crags, *beiye* scriptures whiten with frost,
On sheer cliffs, *tanhua* blossoms blaze in the sun.

A hundred streams’ voices fly through treetops,
A thousand *xun* of emerald descend from the clouds.
I grasp the chestnut, ready to play the lofty mountain’s praise—
Yet where is Zhong Qi to stir my endless inspiration?

**Zhu Xiang, Gentleman for Thorough Counsel, from Jinhua, Ascending Mount Tai**
Climbing clouds, treading steps, I knock at heaven’s gate,
At the summit, I brush the stars as if they could be grasped.
Looking down, a thousand peaks stand in reverent ranks,
Gazing low, the eight directions shrink the cosmos.

Dragon veins and tiger mounds sealed in moss,
Han wu-tong and Qin pines endure through generations.
Who has been the master of these ascents through the ages?
Broken steles and desolate tablets stand alone at dusk.

**Zhang Tiquan, Gentleman for Thorough Counsel, from Zhen ding, Record of Travels at Mount Tai’s Summit**
Where earth and heaven divide, this mountain stands,
Its grandeur shames my poor brush’s attempt to capture it.
Jade tablets and golden mud evoke deep sighs,
Mist-light and layered vapors coil and entwine.

Climbing cliffs, I long to witness the crimson sun,
Treading steps, I watch as I enter the white clouds.
I came to seek immortals and explore sacred traces,
Who knew I’d meet a thousand-ren gathering here?

**Li Tian, Vice Commissioner, from Xiezhou, Ascending Mount Tai**
I gaze down upon the mortal realm, walking the void,
A single pavilion stands high at the sacred peak’s beginning.
From afar, I raise the Purple Tenuity toward Fusang’s domain,
Nearby, I embrace the cinnabar clouds lingering from Taiye’s pool.

Rain ceases, yet the divine precincts remain moist,
The sky lowers, ever beside the Year Star’s abode.
All ascent relies on the mountain spirit’s power,
My inspiration fills the cosmos, free to unfurl or gather.

**Mount Tai, ten thousand *zhang* tall, pierces the layered void,**
A winged steed, galloping the emptiness, seeks to ride the wind.
At Sunrise View, I vaguely glimpse the crimson-tasseled procession,
Cloud forests seem to connect with the jasper palaces.

Suddenly, the Supreme Emperor’s sweet rain descends,
Step by step, the Western Terrace welcomes the jade tread.
Past affairs of feng and shan rites hang empty in history,
Yet this new journey must stand among the greatest of all time.

**Peng Mengzu, Gentleman for Thorough Counsel, from Huainan, Ascending Mount Tai**
Star-banners and jeweled canopies lock the misty void,
A winding ladder ascends ten thousand turns through the ethereal.
The sky’s vastness turns silk-light into a white steed,
The peak’s height shapes layered vapors into a green dragon.

The Silver River threatens to burst from the immortal’s palm,
The cinnabar turtle still hides in the Jade Maiden’s palace.

No sage-era passes without seeking feng and shan rites,
Yet fine phrases and grand odes are but vain craft—
The misty palace halls bow to the boundless heavens,
While the Central Plains, a thousand miles away, fade into emptiness.

The sun rises from the eastern hills, then plunges into the Ji,
